Introduction\\n\\nThe Profile, Subscription \u0026 Personal Settings Experience defines how students manage their personal identity, subscription plan, preferences, and privacy controls.\\n\\nThis layer supports the long-term relationship between the student and AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThe purpose is to provide:\\n\\n- Control.\\n- Transparency.\\n- Personalisation.\\n- Trust.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Profile Experience Philosophy\\n\\nThe profile experience follows these principles.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Student Ownership\\n\\nThe student's:\\n\\n- Learning history.\\n- PLKG.\\n- Preferences.\\n- Progress.\\n\\nbelong to the student.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Simple Management\\n\\nSettings should be understandable and easy to control.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Personalisation\\n\\nStudents can configure how AI Study Buddy supports them.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Trust and Transparency\\n\\nStudents understand:\\n\\n- What data exists.\\n- How it is used.\\n- How they control it.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Personal Profile\\n\\nStudents manage basic information.\\n\\nIncludes:\\n\\n- Name.\\n- Profile image (optional).\\n- Preferred language.\\n- Communication preferences.\\n\\nThe profile represents the student identity within the learning environment.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. BLIE Personalisation Settings\\n\\nStudents control their AI companion experience.\\n\\nPossible settings:\\n\\n## Response Style\\n\\n- Concise.\\n- Balanced.\\n- Detailed.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning Support Level\\n\\n- Reactive assistance.\\n- Guided learning.\\n- Proactive recommendations.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Reminder Preferences\\n\\nStudents control learning notifications.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Subscription Experience\\n\\nAI Study Buddy follows a direct-to-student subscription model.\\n\\nThe platform is designed for individual students downloading the application from app stores.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Subscription Models\\n\\nInitial structure:\\n\\n## Individual Subscription\\n\\nPersonal AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nIncludes:\\n\\n- Personal BLIE access.\\n- Personal PLKG.\\n- Learning analytics.\\n- Document intelligence.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Group Subscription\\n\\nDesigned for students learning together.\\n\\nBenefits:\\n\\n- Lower cost per student.\\n- Shared study resources.\\n- Collaborative learning environment.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Privacy Controls\\n\\nStudents control their data.\\n\\nSettings include:\\n\\n- Data visibility.\\n- Sharing permissions.\\n- Study group sharing.\\n- AI memory preferences.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. BLIE Memory Control\\n\\nStudents can manage AI memory.\\n\\nPossible controls:\\n\\n- View remembered preferences.\\n- Remove saved information.\\n- Adjust memory behaviour.\\n\\nThe student remains in control.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Data Management\\n\\nStudents can manage their learning data.\\n\\nOptions:\\n\\n- Export learning history.\\n- Download personal knowledge data.\\n- Delete account data.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Security Experience\\n\\nSecurity features include:\\n\\n- Account protection.\\n- Authentication management.\\n- Session management.\\n\\nSecurity should remain simple for students.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Notification Settings\\n\\nStudents control:\\n\\n## Learning Notifications\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Preparation reminders.\\n- Revision suggestions.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Academic Notifications\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Upcoming assessments.\\n- Study milestones.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Community Notifications\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Study group activities.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Account Lifecycle\\n\\nStates:\\n\\n## New Account\\n\\nInitial setup.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Active Student\\n\\nRegular learning usage.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Subscription Expired\\n\\nLimited access state.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Account Archived\\n\\nHistorical learning data retained according to policy.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 18. Introduction\\n\\nThe Learning Analytics \u0026 Academic Growth Experience defines how AI Study Buddy measures, visualises, and communicates student learning progress.\\n\\nThe system transforms learning activity into meaningful insights that help students improve.\\n\\nAnalytics are generated from:\\n\\n- Learning activities.\\n- Subject progress.\\n- PLKG development.\\n- BLIE interactions.\\n- Revision activities.\\n- Assessment preparation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Analytics Philosophy\\n\\nThe analytics experience follows these principles.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Growth Over Comparison\\n\\nStudents should measure progress against their own learning journey.\\n\\nThe objective is personal improvement.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Understanding Over Numbers\\n\\nNumbers alone do not represent learning.\\n\\nAnalytics must explain meaning.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Actionable Insights\\n\\nEvery insight should suggest a possible next action.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Student Ownership\\n\\nLearning analytics belong to the student.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Learning Intelligence Model\\n\\nAnalytics are built around four dimensions.\\n\\n``` id=\\\"a91kxz\\\"\\nKnowledge\\n\\n+\\n\\nUnderstanding\\n\\n+\\n\\nLearning Behaviour\\n\\n+\\n\\nAcademic Progress\\n\\n=\\n\\nLearning Intelligence\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Knowledge Growth Analytics\\n\\nThe system measures PLKG development.\\n\\nIndicators:\\n\\n- New concepts acquired.\\n- Knowledge connections created.\\n- Topics understood.\\n- Knowledge gaps reduced.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n\\\"Your Computer Networks knowledge has expanded with 12 connected concepts this month.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Subject Progress Analytics\\n\\nEach subject provides learning insights.\\n\\nDisplays:\\n\\n- Topic progress.\\n- Understanding level.\\n- Revision needs.\\n- Preparation status.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nDatabase Systems\\n\\nTopics:\\n8 / 12 introduced\\n\\nStrong:\\nNormalization\\n\\nNeeds Review:\\nTransaction Management\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Mastery Development\\n\\nMastery represents confidence and understanding.\\n\\nPossible states:\\n\\n## Introduced\\n\\nStudent has encountered the concept.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning\\n\\nStudent is developing understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Practicing\\n\\nStudent applies knowledge.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Confident\\n\\nStudent demonstrates strong understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Needs Reinforcement\\n\\nConcept requires review.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Learning Habit Analytics\\n\\nThe system may analyse learning patterns.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Study consistency.\\n- Preparation habits.\\n- Revision frequency.\\n- Learning sessions.\\n\\nThe purpose is awareness, not judgement.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. BLIE Learning Insights\\n\\nBLIE can provide personalised observations.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n\\\"You usually understand concepts better after examples. I will adjust explanations.\\\"\\n\\n\\\"You have not reviewed this topic recently. A short revision may help.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Academic Journey Timeline\\n\\nStudents can view their long-term progress.\\n\\nTimeline:\\n\\n```\\nSemester 1\\n\\n↓\\n\\nFoundation Knowledge\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSemester 2\\n\\n↓\\n\\nConnected Concepts\\n\\n↓\\n\\nFinal Year\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAdvanced Understanding\\n```\\n\\nThe student sees growth over time.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Learning Gap Analytics\\n\\nThe system identifies areas requiring attention.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Missing prerequisite knowledge.\\n- Unclear concepts.\\n- Weak connections.\\n\\nThe goal is recovery, not failure indication.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Preparation Analytics\\n\\nThe system tracks readiness.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\nUpcoming topic:\\n\\n\\\"Operating Systems\\\"\\n\\nPreparation status:\\n\\n- Required concepts reviewed.\\n- Background knowledge completed.\\n- Ready for lecture.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Assessment Readiness\\n\\nBefore examinations, students can view:\\n\\n- Prepared topics.\\n- Weak areas.\\n- Recommended revision.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n\\\"Your strongest topics are A and B. Focus revision on C and D.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Personal Learning Report\\n\\nStudents may generate periodic reports.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\nWeekly:\\n\\n- Learning activities.\\n- Progress summary.\\n\\nSemester:\\n\\n- Knowledge growth.\\n- Subject development.\\n\\nAcademic journey:\\n\\n- Long-term learning history.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Analytics Visualisation Principles\\n\\nAnalytics should be:\\n\\n## Clear\\n\\nEasy to understand.\\n\\n## Motivating\\n\\nEncourage progress.\\n\\n## Calm\\n\\nAvoid creating anxiety.\\n\\n## Educational\\n\\nExplain meaning.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Privacy Model\\n\\nStudent analytics are private by default.\\n\\nStudents control:\\n\\n- Data access.\\n- Sharing.\\n- Visibility.\\n\\nAcademic growth data belongs to the student.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Offline Experience\\n\\nOffline analytics include:\\n\\nAvailable:\\n\\n- Cached progress.\\n- Previous reports.\\n- Local learning history.\\n\\nPending:\\n\\n- Cloud-generated insights.\\n- Updated analytics.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. Analytics States\\n\\n## Starting Journey\\n\\nLimited data available.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Developing\\n\\nLearning patterns emerging.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Growing\\n\\nKnowledge network expanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Advanced\\n\\nLong-term academic intelligence developed.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 18. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe Learning Analytics \u0026 Academic Growth Experience establishes the reflection system of AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThe system shall:\\n\\n1. Show personal learning growth.\\n2. Explain knowledge development.\\n3. Identify learning gaps.\\n4. Support better study decisions.\\n5. Encourage continuous improvement.\\n6. Preserve student ownership and privacy.\\n\\nAnalytics transform learning activities into personal academic intelligence.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume H11**\\n:::\\n\\nAlhamdulillah.\\n\\n**H11 is complete.**\\n\\nNext:\\n\\n# Volume H12 – Profile, Subscription \u0026 Personal Settings Experience\\n\\nThis will define the user management layer:\\n\\n- Student profile\\n- Subscription plans\\n- Individual vs group subscription\\n- Learning preferences\\n- AI preferences\\n- Privacy controls\\n- Data ownership\\n- Account management\\n\\nThis completes the main student-facing UX architecture before moving into future H13+ expansion documents.\",{},{\"_305\":608,\"_312\":639,\"_35\":640,\"_37\":641,\"_316\":642,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":643,\"_325\":326},\"79653c84-eb40-47c8-a883-cf8a4114bbf5\",[592],{\"_370\":474,\"_323\":651},1783672930.910939,1783672940.87653,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":649},{\"_350\":494,\"_52\":494,\"_442\":14,\"_334\":644,\"_339\":645,\"_519\":646,\"_521\":647,\"_523\":14,\"_524\":14,\"_525\":14,\"_526\":14,\"_527\":14,\"_528\":648,\"_343\":621,\"_469\":-5,\"_347\":622,\"_349\":622,\"_338\":488,\"_360\":497,\"_353\":14},[],[],[],[],{},[650],\"Begin H11. Introduction\\n\\nThe Study Groups \u0026 Knowledge Sharing Experience defines how students collaborate, share resources, and learn together within AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nUniversity students naturally learn through communities:\\n\\n- Classmates.\\n- Course groups.\\n- Study partners.\\n- Academic communities.\\n\\nAI Study Buddy provides a structured environment where collaboration can happen while preserving each student's personal learning identity.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Collaboration Philosophy\\n\\nThe experience follows these principles.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Personal First\\n\\nEvery student maintains their own:\\n\\n- Learning history.\\n- PLKG.\\n- Knowledge progress.\\n\\nShared resources do not replace personal understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Collaborative Growth\\n\\nStudents benefit from collective learning resources.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Quality Over Quantity\\n\\nThe goal is useful academic collaboration, not endless content sharing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Controlled Sharing\\n\\nStudents control what they contribute and access.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Study Group Model\\n\\nA Study Group represents a learning community.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Same subject students.\\n- Same programme students.\\n- Semester cohorts.\\n- Project groups.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Group Subscription Concept\\n\\nAI Study Buddy supports group-based subscription models.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nIndividual subscription:\\n\\nStudent subscribes independently.\\n\\n---\\n\\nGroup subscription:\\n\\nStudents from the same course form a learning group.\\n\\nBenefits:\\n\\n- Discounted subscription.\\n- Shared resources.\\n- Collaborative learning.\\n- Group knowledge environment.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Group Creation Experience\\n\\nA student may:\\n\\n- Create a study group.\\n- Invite classmates.\\n- Join an existing group.\\n\\nGroup information:\\n\\n- Group name.\\n- Subject.\\n- Semester.\\n- Members.\\n- Shared resources.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Course-Based Study Groups\\n\\nThe strongest group experience is connected to subjects.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n\\\"Computer Science Year 1 - Data Structures\\\"\\n\\nMembers share:\\n\\n- Lecture notes.\\n- Study resources.\\n- Discussions.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Shared Knowledge Experience\\n\\nShared resources may include:\\n\\n- Lecture notes.\\n- Summaries.\\n- Learning materials.\\n- Practice questions.\\n- Discussion insights.\\n\\nShared resources remain connected to their academic context.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Personal Knowledge vs Shared Knowledge\\n\\nThe system maintains separation.\\n\\nStructure:\\n\\n``` id=\\\"j3mv6d\\\"\\nShared Knowledge\\n\\n↓\\n\\nStudent Reviews\\n\\n↓\\n\\nStudent Understanding\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPersonal PLKG Update\\n```\\n\\nA shared note does not automatically become personal knowledge.\\n\\nThe student must learn and understand.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Resource Contribution Experience\\n\\nStudents may contribute:\\n\\n- Notes.\\n- Explanations.\\n- Study materials.\\n\\nThe system may track:\\n\\n- Source.\\n- Contributor.\\n- Subject relevance.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. BLIE in Study Groups\\n\\nBLIE can support collaborative learning.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Explain shared materials.\\n- Summarise discussions.\\n- Identify related concepts.\\n- Help resolve questions.\\n\\nBLIE remains subject-aware.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Group Discussion Experience\\n\\nDiscussions should focus on learning.\\n\\nPossible interactions:\\n\\n- Questions.\\n- Explanations.\\n- Concept discussions.\\n- Study planning.\\n\\nThe objective is academic improvement.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Knowledge Quality Experience\\n\\nShared resources should maintain quality.\\n\\nPossible indicators:\\n\\n- Source information.\\n- Community feedback.\\n- Academic relevance.\\n\\nStudents should understand that shared content may require verification.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Privacy \u0026 Permission Model\\n\\nStudents control:\\n\\n- What they share.\\n- Who can access resources.\\n- Group membership.\\n\\nPersonal learning data remains private by default.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Group Learning Progress\\n\\nGroups may view:\\n\\n- Shared activity.\\n- Resource contribution.\\n- Learning milestones.\\n\\nHowever:\\n\\nIndividual mastery remains private.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Group Experience States\\n\\n## Discover\\n\\nStudent finds available groups.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Joined\\n\\nStudent becomes a member.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Active\\n\\nStudents collaborate.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Archived\\n\\nCompleted courses remain accessible as history.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Offline Experience\\n\\nOffline group access:\\n\\nAvailable:\\n\\n- Previously synchronized resources.\\n- Saved discussions.\\n\\nPending:\\n\\n- New messages.\\n- New shared resources.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. Monetisation Integration\\n\\nThe group model supports sustainable growth.\\n\\nPossible subscription structure:\\n\\n## Individual Plan\\n\\nPersonal AI Study Buddy.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Group Plan\\n\\nShared academic environment.\\n\\nBenefits:\\n\\n- Lower cost per student.\\n- Group collaboration.\\n- Shared learning resources.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Future Expansion\\n\\nPotential future academic communities may develop without changing the core architecture.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 18. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe Study Groups \u0026 Knowledge Sharing Experience establishes the collaborative learning layer of AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThe system shall:\\n\\n1. Preserve individual learning ownership.\\n2. Enable structured collaboration.\\n3. Support course-based communities.\\n4. Allow group subscription models.\\n5. Maintain separation between shared resources and personal knowledge.\\n6. Enhance learning through collaboration.\\n\\nAI Study Buddy remains a personal learning companion, strengthened by meaningful communities.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume H10**\\n:::\\n\\nAlhamdulillah.\\n\\n**H10 is complete.**\\n\\nNext:\\n\\n# Volume H11 – Learning Analytics \u0026 Academic Growth Experience\\n\\nThis will define how students understand their progress:\\n\\n- Semester progress\\n- Subject mastery\\n- Knowledge growth\\n- Learning patterns\\n- Achievement milestones\\n- Academic journey from first semester until graduation\\n\\nThis will complete the \\\"living companion\\\" feedback loop.\",{},{\"_305\":653,\"_312\":678,\"_35\":679,\"_37\":680,\"_316\":681,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":682,\"_325\":326},\"c1eba022-91f1-4a93-9134-c34a7646ed6e\",[637],{\"_370\":474,\"_323\":690},1783672915.96932,1783672924.780096,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":688},{\"_350\":494,\"_52\":494,\"_442\":14,\"_334\":683,\"_339\":684,\"_519\":685,\"_521\":686,\"_523\":14,\"_524\":14,\"_525\":14,\"_526\":14,\"_527\":14,\"_528\":687,\"_343\":666,\"_469\":-5,\"_347\":667,\"_349\":667,\"_338\":488,\"_360\":497,\"_353\":14},[],[],[],[],{},[689],\"Begin H10. Introduction\\n\\nThe Study Preparation \u0026 Revision Experience defines how AI Study Buddy helps students prepare before learning and strengthen understanding after learning.\\n\\nThe objective is to move students from passive learning to active knowledge development.\\n\\nThe experience supports the complete learning cycle:\\n\\n```\\nPrepare\\n\\n↓\\n\\nLearn\\n\\n↓\\n\\nUnderstand\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPractice\\n\\n↓\\n\\nReview\\n\\n↓\\n\\nMaster\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Study Preparation Philosophy\\n\\nThe study preparation experience follows these principles.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Preparation Before Learning\\n\\nStudents should not enter a topic without context.\\n\\nAI Study Buddy helps students build the required foundation before lectures begin.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Understanding Before Memorisation\\n\\nThe system prioritises conceptual understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Continuous Reinforcement\\n\\nKnowledge is strengthened through repeated meaningful interaction.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Personalised Learning Path\\n\\nEach student receives guidance based on their PLKG.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Learning Cycle Architecture\\n\\nThe learning cycle:\\n\\n```\\nUpcoming Topic\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPrerequisite Analysis\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPreparation Plan\\n\\n↓\\n\\nLearning Session\\n\\n↓\\n\\nKnowledge Update\\n\\n↓\\n\\nRevision Recommendation\\n\\n↓\\n\\nMastery Development\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Practice Experience\\n\\nPractice activities may include:\\n\\n- Concept questions.\\n- Explanations.\\n- Examples.\\n- Problem-solving exercises.\\n\\nThe objective is understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Study Preparation States\\n\\n## Upcoming\\n\\nTopic identified.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Preparing\\n\\nStudent is building foundations.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning\\n\\nActive study.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Revising\\n\\nKnowledge reinforcement.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Mastered\\n\\nStrong understanding achieved.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 19. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe Study Preparation \u0026 Revision Experience establishes AI Study Buddy as a proactive learning companion.\\n\\nThe system shall:\\n\\n1. Prepare students before topics begin.\\n2. Use PLKG to personalise learning.\\n3. Support continuous revision.\\n4. Identify and recover knowledge gaps.\\n5. Assist assessment preparation.\\n6. Introduction\\n\\nThe Document Library \u0026 Knowledge Processing Experience defines how students manage their academic materials and how AI Study Buddy transforms those materials into structured learning knowledge.\\n\\nStudents commonly receive learning materials in many forms:\\n\\n- Lecture notes.\\n- PDF slides.\\n- Images.\\n- Handwritten notes.\\n- Reference documents.\\n- Study materials.\\n\\nAI Study Buddy converts these disconnected materials into organised knowledge connected to the student's Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG).\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Document Experience Philosophy\\n\\nThe document experience follows these principles.\\n\\n## Knowledge Over Storage\\n\\nThe purpose is not to become a cloud drive.\\n\\nThe purpose is to create understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Simple Capture\\n\\nStudents should easily capture learning materials.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Intelligent Processing\\n\\nAI handles the complexity of organising information.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Student Ownership\\n\\nThe student's learning materials and generated knowledge remain part of their personal learning journey.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Offline Experience\\n\\nOffline document capabilities:\\n\\nAvailable:\\n\\n- Downloaded documents.\\n- Processed text.\\n- Existing knowledge.\\n\\nPending:\\n\\n- New AI processing.\\n- Cloud updates.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. Document States\\n\\n## New Document\\n\\n\\\"Ready for processing.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Processing\\n\\n\\\"AI is understanding your material.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Completed\\n\\n\\\"Knowledge added to your learning journey.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Failed\\n\\n\\\"Processing requires attention.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 18. Introduction\\n\\nThe Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG) Experience defines how students visualize and interact with their personal learning intelligence.\\n\\nThe PLKG represents the evolution of a student's knowledge throughout their university journey.\\n\\nIt transforms learning from disconnected materials into a connected understanding system.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. PLKG Experience Philosophy\\n\\nThe PLKG follows these principles.\\n\\n## Knowledge Growth, Not Data Display\\n\\nThe purpose is understanding, not showing technical graph complexity.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Personal Knowledge Journey\\n\\nEvery student's PLKG is unique.\\n\\nIt reflects:\\n\\n- Subjects studied.\\n- Topics learned.\\n- Concepts understood.\\n- Knowledge relationships.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Progressive Discovery\\n\\nThe graph becomes richer as the student learns.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Action-Oriented Understanding\\n\\nThe PLKG should help students decide:\\n\\n\\\"What should I learn next?\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. PLKG Role in Student Experience\\n\\nThe PLKG connects:\\n\\n``` id=\\\"m7c4d2\\\"\\nCurriculum\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSubjects\\n\\n↓\\n\\nTopics\\n\\n↓\\n\\nConcepts\\n\\n↓\\n\\nStudent Understanding\\n\\n↓\\n\\nLearning Growth\\n```\\n\\nIt becomes the intelligence foundation for personalised learning.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. PLKG Main Views\\n\\nThe student experience includes several perspectives.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Overview View\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nShow overall knowledge growth.\\n\\nDisplays:\\n\\n- Knowledge areas.\\n- Subject connections.\\n- Learning progress.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Subject Knowledge View\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nExplore one subject.\\n\\nDisplays:\\n\\n- Topics.\\n- Concepts.\\n- Relationships.\\n- Progress.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Topic Detail View\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nUnderstand a specific concept.\\n\\nDisplays:\\n\\n- Related concepts.\\n- Required foundations.\\n- Learning status.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Growth Timeline View\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nShow knowledge evolution.\\n\\nDisplays:\\n\\n- Semester progression.\\n- Newly acquired knowledge.\\n- Major milestones.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Knowledge Node Experience\\n\\nA knowledge node represents a learning concept.\\n\\nA node may contain:\\n\\n- Topic name.\\n- Subject relationship.\\n- Learning status.\\n- Confidence level.\\n- Related concepts.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n``` id=\\\"n7f4bq\\\"\\nMachine Learning\\n\\nConnected to:\\n\\n├── Linear Algebra\\n\\n├── Statistics\\n\\n├── Programming\\n\\n└── Algorithms\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Knowledge Relationship Experience\\n\\nRelationships help students understand connections.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n## Foundation Relationship\\n\\n\\\"This concept requires understanding of...\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Application Relationship\\n\\n\\\"This concept is used in...\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Similarity Relationship\\n\\n\\\"This concept is related to...\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Progression Relationship\\n\\n\\\"This concept leads to...\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Knowledge States\\n\\nEach knowledge node may represent learning progress.\\n\\nExample states:\\n\\n## Introduced\\n\\nStudent has encountered the concept.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning\\n\\nStudent is currently studying.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Understanding\\n\\nStudent demonstrates understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Mastered\\n\\nStudent has strong confidence.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Needs Review\\n\\nStudent requires reinforcement.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. PLKG and BLIE Integration\\n\\nBLIE uses PLKG information to provide personalised assistance.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nStudent asks:\\n\\n\\\"Explain recursion.\\\"\\n\\nPLKG shows:\\n\\n- Student knows functions.\\n- Student struggles with algorithm thinking.\\n\\nBLIE adjusts the explanation accordingly.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Knowledge Gap Experience\\n\\nThe PLKG helps identify missing foundations.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nStudent learning:\\n\\nDeep Learning\\n\\nSystem identifies:\\n\\nNeeds review:\\n\\n- Matrix operations.\\n- Probability concepts.\\n\\nThe application recommends preparation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Learning Path Experience\\n\\nThe PLKG can guide future learning.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nCurrent:\\n\\nProgramming Basics\\n\\n↓\\n\\nNext:\\n\\nData Structures\\n\\n↓\\n\\nFuture:\\n\\nArtificial Intelligence\\n\\nThe student understands the learning journey.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Visual Design Principles\\n\\nThe PLKG visualization should be:\\n\\n## Understandable\\n\\nStudents should not need graph knowledge.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Calm\\n\\nAvoid overwhelming visual complexity.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Interactive\\n\\nStudents can explore relationships naturally.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Educational\\n\\nEvery visual element should communicate learning value.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. PLKG Interaction Patterns\\n\\nStudents may:\\n\\n- Select knowledge nodes.\\n- Explore relationships.\\n- Ask BLIE about concepts.\\n- Review learning history.\\n- Discover related topics.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Mobile Experience Considerations\\n\\nBecause AI Study Buddy is mobile-first:\\n\\nThe PLKG should support:\\n\\n- Simplified overview.\\n- Focused exploration.\\n- Search-based discovery.\\n- Topic-centered navigation.\\n\\nA complete graph view should not overwhelm small screens.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. PLKG Growth Experience\\n\\nStudents should feel their knowledge expanding.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\nSemester 1:\\n\\nBasic foundation.\\n\\nSemester 3:\\n\\nConnected knowledge areas.\\n\\nFinal Year:\\n\\nComplex interdisciplinary understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Privacy and Ownership\\n\\nThe PLKG belongs to the student.\\n\\nStudents should control:\\n\\n- Their learning history.\\n- Their personal knowledge data.\\n- Sharing permissions.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Offline Experience\\n\\nOffline PLKG support:\\n\\nAvailable:\\n\\n- Cached knowledge.\\n- Existing relationships.\\n- Personal progress.\\n\\nPending:\\n\\n- New cloud-generated updates.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. PLKG States\\n\\n## New Student\\n\\n\\\"Your knowledge journey begins here.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Growing\\n\\n\\\"Your knowledge network is expanding.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Complex Knowledge\\n\\n\\\"Your subjects are becoming connected.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Graduation Journey\\n\\n\\\"Your academic knowledge history.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 18. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe PLKG Experience establishes the visual and interaction model for personal knowledge growth.\\n\\nThe PLKG shall:\\n\\n1. Represent the student's personal learning journey.\\n2. Connect subjects, topics, and concepts.\\n3. Support BLIE personalisation.\\n4. Reveal knowledge gaps.\\n5. Show academic growth over time.\\n6. Help students understand what to learn next.\\n\\nThe PLKG is the foundation that makes AI Study Buddy a lifelong learning companion rather than a simple study application.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume H7**\\n:::\\n\\nAlhamdulillah.\\n\\n**H7 is complete.**\\n\\nNext:\\n\\n# Volume H8 – Document Library \u0026 Knowledge Processing Experience\\n\\nThis will define how students interact with their learning materials:\\n\\n- Upload lecture PDFs/images\\n- AI extraction experience\\n- Processing status\\n- Converted knowledge\\n- Notes organisation\\n- Search\\n- Connection into PLKG\\n\\nThis is where raw student materials become personal intelligence.\",{},{\"_305\":776,\"_312\":803,\"_35\":804,\"_37\":805,\"_316\":806,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":807,\"_325\":326},\"5f822f57-3058-4ff5-8717-93bb8b59ec88\",[760],{\"_370\":474,\"_323\":815},1783672868.108983,1783672879.040132,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":813},{\"_350\":494,\"_52\":494,\"_442\":14,\"_334\":808,\"_339\":809,\"_519\":810,\"_521\":811,\"_523\":14,\"_524\":14,\"_525\":14,\"_526\":14,\"_527\":14,\"_528\":812,\"_343\":789,\"_469\":-5,\"_347\":790,\"_349\":790,\"_338\":488,\"_360\":497,\"_353\":14},[],[],[],[],{},[814],\"Begin H7. Introduction\\n\\nThe BLIE Experience defines how students interact with the Buddy Learning Intelligent Engine.\\n\\nBLIE is the intelligence layer that helps students:\\n\\n- Understand concepts.\\n- Prepare before learning.\\n- Clarify confusion.\\n- Connect knowledge.\\n- Improve mastery.\\n\\nBLIE transforms AI Study Buddy from a learning application into a personal educational companion.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. BLIE Experience Philosophy\\n\\nBLIE follows these principles.\\n\\n## Learning Companion, Not Chatbot\\n\\nBLIE should feel like a knowledgeable study partner.\\n\\nThe objective is not answering questions only.\\n\\nThe objective is improving understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Context-Aware Intelligence\\n\\nBLIE understands:\\n\\n- Current subject.\\n- Current topic.\\n- Student knowledge level.\\n- Previous learning history.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Guided Learning\\n\\nBLIE should guide students toward understanding rather than simply providing answers.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Student Growth Focus\\n\\nEvery interaction should contribute to learning progress.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. BLIE Role in Student Journey\\n\\nBLIE supports four learning stages.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Before Learning\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nPrepare the student.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Explain upcoming concepts.\\n- Identify prerequisites.\\n- Provide background knowledge.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## During Learning\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nSupport understanding.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Explain difficult concepts.\\n- Answer questions.\\n- Connect ideas.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## After Learning\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nStrengthen memory.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Summarise topics.\\n- Generate revision materials.\\n- Test understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Before Assessment\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nBuild confidence.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Practice questions.\\n- Identify weak areas.\\n- Review important concepts.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. BLIE Entry Points\\n\\nBLIE is available throughout the application.\\n\\nEntry points include:\\n\\n## Dashboard\\n\\nGeneral learning guidance.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Subject Workspace\\n\\nSubject-specific assistance.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Topic View\\n\\nConcept-level explanations.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## PLKG\\n\\nKnowledge exploration.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Revision\\n\\nAssessment preparation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. BLIE Conversation Experience\\n\\nThe conversation experience should feel educational.\\n\\nA typical interaction:\\n\\nStudent Question\\n\\n↓\\n\\nContext Understanding\\n\\n↓\\n\\nKnowledge Retrieval\\n\\n↓\\n\\nReasoning\\n\\n↓\\n\\nLearning Response\\n\\n↓\\n\\nNext Learning Action\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. BLIE Response Design\\n\\nBLIE responses should be structured.\\n\\nA response may contain:\\n\\n## Explanation\\n\\nClear concept explanation.\\n\\n## Connection\\n\\nRelationship with existing knowledge.\\n\\n## Example\\n\\nPractical illustration.\\n\\n## Check Understanding\\n\\nQuestion or activity.\\n\\n## Next Step\\n\\nRecommended learning action.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Explanation Modes\\n\\nStudents learn differently.\\n\\nBLIE may provide different explanation approaches:\\n\\n## Simple Explanation\\n\\nFor first understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Detailed Explanation\\n\\nFor deeper study.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Example-Based Explanation\\n\\nFor practical understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Comparison Explanation\\n\\nFor distinguishing concepts.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Step-by-Step Explanation\\n\\nFor complex processes.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. BLIE Learning Guidance\\n\\nBLIE should proactively support learning.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n\\\"You are starting Algorithms next week. Would you like to review prerequisite concepts?\\\"\\n\\n\\\"You struggled with recursion previously. Would you like a quick revision?\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. BLIE and PLKG Integration\\n\\nBLIE uses the student's Personal Learning Knowledge Graph.\\n\\nThe PLKG helps BLIE understand:\\n\\n- What the student knows.\\n- What concepts are related.\\n- What foundations may be missing.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nStudent asks:\\n\\n\\\"Explain neural networks.\\\"\\n\\nBLIE understands whether the student already understands:\\n\\n- Linear algebra.\\n- Probability.\\n- Machine learning basics.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. BLIE Memory Experience\\n\\nBLIE should provide continuity.\\n\\nThe student should feel:\\n\\n\\\"You remember my learning journey.\\\"\\n\\nMemory may include:\\n\\n- Previous discussions.\\n- Learning progress.\\n- Preferred explanations.\\n- Knowledge gaps.\\n\\nMemory must always respect privacy controls.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. BLIE Learning Actions\\n\\nBLIE may suggest:\\n\\n- Study preparation.\\n- Revision.\\n- Practice questions.\\n- Related topics.\\n- Knowledge review.\\n\\nSuggestions should support learning goals.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. BLIE Trust Experience\\n\\nStudents must understand:\\n\\n- Where knowledge comes from.\\n- When confidence is limited.\\n- How answers are generated.\\n\\nBLIE should encourage verification and deeper learning.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. BLIE Visual Components\\n\\nBLIE interface uses educational components:\\n\\n## AI Response Card\\n\\nFor explanations.\\n\\n## Knowledge Link Card\\n\\nShows related concepts.\\n\\n## Learning Action Card\\n\\nSuggests next steps.\\n\\n## Progress Card\\n\\nShows learning impact.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. BLIE States\\n\\nRequired states:\\n\\n## Thinking\\n\\nAI processing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Responding\\n\\nResponse generation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning\\n\\nUpdating student knowledge.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Offline\\n\\nLimited local assistance.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Error\\n\\nUnable to complete request.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Voice Interaction Readiness\\n\\nThe BLIE experience should support future voice interaction.\\n\\nDesign considerations:\\n\\n- Natural conversation.\\n- Spoken explanations.\\n- Accessibility.\\n\\nVoice capability must follow the same educational principles.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Responsible AI Principles\\n\\nBLIE shall:\\n\\n- Avoid pretending certainty.\\n- Encourage understanding.\\n- Protect student privacy.\\n- Support academic integrity.\\n\\nBLIE helps students learn; it does not replace learning effort.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe BLIE Experience establishes how students interact with AI Study Buddy intelligence.\\n\\nBLIE shall:\\n\\n1. Act as a learning companion.\\n2. Understand student context.\\n3. Support preparation, learning, revision, and assessment.\\n4. Use PLKG to personalise guidance.\\n5. Build long-term learning continuity.\\n6. Introduction\\n\\nThe Subject Workspace defines the primary academic environment for each university subject.\\n\\nEvery enrolled subject becomes an intelligent learning space connected to:\\n\\n- Curriculum structure.\\n- Student materials.\\n- BLIE assistance.\\n- Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG).\\n- Learning progress.\\n\\nThe Subject Workspace answers:\\n\\n\u003e \\\"How can I understand and master this subject?\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Subject Workspace Philosophy\\n\\nThe Subject Workspace follows these principles.\\n\\n## Subject-Centred Learning\\n\\nLearning activities are organised around academic subjects.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Knowledge Over Storage\\n\\nMaterials are transformed into understanding.\\n\\nThe workspace is not a file repository.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Context-Aware Intelligence\\n\\nBLIE understands the current subject context.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Progressive Mastery\\n\\nStudents move from:\\n\\nIntroduction\\n\\n↓\\n\\nUnderstanding\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPractice\\n\\n↓\\n\\nMastery\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Subject Workspace Structure\\n\\nThe subject hierarchy:\\n\\n```\\nSubject\\n\\n├── Overview\\n\\n├── Topics\\n\\n├── Materials\\n\\n├── Study Preparation\\n\\n├── Learning Sessions\\n\\n├── Revision\\n\\n├── Assessment\\n\\n├── Knowledge Map\\n\\n└── Progress\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Subject Overview\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nProvide immediate understanding of the subject.\\n\\nDisplays:\\n\\n- Subject name.\\n- Subject code.\\n- Semester.\\n- Lecturer information (optional).\\n- Progress status.\\n- Current learning focus.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nData Structures\\n\\nCurrent Topic:\\nTrees\\n\\nLearning Status:\\nDeveloping Understanding\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Topic Learning Experience\\n\\nFor each topic, students can:\\n\\n- Read explanations.\\n- Ask BLIE questions.\\n- Review materials.\\n- Explore related concepts.\\n- Practice understanding.\\n\\nThe objective is comprehension, not information consumption.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Materials Experience\\n\\nMaterials include:\\n\\n- Lecture notes.\\n- PDF documents.\\n- Images.\\n- Slides.\\n- References.\\n- Personal notes.\\n\\nMaterials are processed into structured knowledge.\\n\\nThe student sees both:\\n\\nOriginal Material\\n\\n+\\n\\nExtracted Learning Knowledge\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Revision Experience\\n\\nRevision connects previous learning.\\n\\nStudents can:\\n\\n- Review topics.\\n- Identify weak areas.\\n- Ask BLIE for clarification.\\n- Practice understanding.\\n\\nRevision is personalised based on knowledge state.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Subject Knowledge Map\\n\\nEach subject has a connected knowledge view.\\n\\nStudents can see:\\n\\n- Topics.\\n- Relationships.\\n- Learning progress.\\n- Missing foundations.\\n\\nThe subject knowledge map contributes to the overall PLKG.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Subject Progress\\n\\nProgress should represent understanding.\\n\\nPossible indicators:\\n\\n- Topics introduced.\\n- Topics understood.\\n- Topics requiring review.\\n- Mastery development.\\n\\nCompletion alone is not sufficient.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Collaboration Readiness\\n\\nThe Subject Workspace can later support:\\n\\n- Shared resources.\\n- Study groups.\\n- Collaborative knowledge.\\n\\nHowever, personal learning remains the foundation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. It is the student's **learning cockpit** — a place where the student immediately understands:\\n\\n- Where am I in my academic journey?\\n- What should I focus on today?\\n- How is my knowledge growing?\\n- How can BLIE help me?\\n\\nThis document defines the experience architecture, while detailed screen layouts and Figma components can be expanded later.\\n\\n---\\n\\n:::writing{variant=\\\"document\\\" id=\\\"74193\\\"}\\n# AI Study Buddy\\n\\n# Volume H4 – Dashboard Experience\\n\\n**Version:** 1.0 (Architecture Freeze)\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 1. Introduction\\n\\nThe Dashboard Experience defines the primary student interface after onboarding.\\n\\nThe Dashboard acts as the student's personal academic command centre throughout their university journey.\\n\\nIts purpose is to transform complex academic information into a clear daily learning direction.\\n\\nThe Dashboard answers:\\n\\n\u003e \\\"What should I learn, understand, and improve today?\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Dashboard Philosophy\\n\\nThe Dashboard follows these principles:\\n\\n## Context Before Action\\n\\nStudents should first understand their current academic situation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Guidance Over Information\\n\\nThe Dashboard should recommend meaningful actions rather than display excessive data.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Personalised Experience\\n\\nEvery student sees a different Dashboard based on:\\n\\n- Semester.\\n- Subjects.\\n- Learning progress.\\n- Knowledge gaps.\\n- Study habits.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Growth Visibility\\n\\nThe student should see evidence that their knowledge is growing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Dashboard Structure\\n\\nThe Dashboard follows this information hierarchy:\\n\\n```\\nStudent Context\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCurrent Priorities\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSubject Progress\\n\\n↓\\n\\nLearning Actions\\n\\n↓\\n\\nKnowledge Growth\\n\\n↓\\n\\nBLIE Support\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Dashboard Main Areas\\n\\nThe Dashboard consists of:\\n\\n1. Academic Overview\\n2. Today's Learning\\n3. Subject Progress\\n4. BLIE Guidance\\n5. Knowledge Growth\\n6. Upcoming Activities\\n7. Recent Learning History\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Academic Overview\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nProvide immediate understanding of the student's current academic position.\\n\\nDisplays:\\n\\n- Student name.\\n- Current semester.\\n- Programme.\\n- Academic progress.\\n- Current learning stage.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n\\\"Semester 2 • Computer Science • 5 subjects\\\"\\n\\nThe student immediately understands their current journey.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Today's Learning Section\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nGuide the student's daily study activity.\\n\\nThe system presents:\\n\\n- Recommended study tasks.\\n- Upcoming topics.\\n- Revision suggestions.\\n- Preparation activities.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n\\\"Prepare before tomorrow's Database Systems lecture\\\"\\n\\n\\\"Review prerequisite concepts for Algorithms\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. BLIE Daily Guidance\\n\\nBLIE appears as a learning companion.\\n\\nPossible interactions:\\n\\n- \\\"You have a lecture tomorrow. Would you like a preparation overview?\\\"\\n- \\\"You struggled with this concept previously. Let's review it.\\\"\\n- \\\"Your exam is approaching. Here is a revision plan.\\\"\\n\\nBLIE guidance is contextual, not random.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Subject Progress Overview\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nProvide a quick view of academic status.\\n\\nEach subject displays:\\n\\n- Progress.\\n- Current topic.\\n- Knowledge confidence.\\n- Upcoming activities.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nDatabase Systems\\n\\nTopic:\\nRelational Model\\n\\nStatus:\\nLearning\\n\\nNext:\\nPractice Questions\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Knowledge Growth Indicator\\n\\nThe Dashboard provides a simplified view of PLKG growth.\\n\\nIt should communicate:\\n\\n- Knowledge acquired.\\n- Topics connected.\\n- Learning progress.\\n\\nThe Dashboard does not replace the full PLKG view.\\n\\nIt provides motivation and awareness.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Learning Readiness\\n\\nA key differentiator of AI Study Buddy is preparation before learning.\\n\\nThe Dashboard may show:\\n\\n\\\"Upcoming Topic\\\"\\n\\n↓\\n\\n\\\"Required Background Knowledge\\\"\\n\\n↓\\n\\n\\\"Preparation Status\\\"\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nBefore studying Machine Learning:\\n\\n\\\"Review:\\n- Linear Algebra basics\\n- Probability concepts\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Upcoming Academic Activities\\n\\nDisplays:\\n\\n- Lectures.\\n- Assignments.\\n- Tests.\\n- Revision goals.\\n\\nThe purpose is academic awareness.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Recent Learning History\\n\\nStudents can see:\\n\\n- Recently studied topics.\\n- BLIE conversations.\\n- Completed activities.\\n- Knowledge updates.\\n\\nThis reinforces continuity.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Empty States\\n\\nThe Dashboard handles early student states.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n## New Student\\n\\nShows:\\n\\n\\\"Your learning journey begins here.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n## No Materials\\n\\nShows:\\n\\n\\\"Upload your first lecture note to start building your knowledge.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n## No Activity\\n\\nShows:\\n\\n\\\"Ask BLIE about your first subject.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Offline Dashboard Experience\\n\\nWhen offline, the Dashboard displays:\\n\\nAvailable:\\n\\n- Cached subjects.\\n- Downloaded materials.\\n- Previous learning progress.\\n\\nUnavailable:\\n\\n- Real-time AI processing.\\n- Cloud updates.\\n\\nThe student should understand the current state.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Dashboard Personalisation\\n\\nThe Dashboard evolves with the student.\\n\\nFirst Semester:\\n\\nFocus:\\n\\n- Understanding subjects.\\n- Building study habits.\\n\\nMiddle Years:\\n\\nFocus:\\n\\n- Knowledge connections.\\n- Deeper learning.\\n\\nFinal Year:\\n\\nFocus:\\n\\n- Advanced knowledge.\\n- Projects.\\n- Graduation preparation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Dashboard Interaction Principles\\n\\nThe Dashboard should:\\n\\n## Reduce Anxiety\\n\\nStudents should know what to do next.\\n\\n## Encourage Progress\\n\\nStudents should see improvement.\\n\\n## Support Independence\\n\\nStudents remain responsible for learning.\\n\\n## Enable Discovery\\n\\nStudents discover useful learning paths naturally.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe Dashboard Experience establishes the student's daily interaction centre.\\n\\nThe Dashboard shall:\\n\\n1. Present academic context clearly.\\n2. Guide daily learning activities.\\n3. Connect students with BLIE.\\n4. Reflect PLKG growth.\\n5. Support preparation before learning.\\n6. Adapt throughout the student's university journey.\\n\\nThe Dashboard is the primary bridge between the student and the AI Study Buddy ecosystem.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume H4**\\n:::\\n\\nAlhamdulillah.\\n\\n**H4 is complete.**\\n\\nNext:\\n\\n# Volume H5 – Subject Workspace Experience\\n\\nThis will define the most important academic workspace:\\n\\n- Subject overview\\n- Topic structure\\n- Lecture materials\\n- BLIE inside a subject context\\n- Study preparation\\n- Revision\\n- Assessment support\\n- Subject-level PLKG connection\\n\\nThis is where the student's daily university learning actually happens.\",{},{\"_305\":896,\"_312\":923,\"_35\":924,\"_37\":925,\"_316\":926,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":927,\"_325\":326},\"33c31f0e-c1e5-4a54-932f-51aad58ec400\",[880],{\"_370\":474,\"_323\":935},1783672761.689146,1783672771.862517,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":933},{\"_350\":494,\"_52\":494,\"_442\":14,\"_334\":928,\"_339\":929,\"_519\":930,\"_521\":931,\"_523\":14,\"_524\":14,\"_525\":14,\"_526\":14,\"_527\":14,\"_528\":932,\"_343\":909,\"_469\":-5,\"_347\":910,\"_349\":910,\"_338\":488,\"_360\":497,\"_353\":14},[],[],[],[],{},[934],\"Begin H4. Detailed Figma specifications can be expanded later.\\n\\n---\\n\\n:::writing{variant=\\\"document\\\" id=\\\"62947\\\"}\\n# AI Study Buddy\\n\\n# Volume H3 – Student Onboarding Experience\\n\\n**Version:** 1.0 (Architecture Freeze)\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 1. Introduction\\n\\nThe Student Onboarding Experience defines how a new student enters the AI Study Buddy ecosystem.\\n\\nThe objective of onboarding is to transform a new user into an active learner by:\\n\\n- Understanding the student's academic journey.\\n- Establishing their learning environment.\\n- Preparing the initial Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG).\\n- Introducing BLIE as a personal learning companion.\\n\\nOnboarding is the foundation of a multi-year relationship.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Onboarding Philosophy\\n\\nThe onboarding experience follows these principles:\\n\\n## Simple Start\\n\\nStudents should begin quickly without unnecessary complexity.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Personal From Day One\\n\\nThe application begins understanding the student's academic context immediately.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Guided Setup\\n\\nStudents are guided step-by-step rather than presented with complex configurations.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Immediate Value\\n\\nStudents should experience the benefit of AI Study Buddy early.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Onboarding Journey Overview\\n\\nThe onboarding flow:\\n\\n```\\nFirst Launch\\n\\n↓\\n\\nWelcome\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAccount Creation\\n\\n↓\\n\\nStudent Profile\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAcademic Setup\\n\\n↓\\n\\nProgramme Selection\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSemester Setup\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSubject Enrolment\\n\\n↓\\n\\nLearning Preferences\\n\\n↓\\n\\nInitial PLKG Creation\\n\\n↓\\n\\nBLIE Introduction\\n\\n↓\\n\\nStudent Dashboard\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. First Launch Experience\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nIntroduce the purpose of AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThe first impression should communicate:\\n\\n\\\"You now have a learning companion for your university journey.\\\"\\n\\nKey messages:\\n\\n- Understand your subjects.\\n- Build your knowledge.\\n- Study smarter with AI assistance.\\n\\nThe experience should feel welcoming and professional.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Account Creation\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nCreate the student's personal learning account.\\n\\nRequired functions:\\n\\n- Registration.\\n- Authentication.\\n- Account verification.\\n- Secure login.\\n\\nThe process should minimise friction.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Student Profile Setup\\n\\nThe student provides basic academic identity information.\\n\\nInformation includes:\\n\\n- Name.\\n- Preferred learning language.\\n- Academic level.\\n- Learning preferences.\\n\\nThe purpose is personalisation, not data collection.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Academic Profile Setup\\n\\nThis is the foundation of the student's learning environment.\\n\\nThe student defines:\\n\\n- University.\\n- Programme.\\n- Field of study.\\n- Academic year.\\n- Current semester.\\n\\nThis information establishes the academic context for BLIE.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Programme Selection\\n\\nThe student selects their academic programme.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nUniversity\\n\\n↓\\n\\nFaculty\\n\\n↓\\n\\nProgramme\\n\\n↓\\n\\nYear\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSemester\\n```\\n\\nThis allows AI Study Buddy to understand the student's curriculum journey.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Semester Setup\\n\\nThe student creates their current semester.\\n\\nInformation includes:\\n\\n- Semester number.\\n- Academic period.\\n- Current subjects.\\n\\nThe semester becomes the first learning container.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Subject Enrolment\\n\\nStudents select their current subjects.\\n\\nFor each subject:\\n\\nInformation may include:\\n\\n- Subject name.\\n- Subject code.\\n- Credit hours.\\n- Lecturer information (optional).\\n- Available materials.\\n\\nAfter enrolment:\\n\\nThe Subject Workspace is created.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Initial PLKG Creation\\n\\nAfter academic setup, the system creates the student's initial Personal Learning Knowledge Graph.\\n\\nInitial graph sources:\\n\\n- Programme structure.\\n- Semester subjects.\\n- Subject topics.\\n- Curriculum relationships.\\n\\nAt this stage, the PLKG represents:\\n\\n\\\"What the student needs to learn.\\\"\\n\\nOver time it evolves into:\\n\\n\\\"What the student knows.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Learning Preference Setup\\n\\nStudents may configure learning preferences.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Preferred explanation style.\\n- Study goals.\\n- Learning pace.\\n\\nThese preferences help BLIE personalize interactions.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. BLIE Introduction\\n\\nThis is the first emotional connection with the AI companion.\\n\\nThe student is introduced to BLIE as:\\n\\n\\\"A learning partner that understands your subjects and helps you prepare, learn, and revise.\\\"\\n\\nThe introduction should demonstrate:\\n\\n- Asking questions.\\n- Getting explanations.\\n- Receiving study guidance.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. First Learning Interaction\\n\\nThe onboarding should end with immediate educational value.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\nBLIE may:\\n\\n- Explain the student's first subject.\\n- Show upcoming topics.\\n- Suggest preparation steps.\\n\\nThe student should understand:\\n\\n\\\"This app already knows my learning journey.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Dashboard Transition\\n\\nAfter onboarding completion:\\n\\nThe student enters the main learning environment.\\n\\nThe Dashboard should display:\\n\\n- Current semester.\\n- Subjects.\\n- First learning recommendations.\\n- BLIE availability.\\n- Initial knowledge graph status.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Returning Student Experience\\n\\nReturning users should not repeat onboarding.\\n\\nInstead:\\n\\nThe application recognises:\\n\\n- Academic progress.\\n- Previous learning history.\\n- Existing PLKG.\\n- Current semester.\\n\\nThe experience continues from where the student stopped.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. Onboarding States\\n\\nEvery onboarding step requires defined states.\\n\\n## Loading\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nCreating PLKG.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Empty\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nNo subjects selected.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Error\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nUnable to load programme data.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Offline\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nSetup partially completed without connection.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Completed\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nAcademic environment successfully created.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 18. Privacy \u0026 Trust\\n\\nDuring onboarding, students must understand:\\n\\n- What information is collected.\\n- Why it is needed.\\n- How it improves learning.\\n\\nTransparency builds trust from the beginning.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 19. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe Student Onboarding Experience establishes the foundation of the student's relationship with AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThe onboarding shall:\\n\\n1. Introduce the purpose clearly.\\n2. Create a personalised learning environment.\\n3. Establish academic context.\\n4. Begin construction of the student's PLKG.\\n5. Introduce BLIE as a learning companion.\\n6. Deliver immediate educational value.\\n\\nThe onboarding experience is the beginning of the student's multi-year learning journey.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume H3**\\n:::\\n\\nAlhamdulillah.\\n\\n**H3 is complete.**\\n\\nThe next document is:\\n\\n# Volume H4 – Dashboard Experience\\n\\nThis will define the student's daily command centre:\\n\\n- What they see when opening the app\\n- Semester overview\\n- Today's learning priorities\\n- Subject progress\\n- BLIE recommendations\\n- Knowledge growth indicators\\n- Study preparation prompts\\n\\nThis Introduction\\n\\nThe Information Architecture \u0026 Navigation Specification defines the structural organisation of AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThe objective is to create a navigation experience that feels natural for university students while supporting a multi-year learning relationship.\\n\\nThe application structure follows the student's academic journey rather than being organised around technical features.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Information Architecture Principles\\n\\nThe information architecture follows these principles.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Student Journey First\\n\\nThe application structure follows:\\n\\nSemester → Subject → Topic → Knowledge → Mastery\\n\\nrather than:\\n\\nFeature → Tool → Setting.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Context Before Action\\n\\nStudents should understand their current learning context before taking action.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nCurrent semester\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCurrent subjects\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCurrent topics\\n\\n↓\\n\\nRecommended learning actions\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Progressive Discovery\\n\\nNew students should not see unnecessary complexity.\\n\\nAdvanced capabilities become available naturally as learning progresses.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Personal Knowledge Foundation\\n\\nEvery major learning activity connects back to the student's Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG).\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Application Information Model\\n\\nThe application hierarchy is:\\n\\n```\\nStudent\\n\\n └── Academic Journey\\n\\n      └── Programme\\n\\n           └── Semester\\n\\n                └── Subject\\n\\n                     └── Topic\\n\\n                          └── Knowledge\\n\\n                               └── Learning Progress\\n```\\n\\nThis hierarchy represents the student's academic reality.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Primary Application Areas\\n\\nThe application consists of five primary areas.\\n\\n## 1. Home\\n\\nStudent command centre.\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\n- Understand current learning status.\\n- See priorities.\\n- Access important activities.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 2. Subjects\\n\\nAcademic workspace.\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\n- Manage subjects.\\n- Access materials.\\n- Study topics.\\n- Track progress.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 3. BLIE\\n\\nPersonal learning companion.\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\n- Ask questions.\\n- Receive explanations.\\n- Get guidance.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 4. Knowledge\\n\\nPersonal knowledge growth.\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\n- Explore PLKG.\\n- Understand relationships.\\n- Track mastery.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 5. Profile\\n\\nPersonal management.\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\n- Account.\\n- Preferences.\\n- Subscription.\\n- Privacy.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Main Navigation Structure\\n\\nThe mobile application uses a simple primary navigation.\\n\\nRecommended structure:\\n\\n```\\nHome\\n\\nSubjects\\n\\nBLIE\\n\\nKnowledge\\n\\nProfile\\n```\\n\\nThe navigation remains available throughout the student journey.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Home Information Architecture\\n\\nHome provides an overview of current learning.\\n\\nStructure:\\n\\n```\\nHome\\n\\n ├── Semester Overview\\n\\n ├── Today's Learning\\n\\n ├── Subject Progress\\n\\n ├── Upcoming Activities\\n\\n ├── BLIE Suggestions\\n\\n └── Recent Knowledge Growth\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Subject Information Architecture\\n\\nSubjects are the primary academic workspace.\\n\\nStructure:\\n\\n```\\nSubjects\\n\\n └── Subject\\n\\n      ├── Overview\\n\\n      ├── Topics\\n\\n      ├── Materials\\n\\n      ├── Study Preparation\\n\\n      ├── Revision\\n\\n      ├── Assessment\\n\\n      ├── BLIE Support\\n\\n      └── Knowledge Map\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. BLIE Information Architecture\\n\\nBLIE is available across the application.\\n\\nStructure:\\n\\n```\\nBLIE\\n\\n ├── Conversation\\n\\n ├── Learning Questions\\n\\n ├── Explanations\\n\\n ├── Study Guidance\\n\\n ├── Revision Support\\n\\n └── Recommendations\\n```\\n\\nBLIE remains context-aware.\\n\\nA question from a subject page automatically includes subject context.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Knowledge Information Architecture\\n\\nThe Knowledge section represents the student's learning intelligence.\\n\\nStructure:\\n\\n```\\nKnowledge\\n\\n ├── Knowledge Graph\\n\\n ├── Topics\\n\\n ├── Mastery\\n\\n ├── Learning Gaps\\n\\n └── Growth History\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Document Information Architecture\\n\\nDocuments exist within the learning context.\\n\\nStructure:\\n\\n```\\nSubject\\n\\n └── Materials\\n\\n      ├── Uploaded Documents\\n\\n      ├── Processed Knowledge\\n\\n      ├── Extracted Concepts\\n\\n      └── Related Topics\\n```\\n\\nDocuments are not isolated storage objects.\\n\\nThey become part of the student's knowledge journey.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Academic Lifecycle Navigation\\n\\nThe application supports the full university lifecycle.\\n\\n## First Semester\\n\\nFocus:\\n\\n- Setup.\\n- Understanding subjects.\\n- Building initial knowledge.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Middle Semesters\\n\\nFocus:\\n\\n- Knowledge expansion.\\n- Deeper subject relationships.\\n- Improved learning habits.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Final Year\\n\\nFocus:\\n\\n- Advanced knowledge.\\n- Projects.\\n- Research.\\n- Graduation preparation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Navigation Context\\n\\nThe application maintains student context.\\n\\nContext includes:\\n\\n- Current semester.\\n- Active subject.\\n- Current topic.\\n- Recent learning activity.\\n\\nThis allows BLIE and the interface to remain relevant.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Search Architecture\\n\\nSearch supports discovery across:\\n\\n- Subjects.\\n- Topics.\\n- Documents.\\n- Knowledge nodes.\\n- Learning history.\\n\\nSearch results should prioritize relevance to the student's academic context.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Notification Architecture\\n\\nNotifications support learning activities.\\n\\nCategories include:\\n\\n## Academic\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Upcoming assessments.\\n- Subject milestones.\\n\\n## Learning\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Revision reminders.\\n- Recommended preparation.\\n\\n## System\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Synchronization.\\n- Processing completion.\\n\\nNotifications should assist learning, not interrupt unnecessarily.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Offline Navigation\\n\\nThe application maintains usable navigation during offline mode.\\n\\nStudents can access:\\n\\n- Downloaded materials.\\n- Cached knowledge.\\n- Previous learning activities.\\n\\nUnavailable features should be clearly indicated.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Future Screen Mapping\\n\\nThe Information Architecture provides the foundation for future detailed specifications:\\n\\n- H3 – Student Onboarding\\n- H4 – Dashboard\\n- H5 – Subject Workspace\\n- H6 – BLIE Experience\\n- H7 – PLKG Experience\\n- H8 – Document Experience\\n- H9 – Study Preparation \u0026 Revision\\n- H10 – Study Groups\\n- H11 – Analytics \u0026 Growth\\n- H12 – Profile \u0026 Settings\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe Information Architecture establishes how students navigate AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThe application shall:\\n\\n1. Organise around the student's academic journey.\\n2. Make subjects the primary learning workspace.\\n3. Integrate BLIE throughout the experience.\\n4. Make PLKG the foundation of personal knowledge.\\n5. Maintain simple and predictable navigation.\\n6. Support students from first semester until graduation.\\n\\nDetailed screen designs and interaction specifications will be developed in subsequent Volume H documents.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume H2**\\n:::\\n\\nAlhamdulillah.\\n\\n**H2 is complete.**\\n\\nWe now have the foundation for the actual student-facing experience:\\n\\n✅ H0 – UX Philosophy  \\n✅ H1 – Design System Foundation  \\n✅ H2 – Information Architecture \u0026 Navigation  \\n\\nNext is:\\n\\n**Volume H3 – Student Onboarding Experience**\\n\\nThis will define the student's first interaction with AI Study Buddy:\\n- First launch\\n- Account creation\\n- Academic profile setup\\n- Programme and semester setup\\n- Subject enrolment\\n- Initial PLKG creation\\n- First BLIE introduction\\n\\nThis is the moment where the \\\"living study buddy\\\" relationship begins.\",{},{\"_305\":977,\"_312\":1018,\"_35\":1019,\"_37\":1020,\"_316\":1021,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":1022,\"_325\":326},\"27788c08-d5b8-4b0e-8181-2c99e348537f\",[962],{\"_370\":474,\"_323\":1030},1783671972.089122,1783671984.155415,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":1028},{\"_350\":494,\"_52\":494,\"_442\":14,\"_334\":1023,\"_339\":1024,\"_519\":1025,\"_521\":1026,\"_523\":14,\"_524\":14,\"_525\":14,\"_526\":14,\"_527\":14,\"_528\":1027,\"_343\":990,\"_469\":-5,\"_347\":991,\"_349\":991,\"_338\":488,\"_360\":497,\"_353\":14},[],[],[],[],{},[1029],\"Begin H2. Introduction\\n\\nThe Design System defines the visual language, reusable components, and interaction standards for AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThe purpose of the Design System is to ensure that every part of the application delivers a consistent, accessible, and student-centred experience.\\n\\nThe Design System serves as the foundation for:\\n\\n- Figma design.\\n- Frontend implementation.\\n- Component development.\\n- Future platform expansion.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Design System Principles\\n\\nThe Design System follows the UX philosophy established in H0.\\n\\n## Clarity\\n\\nInterfaces should make learning easier to understand.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Consistency\\n\\nThe same interaction should look and behave the same everywhere.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Focus\\n\\nVisual design should support learning, not distract from it.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Scalability\\n\\nComponents should support growth from MVP to millions of students.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Accessibility\\n\\nDesign should support different learning environments and user needs.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Visual Identity Direction\\n\\nThe visual identity should communicate:\\n\\n- Intelligence.\\n- Trust.\\n- Growth.\\n- Calmness.\\n- Academic confidence.\\n\\nThe application should feel:\\n\\n- Modern.\\n- Professional.\\n- Friendly.\\n- Reliable.\\n\\nIt should avoid feeling:\\n\\n- Like a game platform.\\n- Like a social media application.\\n- Like a generic AI tool.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Design Language\\n\\nThe design language is based on five concepts.\\n\\n## Knowledge\\n\\nRepresenting learning and understanding.\\n\\n## Growth\\n\\nRepresenting progress over time.\\n\\n## Connection\\n\\nRepresenting relationships between concepts.\\n\\n## Guidance\\n\\nRepresenting BLIE support.\\n\\n## Achievement\\n\\nRepresenting meaningful academic milestones.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Layout System\\n\\nThe application uses a structured layout system.\\n\\nPrinciples:\\n\\n- Clear hierarchy.\\n- Consistent spacing.\\n- Comfortable reading areas.\\n- Minimal visual noise.\\n\\nLayouts shall support:\\n\\n- Mobile-first experience.\\n- Different screen sizes.\\n- Accessibility requirements.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Typography System\\n\\nTypography shall prioritise readability.\\n\\nRequirements:\\n\\n- Clear text hierarchy.\\n- Comfortable reading size.\\n- Strong contrast.\\n- Consistent usage.\\n\\nTypography levels include:\\n\\n## Display\\n\\nUsed for major learning milestones.\\n\\n## Heading\\n\\nUsed for sections and navigation.\\n\\n## Body\\n\\nUsed for explanations and learning content.\\n\\n## Supporting Text\\n\\nUsed for metadata and secondary information.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Colour Philosophy\\n\\nColours should communicate meaning.\\n\\nThe colour system shall support:\\n\\n## Primary Identity\\n\\nRepresents trust and intelligence.\\n\\n## Learning States\\n\\nRepresents progress and understanding.\\n\\n## Information States\\n\\nRepresents system communication.\\n\\n## Status States\\n\\nRepresents:\\n\\n- Success.\\n- Warning.\\n- Error.\\n- Offline.\\n\\nColours should support comprehension rather than decoration.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Spacing System\\n\\nA consistent spacing system ensures visual harmony.\\n\\nSpacing shall support:\\n\\n- Touch accessibility.\\n- Reading comfort.\\n- Clear grouping.\\n- Component consistency.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Component Architecture\\n\\nComponents are reusable building blocks.\\n\\nMajor categories include:\\n\\n## Navigation Components\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Bottom navigation.\\n- Top navigation.\\n- Tabs.\\n- Breadcrumbs.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Content Components\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Cards.\\n- Lists.\\n- Sections.\\n- Containers.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning Components\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Subject cards.\\n- Topic cards.\\n- Progress indicators.\\n- Knowledge nodes.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## AI Components\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- BLIE response cards.\\n- AI suggestions.\\n- Learning prompts.\\n- Explanation panels.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Data Components\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Charts.\\n- Progress views.\\n- Analytics cards.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Core UI Components\\n\\nThe initial component library includes:\\n\\n## Buttons\\n\\nUsed for:\\n\\n- Actions.\\n- Confirmation.\\n- Navigation.\\n\\nRequirements:\\n\\n- Clear hierarchy.\\n- Accessible touch targets.\\n- Consistent behaviour.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Cards\\n\\nUsed to present:\\n\\n- Subjects.\\n- Topics.\\n- Learning progress.\\n- Recommendations.\\n\\nCards should provide quick understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Input Components\\n\\nUsed for:\\n\\n- Search.\\n- Questions.\\n- Settings.\\n- Student information.\\n\\nInputs must provide clear feedback.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Dialog Components\\n\\nUsed for:\\n\\n- Confirmation.\\n- Important information.\\n- User decisions.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Learning-Specific Components\\n\\nAI Study Buddy requires components designed specifically for education.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Subject Card\\n\\nDisplays:\\n\\n- Subject name.\\n- Progress.\\n- Current topics.\\n- Learning status.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Topic Card\\n\\nDisplays:\\n\\n- Concept.\\n- Relationship.\\n- Learning state.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Progress Component\\n\\nRepresents:\\n\\n- Completion.\\n- Understanding.\\n- Mastery.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Knowledge Graph Component\\n\\nRepresents:\\n\\n- Concepts.\\n- Relationships.\\n- Knowledge growth.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. BLIE Component System\\n\\nBLIE requires a unique interface language.\\n\\nComponents include:\\n\\n## AI Message Card\\n\\nFor explanations and guidance.\\n\\n## Learning Recommendation Card\\n\\nFor suggested actions.\\n\\n## Knowledge Connection Card\\n\\nFor linking concepts.\\n\\n## Study Action Card\\n\\nFor recommended learning activities.\\n\\nThe AI interface should feel educational and structured.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. State Design\\n\\nEvery component shall define states.\\n\\nRequired states:\\n\\n## Default\\n\\nNormal appearance.\\n\\n## Loading\\n\\nProcessing state.\\n\\n## Empty\\n\\nNo available information.\\n\\n## Error\\n\\nProblem state.\\n\\n## Offline\\n\\nLimited connectivity state.\\n\\n## Completed\\n\\nSuccessful learning state.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Motion Principles\\n\\nMotion should communicate:\\n\\n- Progress.\\n- Change.\\n- Feedback.\\n\\nMotion should never distract from learning.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\nAppropriate:\\n\\n- Smooth navigation.\\n- Progress animation.\\n- AI response appearance.\\n\\nAvoid:\\n\\n- Excessive effects.\\n- Attention-seeking animation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Accessibility Standards\\n\\nThe Design System shall support:\\n\\n- Readable typography.\\n- Sufficient contrast.\\n- Clear interaction targets.\\n- Screen accessibility.\\n- Consistent navigation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Component Governance\\n\\nAll future components shall:\\n\\n- Follow the Design System.\\n- Have documented behaviour.\\n- Support accessibility.\\n- Avoid unnecessary duplication.\\n\\nThe component library remains a controlled platform asset.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. Figma Implementation Structure\\n\\nThe Design System shall be organised in Figma as:\\n\\n## Foundation\\n\\n- Colours.\\n- Typography.\\n- Spacing.\\n- Icons.\\n\\n## Components\\n\\n- Buttons.\\n- Cards.\\n- Navigation.\\n- Forms.\\n\\n## Patterns\\n\\n- Dashboard sections.\\n- Learning modules.\\n- AI interactions.\\n\\n## Screens\\n\\nComplete application flows.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 18. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe Design System establishes the visual foundation of AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nAll future UI implementation shall:\\n\\n1. Follow a consistent design language.\\n2. Prioritise learning clarity.\\n3. Use reusable components.\\n4. Support scalability.\\n5. Maintain accessibility.\\n6. Present BLIE and PLKG experiences consistently.\\n\\nDetailed screen specifications will be defined in subsequent Volume H documents.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume H1**\\n:::\\n\\nAlhamdulillah.\\n\\n**H1 is complete.**\\n\\nThe next document is:\\n\\n**Volume H2 – Information Architecture \u0026 Navigation**\\n\\nThis will define:\\n- App structure\\n- Navigation model\\n- User journeys\\n- Screen relationships\\n- How students move from semester setup → subjects → BLIE → PLKG → revision → graduation journey.\",{},{\"_305\":1032,\"_312\":1054,\"_35\":1055,\"_316\":1056,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":1057,\"_325\":326},\"576edd90-bf35-4b9b-9001-3fdc8fd4bd8b\",[1016],{\"_370\":371,\"_323\":1058},1783670935.8864949,{\"_365\":426,\"_427\":428},{\"_360\":497,\"_381\":26},{},{\"_305\":1052,\"_312\":1062,\"_35\":1063,\"_37\":1064,\"_316\":1065,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":1066,\"_325\":326},\"3607fc9a-b9f3-460c-b451-5a52f58bc765\",[1032],{\"_370\":474,\"_323\":1074},1783670935.496532,1783670947.155492,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":1072},{\"_350\":494,\"_52\":494,\"_442\":14,\"_334\":1067,\"_339\":1068,\"_519\":1069,\"_521\":1070,\"_523\":14,\"_524\":14,\"_525\":14,\"_526\":14,\"_527\":14,\"_528\":1071,\"_343\":1044,\"_469\":-5,\"_347\":1045,\"_349\":1045,\"_338\":488,\"_360\":497,\"_353\":14},[],[],[],[],{},[1073],\"Start H1. It defines the design philosophy and principles that every future screen, component, and interaction must follow.\\n\\nThis document does not define colours, components, or screen layouts yet. Those belong to **H1 – Design System \u0026 Component Library Foundation**.\\n\\nH0 answers:\\n\\n**\\\"What kind of experience should AI Study Buddy create for a student?\\\"**\\n\\n---\\n\\n:::writing{variant=\\\"document\\\" id=\\\"86421\\\"}\\n# AI Study Buddy\\n\\n# Volume H0 – UX Philosophy \u0026 Student Experience Principles\\n\\n**Version:** 1.0 (Architecture Freeze)\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 1. Introduction\\n\\nThe UX Philosophy defines the foundation of the AI Study Buddy user experience.\\n\\nAI Study Buddy is designed as a personal educational companion that accompanies a student throughout their university journey — from the first semester until graduation.\\n\\nThe application is not designed as:\\n\\n- A simple AI chatbot.\\n- A digital note storage system.\\n- A replacement for lecturers.\\n- A social media learning platform.\\n\\nIt is designed as:\\n\\n**A living learning companion that helps students understand, organise, remember, and grow their knowledge.**\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Core UX Vision\\n\\nThe core UX vision is:\\n\\n\u003e \\\"Every student should have a personal learning companion that understands their academic journey and helps them become a better learner.\\\"\\n\\nThe application should make students feel:\\n\\n- Supported.\\n- Guided.\\n- Confident.\\n- Organised.\\n- Motivated.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Student-Centred Design Principle\\n\\nThe student is the centre of the experience.\\n\\nEvery feature must answer:\\n\\n\\\"How does this help the student learn better?\\\"\\n\\nThe interface should prioritise:\\n\\n- Understanding over information overload.\\n- Progress over activity tracking.\\n- Mastery over completion.\\n- Confidence over anxiety.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. AI Companion Philosophy\\n\\nBLIE represents the intelligence of the application.\\n\\nThe UX should make BLIE feel like:\\n\\n- A patient tutor.\\n- A study partner.\\n- A knowledgeable guide.\\n- A learning coach.\\n\\nBLIE should not feel like:\\n\\n- A search engine.\\n- A robotic assistant.\\n- A generic question-answer system.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Learning Journey Principle\\n\\nThe experience follows the student's academic lifecycle.\\n\\n## Before Learning\\n\\nHelp students prepare.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Understand upcoming topics.\\n- Review prerequisites.\\n- Build background knowledge.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## During Learning\\n\\nHelp students understand.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Explain concepts.\\n- Connect ideas.\\n- Clarify confusion.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## After Learning\\n\\nHelp students remember.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Revision.\\n- Practice.\\n- Knowledge reinforcement.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Before Assessment\\n\\nHelp students prepare confidently.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Identify gaps.\\n- Review important concepts.\\n- Practice understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Progressive Intelligence Principle\\n\\nAI Study Buddy should become more valuable over time.\\n\\nAt the beginning:\\n\\nThe application understands the student's academic profile.\\n\\nAs learning progresses:\\n\\nThe application understands:\\n\\n- Subjects.\\n- Learning habits.\\n- Knowledge strengths.\\n- Knowledge gaps.\\n- Academic journey.\\n\\nThe student's PLKG becomes the foundation of increasingly personalised assistance.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Knowledge Growth Experience\\n\\nThe student's knowledge growth should be visible.\\n\\nThe application should help students recognise:\\n\\n- What they know.\\n- What they are learning.\\n- What they need to improve.\\n\\nThe PLKG represents progress, not complexity.\\n\\nThe purpose is to build confidence and awareness.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Simplicity Principle\\n\\nUniversity learning is already complex.\\n\\nThe application should reduce complexity.\\n\\nThe UX should:\\n\\n- Present relevant information.\\n- Avoid unnecessary decisions.\\n- Guide the next action.\\n- Reduce cognitive burden.\\n\\nStudents should not need to learn how to use the application.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Trust Principle\\n\\nStudents must trust AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nTrust is built through:\\n\\n- Clear explanations.\\n- Transparent knowledge sources.\\n- Consistent behaviour.\\n- Respect for privacy.\\n- Honest limitations.\\n\\nThe application should never create false confidence.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Personal Ownership Principle\\n\\nEvery student's learning environment is personal.\\n\\nThe experience shall respect:\\n\\n- Personal learning pace.\\n- Personal knowledge graph.\\n- Personal study history.\\n- Personal learning preferences.\\n\\nThe application supports the student's journey; it does not control it.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Motivation Philosophy\\n\\nMotivation should come from meaningful progress.\\n\\nThe application encourages students through:\\n\\n- Visible improvement.\\n- Knowledge growth.\\n- Learning milestones.\\n- Achievement recognition.\\n\\nThe goal is not maximum screen time.\\n\\nThe goal is successful learning.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Emotional Design Principles\\n\\nThe application should create positive learning emotions.\\n\\nStudents should feel:\\n\\n## Clarity\\n\\n\\\"I understand what I need to do.\\\"\\n\\n## Confidence\\n\\n\\\"I am improving.\\\"\\n\\n## Curiosity\\n\\n\\\"I want to explore more.\\\"\\n\\n## Achievement\\n\\n\\\"I can see my progress.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Interaction Principles\\n\\nEvery interaction should be:\\n\\n## Clear\\n\\nThe student understands what is happening.\\n\\n## Helpful\\n\\nThe interaction provides learning value.\\n\\n## Predictable\\n\\nThe application behaves consistently.\\n\\n## Respectful\\n\\nThe student remains in control.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Accessibility Principle\\n\\nLearning should be available to all students.\\n\\nThe experience shall consider:\\n\\n- Readability.\\n- Navigation clarity.\\n- Visual accessibility.\\n- Interaction simplicity.\\n\\nAccessibility is part of quality, not an optional feature.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Long-Term Relationship Principle\\n\\nAI Study Buddy is designed for a multi-year relationship.\\n\\nThe experience should support:\\n\\nSemester 1\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSemester 2\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAdvanced Subjects\\n\\n↓\\n\\nFinal Year Projects\\n\\n↓\\n\\nGraduation\\n\\nThe application becomes more valuable as the student's knowledge history grows.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. UX Success Definition\\n\\nThe UX is successful when students feel:\\n\\n\\\"I have a companion who understands my learning journey and helps me become better every semester.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe UX Philosophy establishes the foundation for all future UI/UX design decisions.\\n\\nAll future screens, components, and interactions shall follow these principles:\\n\\n1. Student-first experience.\\n2. Learning-focused design.\\n3. BLIE as an educational companion.\\n4. PLKG as the student's knowledge foundation.\\n5. Simplicity over complexity.\\n6. Motivation through meaningful progress.\\n7. Trust, privacy, and transparency.\\n\\nDetailed visual design and interface specifications will be defined in subsequent Volume H documents.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume H0**\\n:::\\n\\nAlhamdulillah.\\n\\n**H0 is complete.**\\n\\nNext:\\n\\n**Volume H1 – Design System \u0026 Component Library Foundation**\\n\\nThis will define the visual language:\\n- Design tokens\\n- Typography\\n- Colour philosophy\\n- Layout system\\n- Cards\\n- Buttons\\n- Navigation patterns\\n- AI-specific UI components\\n- Learning progress components\\n\\nThis will become the foundation before we design individual screens.\",{},{\"_305\":1076,\"_312\":1098,\"_35\":1099,\"_316\":1100,\"_318\":319,\"_320\":26,\"_321\":436,\"_323\":1101,\"_325\":326},\"85d7d2ef-7a4a-464c-aab8-53b54983f3d4\",[1060],{\"_370\":444,\"_323\":1105},1783669300.6839557,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":1104},{\"_438\":26,\"_343\":1088,\"_345\":346,\"_347\":1089,\"_349\":1089,\"_350\":488,\"_52\":494,\"_495\":1102,\"_354\":1103,\"_360\":497,\"_442\":26,\"_353\":14},[498],\"2e9ff7ea-a003-4643-a517-8dee37b5c8a0\",[428],{},{\"_305\":1096,\"_312\":1109,\"_35\":1110,\"_37\":1111,\"_316\":1112,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":1113,\"_325\":326},\"bf2eb763-ad5d-4e09-a75d-e9d0b9e1d60b\",[1076],{\"_370\":474,\"_323\":1121},1783669300.351341,1783669309.357876,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":1119},{\"_350\":494,\"_52\":494,\"_442\":14,\"_334\":1114,\"_339\":1115,\"_519\":1116,\"_521\":1117,\"_523\":14,\"_524\":14,\"_525\":14,\"_526\":14,\"_527\":14,\"_528\":1118,\"_343\":1088,\"_469\":-5,\"_347\":1089,\"_349\":1089,\"_338\":488,\"_360\":497,\"_353\":14},[],[],[],[],{},[1120],\"Start H0.
