MVP Delivery Principles\\n\\nImplementation follows these principles.\\n\\n## Foundation First\\n\\nCore platform capabilities shall be completed before advanced features.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Vertical Delivery\\n\\nEach capability shall be implemented from frontend through backend to deployment before beginning the next capability.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Quality Before Expansion\\n\\nPlatform stability is prioritised over feature quantity.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Student Validation\\n\\nReal student feedback guides future improvements after MVP release.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Introduction\\n\\nThe Deployment Roadmap defines the implementation strategy for delivering AI Study Buddy from development to production.\\n\\nThe roadmap establishes a structured deployment process that prioritises stability, security, quality, and continuous improvement while remaining aligned with the approved architecture.\\n\\nDeployment is treated as a controlled engineering activity rather than a single release event.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Objectives\\n\\nThe deployment strategy shall:\\n\\n- Deliver stable software releases.\\n- Protect production data.\\n- Minimise deployment risk.\\n- Support continuous improvement.\\n- Ensure service availability.\\n- Provide a reliable experience for students.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Deployment Principles\\n\\nDeployment follows these principles.\\n\\n## Incremental\\n\\nSmall, controlled releases are preferred over large deployments.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Repeatable\\n\\nEvery deployment follows the same documented process.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Automated\\n\\nDeployment activities shall be automated wherever practical.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Recoverable\\n\\nEvery deployment shall support rollback procedures when necessary.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Verified\\n\\nDeployment is completed only after successful validation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Deployment Environments\\n\\nThe platform uses four deployment environments.\\n\\n## Development\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nActive engineering and feature implementation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Testing\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nIntegration testing and quality assurance.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Staging\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nFinal validation before production release.\\n\\nStaging shall closely mirror the production environment.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Production\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nServe active student users.\\n\\nProduction remains the authoritative operational environment.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Deployment Workflow\\n\\nEvery deployment follows the approved sequence.\\n\\nDevelopment\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCode Review\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAutomated Testing\\n\\n↓\\n\\nTesting Environment\\n\\n↓\\n\\nStaging Validation\\n\\n↓\\n\\nProduction Deployment\\n\\n↓\\n\\nOperational Monitoring\\n\\n↓\\n\\nStudent Feedback\\n\\nThis workflow applies to every production release.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Release Validation\\n\\nBefore deployment, every release shall satisfy:\\n\\n- Functional verification.\\n- Integration verification.\\n- Security validation.\\n- Performance validation.\\n- Documentation review.\\n- Architecture compliance.\\n\\nOnly validated releases proceed to production.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Database Deployment\\n\\nDatabase deployment follows controlled migration procedures.\\n\\nRequirements include:\\n\\n- Version-controlled migrations.\\n- Data integrity verification.\\n- Backup before migration.\\n- Migration validation.\\n- Rollback planning.\\n\\nStudent data shall be preserved throughout deployment.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Mobile Application Release\\n\\nMobile application releases shall include:\\n\\n- Build verification.\\n- Functional validation.\\n- Offline verification.\\n- Synchronization validation.\\n- Compatibility testing.\\n\\nOnly approved builds are released to students.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Backend Deployment\\n\\nBackend deployment includes:\\n\\n- Service validation.\\n- API verification.\\n- Security validation.\\n- BLIE integration verification.\\n- Monitoring activation.\\n\\nBusiness services remain available throughout deployment whenever practical.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Operational Monitoring\\n\\nFollowing deployment, operational monitoring verifies:\\n\\n- Service availability.\\n- API performance.\\n- BLIE operation.\\n- Synchronization health.\\n- Error reporting.\\n- Infrastructure status.\\n\\nOperational monitoring continues throughout the platform lifecycle.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Incident Management\\n\\nOperational incidents shall follow a structured response process.\\n\\nIncident\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAssessment\\n\\n↓\\n\\nContainment\\n\\n↓\\n\\nResolution\\n\\n↓\\n\\nVerification\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPost-Incident Review\\n\\nThe objective is rapid recovery while protecting student learning.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Rollback Strategy\\n\\nIf a deployment introduces unacceptable risk:\\n\\n- Deployment is halted.\\n- Previous stable version is restored.\\n- Student data integrity is verified.\\n- Root cause analysis is performed.\\n\\nRollback procedures shall be documented before every production release.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Release Documentation\\n\\nEvery deployment shall include updated:\\n\\n- Release notes.\\n- Technical documentation.\\n- API documentation.\\n- Operational procedures.\\n- Migration records.\\n\\nDocumentation forms part of the release deliverable.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Success Criteria\\n\\nA deployment is considered successful when:\\n\\n- Platform services operate normally.\\n- Student data remains consistent.\\n- BLIE functions correctly.\\n- Synchronization operates successfully.\\n- Monitoring confirms platform health.\\n- No critical production issues are identified.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Continuous Improvement\\n\\nFollowing each production deployment:\\n\\n- Operational metrics are reviewed.\\n- Student feedback is evaluated.\\n- Engineering observations are documented.\\n- Future improvements are prioritised.\\n\\nDeployment supports continuous platform evolution.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe Deployment Roadmap establishes the deployment strategy for AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThe platform shall:\\n\\n1. Progress through defined deployment environments.\\n2. Validate every release before production.\\n3. Protect student data during deployment.\\n4. Monitor operational health continuously.\\n5. Maintain documented rollback procedures.\\n6. Improve through structured release cycles.\\n\\nDeployment shall remain fully aligned with the Engineering Constitution and the approved implementation architecture.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Implementation Notes (Not Part of Current Architecture)\\n\\nFuture deployment tooling, automation, and operational practices may evolve provided they remain consistent with the deployment principles established in this document.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume G12**\\n:::\\n\\nAlhamdulillah.\\n\\nWith **G12 completed**, there is now **only one remaining document** in the Volume G series:\\n\\n- **G13 – MVP Delivery Roadmap**\\n\\nCompleting G13 will conclude the entire **Volume G – Implementation Blueprint**, which in turn completes the **A–G Architecture Blueprint** for AI Study Buddy. Introduction\\n\\nThe Testing Strategy defines the quality assurance approach for AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThe objective of this document is to ensure that every component of the platform operates reliably, securely, and consistently throughout the student's academic journey.\\n\\nTesting is an integral part of engineering and shall be performed throughout development rather than only before release.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Objectives\\n\\nThe testing strategy shall:\\n\\n- Verify functional correctness.\\n- Protect student data.\\n- Ensure platform reliability.\\n- Validate BLIE behaviour.\\n- Maintain synchronization integrity.\\n- Support continuous improvement.\\n\\nTesting shall verify that implementation remains consistent with the approved architecture.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Testing Principles\\n\\nTesting follows these principles.\\n\\n## Continuous\\n\\nTesting occurs throughout development.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Automated\\n\\nAutomated testing is preferred wherever practical.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Repeatable\\n\\nTests shall produce consistent and reproducible results.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Independent\\n\\nEach test validates a clearly defined behaviour.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Architecture-Driven\\n\\nTests verify implementation against the approved architecture.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Testing Scope\\n\\nTesting covers:\\n\\n- Mobile Application.\\n- Backend Services.\\n- BLIE.\\n- PLKG.\\n- Document Intelligence.\\n- Synchronization.\\n- APIs.\\n- Security.\\n- Performance.\\n\\nEvery major platform component shall be tested.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Unit Testing\\n\\nUnit testing validates individual software components.\\n\\nExamples include:\\n\\n- Business logic.\\n- Validation rules.\\n- Utility functions.\\n- Data processing.\\n- BLIE processing components.\\n\\nUnit tests shall execute independently.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Integration Testing\\n\\nIntegration testing verifies interaction between components.\\n\\nExamples include:\\n\\n- Mobile and backend communication.\\n- Backend and database interaction.\\n- BLIE and PLKG integration.\\n- Document Intelligence and PLKG updates.\\n- Synchronization workflows.\\n\\nIntegration testing ensures components operate together correctly.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. End-to-End Testing\\n\\nEnd-to-End testing validates complete student workflows.\\n\\nExamples include:\\n\\n- Student registration.\\n- Subject enrolment.\\n- Document upload.\\n- BLIE learning session.\\n- Study preparation.\\n- Revision workflow.\\n- Semester progression.\\n\\nTesting reflects real student usage.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. BLIE Validation\\n\\nBLIE testing verifies:\\n\\n- Intent analysis.\\n- Context assembly.\\n- Knowledge retrieval.\\n- Curriculum alignment.\\n- Memory integration.\\n- Response generation.\\n- Response validation.\\n\\nTesting confirms BLIE behaves consistently with the approved architecture.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. PLKG Validation\\n\\nPLKG testing verifies:\\n\\n- Graph construction.\\n- Knowledge updates.\\n- Relationship integrity.\\n- Synchronization.\\n- Learning progression.\\n\\nGraph consistency shall be maintained throughout testing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Document Intelligence Testing\\n\\nTesting verifies:\\n\\n- File processing.\\n- Text extraction.\\n- Educational content analysis.\\n- Knowledge structuring.\\n- PLKG enrichment.\\n\\nProcessing failures shall not compromise student knowledge.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Synchronization Testing\\n\\nSynchronization testing verifies:\\n\\n- Offline learning.\\n- Local updates.\\n- Cloud synchronization.\\n- Conflict handling.\\n- Recovery after connection loss.\\n\\nTesting confirms learning continuity across connectivity changes.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Security Testing\\n\\nSecurity validation includes:\\n\\n- Authentication.\\n- Authorization.\\n- Access control.\\n- Input validation.\\n- Secure communication.\\n- Data protection.\\n\\nStudent privacy remains a mandatory requirement.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Performance Testing\\n\\nPerformance testing verifies:\\n\\n- Application responsiveness.\\n- API response times.\\n- BLIE processing.\\n- Document processing.\\n- Synchronization performance.\\n- System stability under load.\\n\\nPerformance shall remain acceptable as the platform scales.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Regression Testing\\n\\nRegression testing ensures that:\\n\\n- Existing functionality remains operational.\\n- Architecture remains consistent.\\n- Previously resolved issues do not reappear.\\n\\nRegression testing forms part of every release.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. User Acceptance Testing\\n\\nUser Acceptance Testing confirms that implemented features support real student learning.\\n\\nValidation includes:\\n\\n- Learning workflows.\\n- User experience.\\n- Educational usefulness.\\n- Functional completeness.\\n\\nStudent feedback supports continuous refinement.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Release Readiness\\n\\nA release is ready when:\\n\\n- Functional testing passes.\\n- Integration testing passes.\\n- End-to-End testing passes.\\n- Security validation is complete.\\n- Performance requirements are met.\\n- Documentation is updated.\\n\\nQuality requirements are mandatory for every release.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe Testing Strategy establishes the quality assurance framework for AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThe platform shall:\\n\\n1. Verify every major platform component.\\n2. Test throughout the development lifecycle.\\n3. Validate BLIE and PLKG behaviour.\\n4. Protect student privacy and data integrity.\\n5. Ensure synchronization reliability.\\n6. Confirm implementation remains consistent with the approved architecture.\\n\\nTesting shall be treated as an essential engineering activity rather than a final development phase.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Implementation Notes (Not Part of Current Architecture)\\n\\nFuture testing tools, automation frameworks, or quality processes may evolve without altering the testing principles established in this document.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume G11**\\n:::\\n\\nAlhamdulillah.\\n\\nWith **G11 complete**, only **two documents remain** to finish the entire **Volume G – Implementation Blueprint**:\\n\\n- **G12 – Deployment Roadmap**\\n- **G13 – MVP Delivery Roadmap**\\n\\nOnce these are completed, the complete **A–G Architecture Blueprint** for AI Study Buddy will be finished, providing a comprehensive foundation before we begin the detailed **Volume H UI/UX Design Specification**. memcite\",{},{\"_305\":1288,\"_312\":1309,\"_35\":1310,\"_316\":1311,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":1312,\"_325\":326},\"1a893fc2-e167-44f3-8b9d-ac95832d1ebd\",[1272],{\"_370\":371,\"_323\":1313},1783667155.1958559,{\"_365\":426,\"_427\":428},{\"_360\":497,\"_381\":26},{},{\"_305\":1307,\"_312\":1317,\"_35\":1318,\"_37\":1319,\"_316\":1320,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":1321,\"_325\":326},\"e5dd69c4-bc1d-48a5-b2f6-9ff66d641ce3\",[1288],{\"_370\":474,\"_323\":1329},1783667154.697364,1783667167.286714,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":1327},{\"_350\":494,\"_52\":494,\"_442\":14,\"_334\":1322,\"_339\":1323,\"_519\":1324,\"_521\":1325,\"_523\":14,\"_524\":14,\"_525\":14,\"_526\":14,\"_527\":14,\"_528\":1326,\"_343\":1300,\"_469\":-5,\"_347\":1301,\"_349\":1301,\"_338\":1134,\"_360\":497,\"_353\":14},[],[],[],[],{},[1328],\"Proceed G11 – Testing Strategy. It establishes the user experience philosophy, navigation, and screen architecture. The detailed screen specifications, wireframes, components, and interaction behaviours will be documented later in **Volume H**.\\n\\n---\\n\\n:::writing{variant=\\\"document\\\" id=\\\"29461\\\"}\\n# AI Study Buddy\\n\\n# Volume G10 – UI/UX Build Specification\\n\\n**Version:** 1.0 (Architecture Freeze)\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 1. Introduction\\n\\nThe UI/UX Build Specification defines the user experience architecture of AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThe purpose of this document is to ensure every interface, workflow, and interaction supports the platform's primary mission:\\n\\n**Helping university students learn effectively from their first semester until graduation.**\\n\\nThe application is not designed to become another social platform or AI chatbot.\\n\\nIt is designed to become a trusted academic companion.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Design Philosophy\\n\\nThe user experience shall be guided by the following principles.\\n\\n## Student First\\n\\nEvery screen exists to improve learning.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning Before Features\\n\\nTechnology shall never distract from studying.\\n\\nEvery interaction should reduce learning friction.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Calm Intelligence\\n\\nBLIE should feel supportive, knowledgeable and dependable.\\n\\nThe interface should never overwhelm students.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Progressive Learning\\n\\nThe application grows together with the student's academic journey.\\n\\nComplexity increases only when needed.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Consistency\\n\\nNavigation, layouts and interactions remain predictable throughout the application.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. User Experience Goals\\n\\nThe application shall enable students to:\\n\\n- Organise their studies.\\n- Understand difficult concepts.\\n- Prepare before lectures.\\n- Revise efficiently.\\n- Build long-term knowledge.\\n- Track learning progress.\\n- Graduate with confidence.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Information Architecture\\n\\nThe application is organised around the student's learning journey.\\n\\nPrimary areas include:\\n\\n- Dashboard\\n- Subjects\\n- BLIE\\n- Documents\\n- Study Groups\\n- Profile\\n\\nEvery feature belongs within one of these primary areas.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Navigation Architecture\\n\\nNavigation shall remain simple and consistent.\\n\\nStudents should always know:\\n\\n- Where they are.\\n- What they are studying.\\n- What they should do next.\\n\\nThe navigation hierarchy supports both new and experienced students.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Student Journey\\n\\nThe experience follows the student's academic lifecycle.\\n\\nRegistration\\n\\n↓\\n\\nProgramme Setup\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSemester Setup\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSubject Enrolment\\n\\n↓\\n\\nStudy Preparation\\n\\n↓\\n\\nLecture Learning\\n\\n↓\\n\\nRevision\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAssessment\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSemester Completion\\n\\n↓\\n\\nNext Semester\\n\\n↓\\n\\nGraduation\\n\\nThe interface evolves naturally throughout this journey.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Dashboard Experience\\n\\nThe Dashboard serves as the student's learning home.\\n\\nIt provides:\\n\\n- Current semester overview.\\n- Today's study priorities.\\n- Subject progress.\\n- Learning reminders.\\n- Recent activities.\\n- BLIE recommendations.\\n\\nThe Dashboard helps students understand their current learning status at a glance.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Subject Experience\\n\\nEach subject functions as an independent learning workspace.\\n\\nStudents can:\\n\\n- View learning materials.\\n- Access lecture notes.\\n- Study with BLIE.\\n- Review learning progress.\\n- Prepare for upcoming topics.\\n\\nSubjects remain the centre of daily learning activities.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. BLIE Experience\\n\\nBLIE is presented as a learning companion rather than a generic AI assistant.\\n\\nBLIE shall:\\n\\n- Explain concepts.\\n- Guide learning.\\n- Encourage understanding.\\n- Recommend prerequisite topics.\\n- Support revision.\\n\\nInteractions remain educational, contextual and personalised.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Personal Learning Knowledge Graph Experience\\n\\nStudents can observe the growth of their learning knowledge through the PLKG.\\n\\nThe PLKG experience should help students:\\n\\n- Understand topic relationships.\\n- Identify learning gaps.\\n- Observe academic progress.\\n- Build confidence through visible knowledge growth.\\n\\nThe graph exists to support understanding rather than visual complexity.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Document Experience\\n\\nLearning materials are organised within each subject.\\n\\nStudents may:\\n\\n- Upload learning resources.\\n- View processing status.\\n- Search documents.\\n- Access extracted knowledge.\\n\\nDocument management remains simple and focused on learning.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Study Group Experience\\n\\nStudy Groups support collaborative learning.\\n\\nStudents may:\\n\\n- Join approved groups.\\n- Share learning resources.\\n- Participate in discussions.\\n- Learn collaboratively.\\n\\nPersonal learning remains independent while approved shared resources enhance collective understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Learning Motivation\\n\\nThe application encourages consistent learning through meaningful academic progress.\\n\\nExamples include:\\n\\n- Completing study plans.\\n- Building subject mastery.\\n- Maintaining study consistency.\\n- Completing semester goals.\\n- Growing the Personal Learning Knowledge Graph.\\n\\nRecognition reflects genuine learning achievements rather than application usage.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Interaction Principles\\n\\nEvery interaction shall be:\\n\\n- Clear.\\n- Predictable.\\n- Responsive.\\n- Accessible.\\n- Educational.\\n\\nThe interface should reduce unnecessary cognitive effort.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Visual Design Principles\\n\\nThe visual language shall emphasise:\\n\\n- Simplicity.\\n- Readability.\\n- Consistency.\\n- Accessibility.\\n- Educational focus.\\n\\nVisual elements support comprehension rather than decoration.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Feedback Principles\\n\\nThe application shall provide timely feedback for:\\n\\n- User actions.\\n- Background processing.\\n- Synchronization.\\n- Learning progress.\\n- BLIE interactions.\\n\\nStudents should always understand the current state of the application.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. Offline Experience\\n\\nOffline operation shall remain consistent with the approved synchronization architecture.\\n\\nStudents should clearly understand:\\n\\n- Available offline resources.\\n- Pending synchronization.\\n- Completed synchronization.\\n\\nOffline learning shall remain uninterrupted whenever possible.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 18. Accessibility\\n\\nThe interface shall support:\\n\\n- Clear typography.\\n- Consistent navigation.\\n- Readable layouts.\\n- Accessible interactions.\\n\\nAccessibility shall be considered throughout implementation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 19. Screen Inventory\\n\\nThe initial implementation includes:\\n\\n- Splash Screen\\n- Onboarding\\n- Authentication\\n- Programme Setup\\n- Semester Setup\\n- Dashboard\\n- Subject Workspace\\n- BLIE\\n- Documents\\n- Study Preparation\\n- Revision\\n- Assessments\\n- Study Groups\\n- Profile\\n- Settings\\n\\nDetailed specifications for every screen are defined in Volume H.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 20. Design System\\n\\nThe complete Design System—including colours, typography, spacing, components, icons, animations, and reusable UI patterns—is specified in Volume H.\\n\\nThe implementation shall remain consistent with the approved Design System.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 21. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe UI/UX Build Specification establishes the user experience blueprint for AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThe application shall:\\n\\n1. Prioritise learning above all other interactions.\\n2. Present BLIE as a trusted academic companion.\\n3. Organise the interface around the student's learning journey.\\n4. Provide simple, consistent, and accessible navigation.\\n5. Support personalised learning through the PLKG.\\n6. Encourage meaningful academic progress.\\n7. Maintain a calm, focused, and educational experience.\\n\\nDetailed screen specifications, interaction behaviours, component libraries, and design assets are documented separately in the Volume H UI/UX Design Specification Series.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Implementation Notes (Not Part of Current Architecture)\\n\\nFuture refinements to the visual design or interaction details may be introduced through the Volume H Design Specification series, provided they remain consistent with the user experience principles established in this document.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume G10**\\n:::\\n\\nAlhamdulillah.\\n\\nI believe we have now established a clean separation:\\n\\n- **Volume G** defines **what** the implementation should be.\\n- **Volume H** will define **exactly how** every screen, component, and interaction is designed.\\n\\nThis keeps the architecture stable while allowing the design specification to evolve in detail without changing the core blueprint. memcite\",{},{\"_305\":1331,\"_312\":1352,\"_35\":1353,\"_37\":1354,\"_316\":1355,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":1356,\"_325\":326},\"3f5400cb-0468-409d-8867-e2f722d65c57\",[1315],{\"_370\":474,\"_323\":1364},1783658498.34099,1783658516.821923,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":1362},{\"_350\":494,\"_52\":494,\"_442\":14,\"_334\":1357,\"_339\":1358,\"_519\":1359,\"_521\":1360,\"_523\":14,\"_524\":14,\"_525\":14,\"_526\":14,\"_527\":14,\"_528\":1361,\"_343\":1343,\"_469\":-5,\"_347\":1344,\"_349\":1344,\"_338\":1134,\"_360\":497,\"_353\":14},[],[],[],[],{},[1363],\"Proceed G10 - Introduction\\n\\nThe API Specification defines the implementation standards for communication between the AI Study Buddy mobile application and backend services.\\n\\nThe APIs provide secure, consistent, and versioned access to all approved platform capabilities while maintaining the architectural principles established in Volumes F and G.\\n\\nThe backend remains the authoritative source of business logic.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Objectives\\n\\nThe API platform shall:\\n\\n- Provide secure communication.\\n- Support mobile application services.\\n- Enable BLIE interactions.\\n- Support synchronization.\\n- Maintain consistent request and response formats.\\n- Preserve backward compatibility where practical.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. API Principles\\n\\nImplementation follows these principles.\\n\\n## API-First\\n\\nEvery backend capability is exposed through documented APIs.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Stateless\\n\\nEach request contains the information required for processing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Secure\\n\\nProtected endpoints require authentication and authorization.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Versioned\\n\\nPublic APIs shall be versioned to support future platform evolution.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Consistent\\n\\nAll APIs shall use standardized request, response, and error structures.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. API Architecture\\n\\nCommunication follows the approved architecture.\\n\\nMobile Application\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAPI Gateway\\n\\n↓\\n\\nBackend Services\\n\\n↓\\n\\nBLIE\\n\\n↓\\n\\nDatabase \u0026 Storage\\n\\nClients communicate only with approved API endpoints.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Authentication APIs\\n\\nAuthentication services support:\\n\\n- Student registration.\\n- Student login.\\n- Session validation.\\n- Session termination.\\n- Profile retrieval.\\n\\nAuthentication follows the approved security architecture.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Student APIs\\n\\nStudent services provide access to:\\n\\n- Academic profile.\\n- Programme information.\\n- Subject enrolment.\\n- Learning history.\\n\\nStudents may access only their own information.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. BLIE APIs\\n\\nBLIE APIs support:\\n\\n- Learning questions.\\n- Concept explanations.\\n- Study guidance.\\n- Revision assistance.\\n- Personalized educational responses.\\n\\nBLIE requests are processed through the approved orchestration architecture.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. PLKG APIs\\n\\nPLKG services provide access to:\\n\\n- Personal knowledge structure.\\n- Learning progress.\\n- Knowledge relationships.\\n- Graph summaries.\\n\\nGraph modifications occur only through approved learning workflows.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Document APIs\\n\\nDocument services support:\\n\\n- Upload.\\n- Processing status.\\n- Learning resource management.\\n\\nKnowledge extraction occurs through background processing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Synchronization APIs\\n\\nSynchronization services support:\\n\\n- Uploading local changes.\\n- Downloading cloud updates.\\n- Conflict handling.\\n- Synchronization status.\\n\\nSynchronization follows the approved offline architecture.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Study Group APIs\\n\\nStudy Group services provide:\\n\\n- Group management.\\n- Shared learning resources.\\n- Membership management.\\n- Collaborative learning functions.\\n\\nAccess is controlled through approved authorization rules.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Assessment APIs\\n\\nAssessment services provide:\\n\\n- Learning assessments.\\n- Progress tracking.\\n- Learning analytics.\\n- Readiness information.\\n\\nAssessment processing follows the approved learning analytics architecture.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Notification APIs\\n\\nNotification services support:\\n\\n- Study reminders.\\n- Learning updates.\\n- Assessment notifications.\\n- Synchronization notifications.\\n\\nStudents manage notification preferences through approved settings.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Error Responses\\n\\nEvery API shall return consistent error information.\\n\\nResponses shall:\\n\\n- Identify the error.\\n- Indicate whether retry is appropriate.\\n- Avoid exposing internal implementation details.\\n\\nError handling remains consistent across all services.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Security\\n\\nEvery protected request follows:\\n\\nAuthentication\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAuthorization\\n\\n↓\\n\\nInput Validation\\n\\n↓\\n\\nBusiness Logic\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAudit Logging\\n\\nNo protected endpoint bypasses this sequence.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. API Documentation\\n\\nEvery public API shall include:\\n\\n- Endpoint definition.\\n- Request format.\\n- Response format.\\n- Authentication requirements.\\n- Validation rules.\\n- Error responses.\\n- Version information.\\n\\nDocumentation is maintained together with implementation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. Deployment Readiness\\n\\nAPI services are ready for deployment when:\\n\\n- Functional validation is complete.\\n- Security requirements are satisfied.\\n- Performance requirements are met.\\n- Documentation is current.\\n- Monitoring is operational.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 18. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe API Specification defines the implementation standards for all communication between AI Study Buddy clients and backend services.\\n\\nThe API platform shall:\\n\\n1. Maintain secure and versioned communication.\\n2. Expose approved platform capabilities through documented endpoints.\\n3. Keep business logic within backend services.\\n4. Support synchronization and BLIE interactions.\\n5. Maintain consistent request, response, and error formats.\\n6. Preserve compatibility with the approved architecture.\\n\\nImplementation shall remain fully aligned with the API \u0026 Backend Service Architecture defined in Volume F15.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Implementation Notes (Not Part of Current Architecture)\\n\\nFuture API enhancements may improve performance, documentation quality, or operational efficiency without altering the approved API architecture or Engineering Constitution.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume G9**\\n:::\\n\\nBismillah.\\n\\nWith **G9 completed**, only **four documents remain** to complete the entire **Volume G – Implementation Blueprint**:\\n\\n- **G10 – UI/UX Build Specification**\\n- **G11 – Testing Strategy**\\n- **G12 – Deployment Roadmap**\\n- **G13 – MVP Delivery Roadmap**\\n\\nThese final four documents will complete the implementation blueprint for AI Study Buddy while remaining fully consistent with the architecture that we have already locked. memcite\",{},{\"_305\":1442,\"_312\":1463,\"_35\":1464,\"_37\":1465,\"_316\":1466,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":1467,\"_325\":326},\"7b09c6b4-5718-4543-9105-056f72fca3eb\",[1426],{\"_370\":474,\"_323\":1475},1783658231.721051,1783658243.147356,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":1473},{\"_350\":494,\"_52\":494,\"_442\":14,\"_334\":1468,\"_339\":1469,\"_519\":1470,\"_521\":1471,\"_523\":14,\"_524\":14,\"_525\":14,\"_526\":14,\"_527\":14,\"_528\":1472,\"_343\":1454,\"_469\":-5,\"_347\":1455,\"_349\":1455,\"_338\":1134,\"_360\":497,\"_353\":14},[],[],[],[],{},[1474],\"Start G9. Introduction\\n\\nThe Document Intelligence Implementation Blueprint defines how AI Study Buddy processes student learning materials and transforms them into structured educational knowledge.\\n\\nThe implementation follows the approved Knowledge Processing \u0026 Document Intelligence Architecture and provides the mechanism by which uploaded learning resources enrich the student's Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG).\\n\\nThe objective is to convert learning materials into meaningful educational knowledge that supports personalized learning.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Objectives\\n\\nThe Document Intelligence implementation shall:\\n\\n- Process uploaded learning materials.\\n- Extract educational content.\\n- Identify academic concepts.\\n- Support PLKG enrichment.\\n- Provide structured knowledge for BLIE.\\n- Preserve the original learning resources.\\n\\nDocument Intelligence supports learning by understanding educational content rather than simply storing files.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Implementation Principles\\n\\nImplementation follows these principles.\\n\\n## Preserve Original Resources\\n\\nOriginal uploaded files remain unchanged.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Knowledge Before Storage\\n\\nEducational knowledge is extracted and structured before being integrated into the student's learning graph.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Student Ownership\\n\\nProcessed knowledge belongs to the student's personal learning environment.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Incremental Processing\\n\\nDocuments may be processed progressively without interrupting the student's learning experience.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Curriculum Awareness\\n\\nKnowledge extraction operates within the student's academic context whenever applicable.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Processing Workflow\\n\\nEvery uploaded learning resource follows the approved processing sequence.\\n\\nStudent Upload\\n\\n↓\\n\\nFile Validation\\n\\n↓\\n\\nText Extraction\\n\\n↓\\n\\nEducational Content Analysis\\n\\n↓\\n\\nConcept Identification\\n\\n↓\\n\\nKnowledge Structuring\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPLKG Enrichment\\n\\n↓\\n\\nBLIE Availability\\n\\nEach stage completes before the document becomes part of the student's learning knowledge.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. File Intake\\n\\nThe implementation accepts approved learning materials uploaded by students.\\n\\nExamples include:\\n\\n- Lecture notes.\\n- Course notes.\\n- Assignment materials.\\n- Study references.\\n- Presentation slides.\\n\\nUploaded files are securely stored before processing begins.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Text Extraction\\n\\nThe implementation extracts readable text from uploaded learning resources.\\n\\nWhere applicable, OCR is applied to image-based content.\\n\\nExtracted text becomes the foundation for educational analysis.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Educational Content Analysis\\n\\nThe extracted text is analysed to identify educational information relevant to the student's learning.\\n\\nThe analysis focuses on:\\n\\n- Academic concepts.\\n- Definitions.\\n- Explanatory content.\\n- Topic relationships.\\n- Learning structure.\\n\\nThe objective is to prepare information for structured knowledge processing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Concept Identification\\n\\nThe implementation identifies educational concepts that correspond with the student's learning journey.\\n\\nIdentified concepts are prepared for integration into the Personal Learning Knowledge Graph.\\n\\nDuplicate concepts are recognised and handled appropriately to maintain graph consistency.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Knowledge Structuring\\n\\nIdentified concepts are organised into structured knowledge suitable for the PLKG.\\n\\nThe implementation prepares:\\n\\n- Knowledge nodes.\\n- Knowledge relationships.\\n- Learning associations.\\n\\nThe resulting structure follows the approved PLKG architecture.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. PLKG Enrichment\\n\\nStructured knowledge is incorporated into the student's Personal Learning Knowledge Graph.\\n\\nEnrichment occurs only after successful validation.\\n\\nThe implementation preserves graph integrity throughout the update process.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. BLIE Integration\\n\\nAfter processing is complete, the newly structured knowledge becomes available to BLIE.\\n\\nBLIE may utilise the processed knowledge to:\\n\\n- Personalize explanations.\\n- Improve learning guidance.\\n- Support revision.\\n- Retrieve subject-specific knowledge.\\n\\nBLIE accesses structured knowledge rather than the raw uploaded document whenever appropriate.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Background Processing\\n\\nDocument Intelligence operates as an asynchronous background service.\\n\\nStudents may continue using the application while processing occurs.\\n\\nProcessing status is maintained until completion.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Error Handling\\n\\nThe implementation shall:\\n\\n- Detect unsupported files.\\n- Handle extraction failures.\\n- Recover from processing interruptions.\\n- Preserve uploaded resources.\\n- Prevent partial knowledge updates.\\n\\nProcessing failures shall not corrupt the student's learning graph.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Security\\n\\nDocument Intelligence shall:\\n\\n- Process only authorised student resources.\\n- Protect uploaded files.\\n- Secure extracted educational content.\\n- Respect the student privacy architecture defined in Volume F6.\\n\\nStudent learning resources remain private unless intentionally shared through approved Study Group functionality.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Quality Standards\\n\\nDocument Intelligence implementation shall include:\\n\\n- File validation testing.\\n- Text extraction validation.\\n- Knowledge extraction verification.\\n- PLKG integration testing.\\n- Performance monitoring.\\n- Operational logging.\\n\\nQuality assurance ensures reliable educational knowledge processing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Deployment Readiness\\n\\nThe implementation is ready for deployment when:\\n\\n- File processing operates correctly.\\n- Text extraction is validated.\\n- Knowledge structuring is verified.\\n- PLKG enrichment functions reliably.\\n- BLIE integration is complete.\\n- Security requirements are satisfied.\\n- Documentation is current.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe Document Intelligence Implementation Blueprint defines how approved learning resources shall be transformed into structured educational knowledge.\\n\\nThe implementation shall:\\n\\n1. Securely receive uploaded learning resources.\\n2. Extract educational content.\\n3. Identify academic concepts.\\n4. Structure knowledge for the PLKG.\\n5. Enrich the student's Personal Learning Knowledge Graph.\\n6. Provide structured knowledge to BLIE.\\n7. Preserve the integrity, security, and ownership of student learning resources.\\n\\nImplementation shall remain fully aligned with the approved Document Intelligence Architecture defined in Volume F8.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Implementation Notes (Not Part of Current Architecture)\\n\\nFuture implementation improvements may optimise document processing performance, extraction accuracy, and processing efficiency provided they remain consistent with the approved architecture and Engineering Constitution.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume G8**\\n:::\\n\\nAlhamdulillah.\\n\\nWith **G8 completed**, the **core implementation blueprints are now complete**:\\n\\n- ✅ G4 – Backend Implementation Blueprint\\n- ✅ G5 – Mobile Application Implementation Blueprint\\n- ✅ G6 – BLIE Implementation Blueprint\\n- ✅ G7 – PLKG Implementation Blueprint\\n- ✅ G8 – Document Intelligence Implementation Blueprint\\n\\nThe remaining documents (**G9–G13**) focus on engineering execution rather than architecture:\\n\\n- **G9** – API Specification\\n- **G10** – UI/UX Build Specification\\n- **G11** – Testing Strategy\\n- **G12** – Deployment Roadmap\\n- **G13** – MVP Delivery Roadmap\\n\\nThese will complete the Volume G Implementation Blueprint series. memcite\",{},{\"_305\":1477,\"_312\":1498,\"_35\":1499,\"_37\":1500,\"_316\":1501,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":1502,\"_325\":326},\"194da656-a4a5-4760-81c4-3e4754cb91c1\",[1461],{\"_370\":474,\"_323\":1510},1783658195.067268,1783658209.489996,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":1508},{\"_350\":494,\"_52\":494,\"_442\":14,\"_334\":1503,\"_339\":1504,\"_519\":1505,\"_521\":1506,\"_523\":14,\"_524\":14,\"_525\":14,\"_526\":14,\"_527\":14,\"_528\":1507,\"_343\":1489,\"_469\":-5,\"_347\":1490,\"_349\":1490,\"_338\":1134,\"_360\":497,\"_353\":14},[],[],[],[],{},[1509],\"G8 please to complete the blueprint . Introduction\\n\\nThe Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG) Implementation Blueprint defines how the PLKG shall be implemented within AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThe PLKG represents each student's personal learning knowledge structure throughout their academic journey.\\n\\nIt continuously evolves as the student progresses from the first semester until graduation.\\n\\nThe implementation follows the approved PLKG architecture and serves as the foundation for personalized learning.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Objectives\\n\\nThe PLKG shall:\\n\\n- Represent the student's learning knowledge.\\n- Connect related academic concepts.\\n- Track knowledge growth.\\n- Support BLIE reasoning.\\n- Preserve long-term learning memory.\\n- Personalize educational guidance.\\n\\nEach student owns an independent PLKG.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Implementation Principles\\n\\nImplementation follows these principles.\\n\\n## Individual Ownership\\n\\nEvery student has a separate PLKG.\\n\\nKnowledge graphs are never shared between students.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Continuous Growth\\n\\nThe PLKG grows incrementally as learning progresses.\\n\\nKnowledge is accumulated rather than recreated.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Curriculum Alignment\\n\\nKnowledge relationships reflect the student's academic curriculum and learning progression.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Structured Knowledge\\n\\nThe PLKG stores structured knowledge relationships rather than raw documents.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Explainability\\n\\nKnowledge relationships shall remain traceable and understandable.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. PLKG Lifecycle\\n\\nThe PLKG evolves throughout the student's academic journey.\\n\\nThe lifecycle consists of:\\n\\nStudent Registration\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAcademic Profile\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSubject Enrolment\\n\\n↓\\n\\nInitial Knowledge Graph\\n\\n↓\\n\\nKnowledge Growth\\n\\n↓\\n\\nContinuous Updates\\n\\n↓\\n\\nGraduation\\n\\n↓\\n\\nLong-Term Learning Record\\n\\nThe PLKG remains the student's academic knowledge history.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Graph Construction\\n\\nThe initial PLKG is created after:\\n\\n- Student registration.\\n- Programme selection.\\n- Subject enrolment.\\n\\nInitial graph nodes represent the approved curriculum structure.\\n\\nAdditional knowledge is introduced through learning activities.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Knowledge Nodes\\n\\nKnowledge nodes represent academic concepts.\\n\\nNodes may originate from:\\n\\n- Curriculum topics.\\n- Lecture materials.\\n- Student notes.\\n- Learning activities.\\n- Knowledge extraction.\\n\\nEvery node belongs to the student's PLKG.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Knowledge Relationships\\n\\nRelationships connect academic concepts.\\n\\nExamples include:\\n\\n- Prerequisite relationships.\\n- Concept associations.\\n- Learning dependencies.\\n- Subject relationships.\\n\\nRelationships are maintained throughout the student's academic journey.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Knowledge Updates\\n\\nPLKG updates occur following meaningful learning events.\\n\\nExamples include:\\n\\n- Document processing.\\n- BLIE interactions.\\n- Subject progression.\\n- Assessment activities.\\n- Learning completion.\\n\\nUpdates follow the approved knowledge processing architecture.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. BLIE Integration\\n\\nBLIE interacts with the PLKG to:\\n\\n- Retrieve related concepts.\\n- Understand learning context.\\n- Support personalized explanations.\\n- Recommend prerequisite learning.\\n- Improve educational reasoning.\\n\\nThe PLKG remains the primary source of personalized learning knowledge.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Data Integrity\\n\\nImplementation shall ensure:\\n\\n- Valid knowledge relationships.\\n- Consistent graph structure.\\n- Controlled updates.\\n- Recovery from synchronization failures.\\n\\nThe integrity of the student's learning graph shall be preserved.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Security\\n\\nThe PLKG shall be protected through:\\n\\n- Student authentication.\\n- Authorization controls.\\n- Secure storage.\\n- Encrypted communication.\\n\\nStudents retain ownership of their learning graph.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Quality Standards\\n\\nPLKG implementation shall include:\\n\\n- Graph validation.\\n- Relationship verification.\\n- Synchronization testing.\\n- Performance testing.\\n- Security validation.\\n- Operational monitoring.\\n\\nGraph quality directly affects BLIE performance.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Deployment Readiness\\n\\nThe PLKG implementation is ready for deployment when:\\n\\n- Graph construction functions correctly.\\n- Knowledge updates operate reliably.\\n- Synchronization is validated.\\n- BLIE integration is complete.\\n- Security requirements are satisfied.\\n- Documentation is current.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe PLKG Implementation Blueprint defines how the approved Personal Learning Knowledge Graph shall be implemented.\\n\\nThe implementation shall:\\n\\n1. Preserve the integrity and ownership of the student's learning knowledge.\\n\\nImplementation shall remain fully aligned with the approved PLKG architecture defined in Volumes E and F.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Implementation Notes (Not Part of Current Architecture)\\n\\nFuture implementation improvements may optimise graph storage, synchronization, and query performance provided they remain consistent with the approved PLKG architecture and Engineering Constitution.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume G7**\\n:::\\n\\nBismillah.\\n\\nWith **G7 completed**, only **six implementation documents** remain in the Volume G series:\\n\\n- **G8 – Document Intelligence Implementation Blueprint**\\n- **G9 – API Specification**\\n- **G10 – UI/UX Build Specification**\\n- **G11 – Testing Strategy**\\n- **G12 – Deployment Roadmap**\\n- **G13 – MVP Delivery Roadmap**\\n\\nThese final documents will complete the implementation blueprint while remaining fully aligned with the architecture we have already frozen. memcite\",{},{\"_305\":1512,\"_312\":1533,\"_35\":1534,\"_37\":1535,\"_316\":1536,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":1537,\"_325\":326},\"c9e6517c-9757-40eb-b166-f393b5101064\",[1496],{\"_370\":474,\"_323\":1545},1783658133.902396,1783658146.807532,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":1543},{\"_350\":494,\"_52\":494,\"_442\":14,\"_334\":1538,\"_339\":1539,\"_519\":1540,\"_521\":1541,\"_523\":14,\"_524\":14,\"_525\":14,\"_526\":14,\"_527\":14,\"_528\":1542,\"_343\":1524,\"_469\":-5,\"_347\":1525,\"_349\":1525,\"_338\":1134,\"_360\":497,\"_353\":14},[],[],[],[],{},[1544],\"Begin G7. It translates the already approved **BLIE Architecture (Volume D)** and related technical volumes (**F2, F7, F9, F10, and F11**) into an implementation blueprint.\\n\\n---\\n\\n:::writing{variant=\\\"document\\\" id=\\\"37684\\\"}\\n# AI Study Buddy\\n\\n# Volume G6 – BLIE Implementation Blueprint\\n\\n**Version:** 1.0 (Architecture Freeze)\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 1. Introduction\\n\\nThe BLIE Implementation Blueprint defines how the Buddy Learning Intelligent Engine (BLIE) shall be implemented.\\n\\nBLIE is the central intelligence layer of AI Study Buddy. It coordinates learning context, personal memory, curriculum intelligence, knowledge retrieval, and AI reasoning to provide personalized educational assistance.\\n\\nThis document translates the approved BLIE architecture into an implementation guide.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Objectives\\n\\nBLIE shall:\\n\\n- Understand student learning intent.\\n- Assemble personalized learning context.\\n- Retrieve relevant knowledge.\\n- Coordinate AI reasoning.\\n- Produce curriculum-aligned responses.\\n- Continuously improve student learning through personalization.\\n\\nBLIE remains the intelligence layer of the platform.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Implementation Principles\\n\\nImplementation follows these principles.\\n\\n## Intelligence Before Generation\\n\\nBLIE builds understanding before invoking AI reasoning.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Retrieval-First\\n\\nRelevant knowledge is retrieved before generating responses.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Personalization\\n\\nEvery response considers the student's academic context and learning history.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Curriculum Alignment\\n\\nResponses shall remain consistent with the student's enrolled subjects and learning objectives.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Provider Independence\\n\\nBLIE remains independent of any individual AI provider.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. BLIE Processing Flow\\n\\nEvery learning request follows this sequence:\\n\\nStudent Request\\n\\n↓\\n\\nIntent Analysis\\n\\n↓\\n\\nMemory Retrieval\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPLKG Retrieval\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCurriculum Context\\n\\n↓\\n\\nKnowledge Retrieval\\n\\n↓\\n\\nContext Assembly\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAI Reasoning\\n\\n↓\\n\\nResponse Validation\\n\\n↓\\n\\nStudent Response\\n\\n↓\\n\\nMemory Update (when applicable)\\n\\nThis sequence remains consistent across all learning interactions.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Intent Analysis\\n\\nBLIE determines the purpose of each student request.\\n\\nExamples include:\\n\\n- Concept explanation.\\n- Revision assistance.\\n- Study preparation.\\n- Assessment support.\\n- Learning guidance.\\n\\nIntent analysis determines the subsequent processing workflow.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Context Assembly\\n\\nBLIE constructs a learning context using approved information sources.\\n\\nContext may include:\\n\\n- Student profile.\\n- Current semester.\\n- Enrolled subjects.\\n- PLKG relationships.\\n- Learning history.\\n- Retrieved educational knowledge.\\n\\nOnly relevant context is included in each reasoning request.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Memory Integration\\n\\nBLIE retrieves information from the student's personal learning memory.\\n\\nExamples include:\\n\\n- Previously studied concepts.\\n- Areas requiring reinforcement.\\n- Recent learning activities.\\n- Historical interactions.\\n\\nMemory supports continuity throughout the student's academic journey.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. PLKG Integration\\n\\nBLIE interacts with the Personal Learning Knowledge Graph to:\\n\\n- Locate related concepts.\\n- Determine prerequisite knowledge.\\n- Assess concept relationships.\\n- Support personalized explanations.\\n\\nThe PLKG remains the student's long-term knowledge structure.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Knowledge Retrieval\\n\\nBLIE retrieves educational knowledge from approved sources before AI reasoning.\\n\\nRetrieved information supports:\\n\\n- Accurate explanations.\\n- Context-aware responses.\\n- Curriculum consistency.\\n\\nRetrieval follows the approved architecture defined in Volume F9.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. AI Orchestration\\n\\nBLIE prepares the reasoning request by combining:\\n\\n- Student intent.\\n- Retrieved knowledge.\\n- Personal learning context.\\n- Curriculum context.\\n\\nThe assembled context is submitted through the approved AI provider abstraction layer.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Response Validation\\n\\nBefore presenting a response, BLIE verifies that it is:\\n\\n- Relevant.\\n- Curriculum-aligned.\\n- Contextually appropriate.\\n- Consistent with retrieved knowledge.\\n\\nValidation maintains educational quality.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Learning Update\\n\\nFollowing each interaction, BLIE determines whether updates are required.\\n\\nPossible updates include:\\n\\n- Learning history.\\n- PLKG relationships.\\n- Personal memory.\\n- Learning analytics.\\n\\nUpdates occur only when educationally meaningful.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Error Handling\\n\\nBLIE shall:\\n\\n- Detect incomplete context.\\n- Handle retrieval failures.\\n- Manage AI provider errors.\\n- Return informative responses.\\n- Preserve learning continuity.\\n\\nStudents should receive meaningful guidance even when certain services are temporarily unavailable.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Quality Standards\\n\\nBLIE implementation shall include:\\n\\n- Unit testing.\\n- Integration testing.\\n- Retrieval validation.\\n- AI response evaluation.\\n- Performance monitoring.\\n- Operational logging.\\n\\nQuality assurance applies to every BLIE component.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Deployment Readiness\\n\\nBLIE is considered ready for deployment when:\\n\\n- Processing workflows function correctly.\\n- Retrieval operates as designed.\\n- Memory integration is verified.\\n- Response validation passes.\\n- Monitoring is operational.\\n- Documentation is complete.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe BLIE Implementation Blueprint defines how the approved Buddy Learning Intelligent Engine shall be implemented.\\n\\nBLIE shall:\\n\\n1. Analyse student learning intent.\\n2. Retrieve relevant educational knowledge.\\n3. Integrate personal learning memory.\\n4. Utilise the Personal Learning Knowledge Graph.\\n5. Coordinate AI reasoning through the approved orchestration layer.\\n6. Validate educational responses before presentation.\\n7. Continuously support personalized learning throughout the student's academic journey.\\n\\nImplementation shall remain fully aligned with the approved BLIE architecture defined in Volumes D and F.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Implementation Notes (Not Part of Current Architecture)\\n\\nFuture implementation improvements may optimise reasoning performance, context assembly, or AI model selection without changing the approved BLIE architecture or engineering principles.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume G6**\\n:::\\n\\nBismillah.\\n\\nWith **G6 complete**, the next document is **Volume G7 – PLKG Implementation Blueprint**, where we will define how the student's Personal Learning Knowledge Graph is constructed, updated, synchronized, and maintained throughout their journey from the first semester until graduation, strictly following the architecture already frozen in Volumes E and F. memcite\",{},{\"_305\":1547,\"_312\":1574,\"_35\":1575,\"_37\":1576,\"_316\":1577,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":1578,\"_325\":326},\"4a61a06b-5a03-4532-ae6c-44c314c44bcc\",[1531],{\"_370\":474,\"_323\":1586},1783658095.492048,1783658111.45042,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":1584},{\"_350\":494,\"_52\":494,\"_442\":14,\"_334\":1579,\"_339\":1580,\"_519\":1581,\"_521\":1582,\"_523\":14,\"_524\":14,\"_525\":14,\"_526\":14,\"_527\":14,\"_528\":1583,\"_343\":1559,\"_469\":-5,\"_347\":1560,\"_349\":1560,\"_338\":1134,\"_360\":497,\"_353\":14},[],[],[],[],{},[1585],\"Start G6. Objectives\\n\\nThe mobile application shall:\\n\\n- Deliver a responsive user experience.\\n- Support offline-first learning.\\n- Synchronize seamlessly with the cloud.\\n- Provide secure access to student data.\\n- Present BLIE in a simple and intuitive manner.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Presentation Layer\\n\\nResponsibilities include:\\n\\n- User interface.\\n- Navigation.\\n- Student interactions.\\n- Display of learning progress.\\n- BLIE conversations.\\n- Study resources.\\n\\nThe Presentation Layer contains no business logic.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Application Logic Layer\\n\\nResponsibilities include:\\n\\n- User workflows.\\n- Session management.\\n- Local state management.\\n- Screen coordination.\\n- Validation before API requests.\\n\\nBusiness rules remain in the backend.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Network Layer\\n\\nThe Network Layer manages communication with backend services.\\n\\nResponsibilities include:\\n\\n- API requests.\\n- Authentication tokens.\\n- Secure communication.\\n- Error handling.\\n- Request retries.\\n\\nAll communication follows the API architecture defined in Volume F15.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Security Implementation\\n\\nThe mobile application shall:\\n\\n- Protect authentication sessions.\\n- Encrypt sensitive local data.\\n- Use secure communication channels.\\n- Respect student privacy.\\n\\nSecurity implementation follows the approved Security Architecture.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Error Handling\\n\\nThe application shall:\\n\\n- Detect connectivity issues.\\n- Display meaningful error messages.\\n- Retry failed synchronization.\\n- Preserve unsynchronized work.\\n- Record operational information where appropriate.\\n\\nErrors shall not result in unnecessary data loss.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Integrate with BLIE through approved APIs.\\n6. Protect student data at all times.\\n\\nImplementation shall remain consistent with the Mobile Application Architecture defined in Volume F14.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Implementation Notes (Not Part of Current Architecture)\\n\\nFuture implementation optimisations may improve performance, user experience, or platform capabilities provided they remain consistent with the approved architecture and Engineering Constitution.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume G5**\\n:::\\n\\nBismillah.\\n\\nWith **G5 completed**, the next document will be **Volume G6 – BLIE Implementation Blueprint**, which will describe how the Buddy Learning Intelligent Engine is implemented based entirely on the architecture already frozen in Volumes D and F, without introducing new capabilities or changing its design. memcite\",{},{\"_305\":1588,\"_312\":1609,\"_35\":1610,\"_37\":1611,\"_316\":1612,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":1613,\"_325\":326},\"6f33853a-9cd1-4bd8-929c-c51e7e0ac51f\",[1572],{\"_370\":474,\"_323\":1621},1783657698.193365,1783657710.341627,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":1619},{\"_350\":494,\"_52\":494,\"_442\":14,\"_334\":1614,\"_339\":1615,\"_519\":1616,\"_521\":1617,\"_523\":14,\"_524\":14,\"_525\":14,\"_526\":14,\"_527\":14,\"_528\":1618,\"_343\":1600,\"_469\":-5,\"_347\":1601,\"_349\":1601,\"_338\":1134,\"_360\":497,\"_353\":14},[],[],[],[],{},[1620],\"Proceed G5. Implementation Principles\\n\\nImplementation shall follow these principles.\\n\\n## Modular\\n\\nEach business capability is implemented as an independent module.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## API-First\\n\\nEvery capability is accessed through documented APIs.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Stateless\\n\\nApplication services remain stateless wherever practical.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Secure\\n\\nAuthentication and authorization apply to every protected endpoint.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Scalable\\n\\nModules shall support independent scaling without architectural changes.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Backend Structure\\n\\nThe backend implementation consists of:\\n\\n- API Layer\\n- Business Logic Layer\\n- BLIE Layer\\n- Data Access Layer\\n- Background Worker Layer\\n- Integration Layer\\n\\nEach layer has a clearly defined responsibility.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. API Layer\\n\\nResponsibilities:\\n\\n- Receive client requests.\\n- Validate input.\\n- Authenticate requests.\\n- Authorize access.\\n- Return standardized responses.\\n\\nThe API layer contains no business rules.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Business Logic Layer\\n\\nResponsibilities:\\n\\n- Student management.\\n- Subject management.\\n- Curriculum operations.\\n- Assessments.\\n- Study Groups.\\n- Subscription management.\\n- Learning progress.\\n\\nBusiness rules are implemented here.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. BLIE Layer\\n\\nThe BLIE implementation coordinates:\\n\\n- Context assembly.\\n- Memory retrieval.\\n- PLKG retrieval.\\n- Curriculum intelligence.\\n- AI orchestration.\\n- Response generation.\\n\\nBLIE remains independent of individual AI providers.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Data Access Layer\\n\\nResponsibilities:\\n\\n- Database operations.\\n- Object storage access.\\n- Transaction management.\\n- Data validation.\\n\\nDatabase access is centralized within this layer.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Background Worker Layer\\n\\nBackground workers execute long-running tasks.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- OCR processing.\\n- Document analysis.\\n- Knowledge extraction.\\n- PLKG updates.\\n- Learning analytics.\\n- Notification processing.\\n\\nWorkers communicate through the approved event-driven architecture.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Integration Layer\\n\\nResponsibilities:\\n\\n- AI providers.\\n- Authentication services.\\n- Object storage.\\n- Notification services.\\n\\nExternal integrations remain isolated from core business logic.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Module Responsibilities\\n\\nBackend modules include:\\n\\n- Identity\\n- Student\\n- Curriculum\\n- BLIE\\n- PLKG\\n- Assessment\\n- Study Group\\n- Subscription\\n- Notification\\n- Synchronization\\n- Document Intelligence\\n\\nEach module owns its own business capability.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Error Handling\\n\\nBackend services shall:\\n\\n- Validate all requests.\\n- Return consistent error responses.\\n- Record operational logs.\\n- Protect sensitive information.\\n- Support troubleshooting.\\n\\nInternal implementation details shall never be exposed to clients.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Security Implementation\\n\\nEvery protected request follows:\\n\\nAuthentication\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAuthorization\\n\\n↓\\n\\nValidation\\n\\n↓\\n\\nBusiness Logic\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAudit Logging\\n\\nSecurity remains consistent across all backend modules.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Background Processing Flow\\n\\nLong-running operations follow:\\n\\nClient Request\\n\\n↓\\n\\nEvent Queue\\n\\n↓\\n\\nWorker Processing\\n\\n↓\\n\\nDatabase Update\\n\\n↓\\n\\nNotification\\n\\nThis prevents blocking user interactions.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Backend Quality Standards\\n\\nEvery backend module shall include:\\n\\n- Unit tests.\\n- Integration tests.\\n- Logging.\\n- Monitoring.\\n- Documentation.\\n- Error handling.\\n\\nImplementation quality is part of the feature definition.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Maintain modular business services.\\n2. Keep business logic separate from APIs.\\n3. Centralize BLIE orchestration.\\n4. Protect student data.\\n5. Execute long-running work asynchronously.\\n6. Development Vision\\n\\nThe goal is not to build every feature immediately.\\n\\nThe goal is to build a strong educational platform that grows safely without requiring architectural redesign.\\n\\nEvery development phase should produce a working product that students can use.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Development Principles\\n\\nThe engineering team shall follow these principles.\\n\\n## Architecture First\\n\\nImplementation follows approved architecture.\\n\\nArchitecture does not follow implementation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Vertical Slice Development\\n\\nComplete one capability end-to-end before beginning the next.\\n\\nEach feature includes:\\n\\n- Mobile interface.\\n- Backend services.\\n- Database.\\n- BLIE integration.\\n- Synchronization.\\n- Testing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Continuous Delivery\\n\\nDeliver small improvements frequently.\\n\\nEvery release should provide measurable value.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Feedback Driven\\n\\nReal student feedback guides product refinement.\\n\\nArchitecture remains stable while implementation evolves.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Technical Debt Management\\n\\nTechnical debt is tracked, prioritised, and resolved intentionally.\\n\\nShort-term shortcuts must never compromise the platform's long-term integrity.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. MVP Definition\\n\\nThe MVP must answer one question:\\n\\n**Can BLIE genuinely improve a student's learning experience?**\\n\\nThe MVP includes only essential capabilities:\\n\\n- Authentication.\\n- Student profile.\\n- Subject management.\\n- Document upload.\\n- OCR.\\n- BLIE Chat.\\n- Basic PLKG.\\n- Learning history.\\n- Offline support.\\n- Cloud synchronization.\\n\\nEverything else can evolve later.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Development Workflow\\n\\nEvery feature follows the same lifecycle.\\n\\n```text id=\\\"g1flow01\\\"\\nArchitecture\\n\\n↓\\n\\nTechnical Design\\n\\n↓\\n\\nImplementation\\n\\n↓\\n\\nTesting\\n\\n↓\\n\\nReview\\n\\n↓\\n\\nDeployment\\n\\n↓\\n\\nMonitoring\\n\\n↓\\n\\nFeedback\\n\\n↓\\n\\nIteration\\n```\\n\\nThis workflow applies to every release.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Source Control Strategy\\n\\nDevelopment uses:\\n\\n- Main branch.\\n- Development branch.\\n- Feature branches.\\n\\nEvery change is reviewed before merging into the main branch.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Coding Standards\\n\\nThe engineering team shall adopt consistent standards.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Clear naming conventions.\\n- Modular design.\\n- Small functions.\\n- Comprehensive documentation.\\n- Automated formatting.\\n- Static analysis.\\n\\nConsistency is more valuable than personal preference.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Documentation Strategy\\n\\nDocumentation evolves together with the software.\\n\\nMajor updates include:\\n\\n- Architecture.\\n- APIs.\\n- Database.\\n- Deployment.\\n- User guides.\\n- Developer guides.\\n\\nDocumentation is treated as part of the product.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Release Strategy\\n\\nReleases occur incrementally.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Internal development.\\n- Alpha testing.\\n- Closed beta.\\n- Open beta.\\n- Public release.\\n\\nEach stage validates stability before expanding the user base.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Success Metrics\\n\\nEngineering success is measured by:\\n\\n- Platform stability.\\n- Performance.\\n- Student engagement.\\n- Learning effectiveness.\\n- Deployment reliability.\\n- Development velocity.\\n\\nThe platform is successful only if students benefit from using it.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Risk Management\\n\\nKey engineering risks include:\\n\\n- Scope expansion.\\n- AI cost growth.\\n- Performance bottlenecks.\\n- Data consistency.\\n- Security vulnerabilities.\\n- Operational complexity.\\n\\nRisks should be reviewed continuously throughout development.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Long-Term Roadmap\\n\\nThe architecture supports continuous evolution.\\n\\nYear 1\\n\\nBuild a stable MVP.\\n\\n↓\\n\\nYear 2\\n\\nExpand educational intelligence.\\n\\n↓\\n\\nYear 3\\n\\nScale globally.\\n\\n↓\\n\\nFuture\\n\\nSupport lifelong learning beyond university.\\n\\nThe roadmap emphasises sustainable growth rather than rapid feature accumulation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe Engineering Strategy \u0026 Development Roadmap establishes the implementation philosophy for AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThe engineering organisation shall:\\n\\n1. It acts as the constitution that every engineer, AI coding assistant, and future contributor must follow.\\n\\n---\\n\\n:::writing{variant=\\\"document\\\" id=\\\"10372\\\"}\\n# AI Study Buddy\\n\\n# Volume G0 – Engineering Constitution\\n\\n**Version:** 1.0 (Architecture Freeze)\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 1. Introduction\\n\\nThe Engineering Constitution defines the fundamental engineering principles that govern the design, implementation, operation, and future evolution of AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThis document is the highest technical authority of the project.\\n\\nEvery software component, AI workflow, database schema, API, mobile application, and infrastructure decision shall comply with this constitution.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Mission\\n\\nThe mission of AI Study Buddy is:\\n\\n\u003e To become every university student's lifelong intelligent learning companion, helping them learn more effectively from their first semester until graduation through personalized educational intelligence.\\n\\nTechnology exists to serve learning.\\n\\nEvery engineering decision shall improve the student's learning experience.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Core Engineering Principles\\n\\nThe platform shall always follow these principles.\\n\\n## Student First\\n\\nEngineering decisions must prioritize educational outcomes over technical convenience.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Simplicity Before Complexity\\n\\nChoose the simplest architecture that satisfies the requirements.\\n\\nComplexity must always be justified.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Modular Architecture\\n\\nEvery major capability shall exist as an independent module or service.\\n\\nNo component should become unnecessarily dependent on another.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Scalability\\n\\nEvery design should support growth from thousands to millions of students without requiring architectural redesign.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Reliability\\n\\nStudents should trust AI Study Buddy as a dependable learning companion.\\n\\nAvailability, correctness, and consistency are essential.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Security\\n\\nStudent privacy and data protection are built into every layer of the platform.\\n\\nSecurity is never an optional feature.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Maintainability\\n\\nThe codebase should remain understandable and extensible for future contributors.\\n\\nReadable systems are preferred over clever systems.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. BLIE Principles\\n\\nBLIE is the intelligence layer of the platform.\\n\\nBLIE shall always own:\\n\\n- Learning logic.\\n- Personalization.\\n- Memory.\\n- Curriculum intelligence.\\n- Knowledge reasoning.\\n- Recommendation logic.\\n\\nAI models provide reasoning services only.\\n\\nBLIE owns the educational intelligence.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG)\\n\\nEvery student owns an independent PLKG.\\n\\nThe PLKG represents the student's personal learning journey.\\n\\nIt shall never be shared automatically.\\n\\nEvery modification to the PLKG must result from meaningful learning activity or verified educational processing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Retrieval Before Generation\\n\\nEvery AI response shall follow this sequence:\\n\\n1. Understand the student's intent.\\n2. Retrieve relevant knowledge.\\n3. Retrieve the student's learning context.\\n4. Assemble the reasoning context.\\n5. Invoke the AI model.\\n6. Validate the response.\\n7. Update learning memory when appropriate.\\n\\nBLIE shall never rely solely on an AI model's internal knowledge when trusted educational context is available.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. AI Provider Independence\\n\\nThe platform shall not depend on a single AI provider.\\n\\nAll AI models are accessed through a provider abstraction layer.\\n\\nChanging AI providers shall not require changes to application logic.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Cloud-First, Offline-First\\n\\nCloud infrastructure remains the system of record.\\n\\nThe mobile application shall continue supporting meaningful learning while offline.\\n\\nSynchronization restores consistency automatically when connectivity returns.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. API-First Development\\n\\nEvery platform capability shall be exposed through stable, documented APIs.\\n\\nClients shall never access backend databases directly.\\n\\nAll business rules remain on the server.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Service Ownership\\n\\nEvery backend service owns one business capability.\\n\\nExamples include:\\n\\n- Identity.\\n- BLIE.\\n- PLKG.\\n- Curriculum.\\n- Assessments.\\n- Study Groups.\\n- Subscription.\\n\\nCross-service coupling should be minimized.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Event-Driven Processing\\n\\nLong-running work shall execute asynchronously.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Document processing.\\n- OCR.\\n- Knowledge extraction.\\n- Learning analytics.\\n- AI enrichment.\\n\\nStudents should never wait unnecessarily for background processing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Privacy by Design\\n\\nStudents retain ownership of:\\n\\n- Notes.\\n- Uploaded documents.\\n- Learning history.\\n- PLKG.\\n- Personal learning analytics.\\n\\nOnly the minimum necessary data may be shared with external AI providers.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Documentation Before Implementation\\n\\nArchitecture changes shall be documented before implementation.\\n\\nThe approved documentation becomes the reference for development.\\n\\nImplementation follows documentation—not the reverse.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Backward Compatibility\\n\\nWhenever practical:\\n\\n- APIs remain backward compatible.\\n- Data migrations are non-destructive.\\n- Existing student data is preserved.\\n\\nBreaking changes require clear migration strategies.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Quality Standards\\n\\nEvery feature shall include:\\n\\n- Automated tests.\\n- Error handling.\\n- Logging.\\n- Monitoring.\\n- Documentation.\\n\\nQuality is a mandatory requirement, not an enhancement.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Cost Awareness\\n\\nEngineering decisions shall balance:\\n\\n- Performance.\\n- Reliability.\\n- Scalability.\\n- Operational cost.\\n\\nResources should be used efficiently without reducing educational value.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. Future Evolution\\n\\nThe architecture shall support future technologies without fundamental redesign.\\n\\nExamples include:\\n\\n- New AI models.\\n- Local on-device intelligence.\\n- Voice interfaces.\\n- New learning modalities.\\n\\nThe platform evolves by extending its architecture rather than replacing it.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 18. Engineering Decision Process\\n\\nWhen multiple implementation options exist, evaluate them in this order:\\n\\n1. Educational benefit.\\n2. Student privacy.\\n3. Architectural consistency.\\n4. Simplicity.\\n5. Reliability.\\n6. Scalability.\\n7. Maintainability.\\n8. Performance.\\n9. Cost.\\n\\nThis order reflects the priorities of AI Study Buddy.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 19. Definition of Done\\n\\nA feature is considered complete only when:\\n\\n- The implementation follows the approved architecture.\\n- Automated tests pass.\\n- Documentation is updated.\\n- Security requirements are satisfied.\\n- Performance targets are met.\\n- Monitoring is in place.\\n- Code review is completed.\\n\\nFunctionality alone does not define completion.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 20. Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThis Engineering Constitution is the governing technical document for AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nAll future implementation shall remain aligned with the architectural principles established in Volumes A through G.\\n\\nChanges to this constitution require careful review because they affect the long-term integrity of the platform.\\n\\nThe guiding principle is:\\n\\n**Every line of code should strengthen the student's learning journey. Every architectural decision should preserve the integrity, scalability, and trustworthiness of AI Study Buddy.**\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume G0**\\n:::\\n\\nAlhamdulillah.\\n\\nThis constitution is intentionally concise and principle-driven. It should be referenced by every future implementation document, every repository's `AGENTS.md`, and every AI coding assistant prompt so that regardless of whether development is done by humans, Codex, Claude Code, or future AI agents, they all follow the same engineering philosophy and architectural constraints. memcite\",{},{\"_305\":1994,\"_312\":2020,\"_35\":2021,\"_37\":2022,\"_316\":2023,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":2024,\"_325\":326},\"0ac0e3f4-bddd-4ae0-bd63-7148785d15f2\",[1978],{\"_370\":474,\"_323\":2032},1783641287.852347,1783641303.856571,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":2030},{\"_350\":494,\"_52\":494,\"_442\":14,\"_334\":2025,\"_339\":2026,\"_519\":2027,\"_521\":2028,\"_523\":14,\"_524\":14,\"_525\":14,\"_526\":14,\"_527\":14,\"_528\":2029,\"_343\":2006,\"_469\":-5,\"_347\":2007,\"_349\":2007,\"_338\":1134,\"_360\":497,\"_353\":14},[],[],[],[],{},[2031],\"Start with G0 – Engineering Constitution. architecture, then iterate.**\\n\\nThis keeps development focused and prevents unnecessary complexity while preserving the architecture we have already frozen.\\n\\nI also recommend one additional document that will become the **master reference** for the engineering team:\\n\\n## G0 – Engineering Constitution\\n\\nThis document would define the non-negotiable engineering rules, for example:\\n\\n- Never bypass BLIE.\\n- Never expose PLKG directly to clients.\\n- Cloud-first, offline-first architecture.\\n- Every AI response must be retrieval-grounded.\\n- Every feature must respect student privacy.\\n- No vendor lock-in.\\n- Service-oriented backend.\\n- API-first development.\\n- Backward compatibility whenever practical.\\n- Architecture changes require documentation updates before implementation.\\n\\nThis would serve the same purpose as an **AGENTS.md** or engineering charter, ensuring every developer and AI coding assistant (such as Codex or Claude Code) follows the same architectural principles.\\n\\nI recommend we begin with **Volume G0 – Engineering Constitution** before G1. It will become the \\\"constitution\\\" for the entire AI Study Buddy codebase and ensure the implementation remains faithful to the architecture we've established.
