lah.\\n\\nWe now proceed with **Volume F9 – BLIE Retrieval \u0026 Reasoning Architecture (RAG + Knowledge Graph)**.\\n\\nThis is one of the most critical architecture volumes because this is where all previous components converge:\\n\\n- **F1 Database** provides the foundation.\\n- **F2 BLIE Pipeline** provides intelligence processing.\\n- **F7 Memory Architecture** provides student understanding.\\n- **F8 Document Intelligence** provides knowledge extraction.\\n- **PLKG** provides the student's personal learning map.\\n\\nF9 defines:\\n\\n\u003e **How BLIE thinks before answering a student.**\\n\\nThe key difference:\\n\\nA normal AI assistant:\\n\\n```\\nQuestion\\n   ↓\\nLLM\\n   ↓\\nAnswer\\n```\\n\\nAI Study Buddy:\\n\\n```\\nQuestion\\n   ↓\\nUnderstand Student Intent\\n   ↓\\nUnderstand Student Knowledge State\\n   ↓\\nRetrieve Relevant Knowledge\\n   ↓\\nTraverse Knowledge Graph\\n   ↓\\nReason Based on Context\\n   ↓\\nGenerate Personalized Learning Response\\n   ↓\\nUpdate Learning Memory\\n```\\n\\nBismillah, we begin.\\n\\n---\\n\\n:::writing{variant=\\\"document\\\" id=\\\"64831\\\"}\\n# AI Study Buddy\\n\\n# Volume F9 – BLIE Retrieval \u0026 Reasoning Architecture\\n## (RAG + Knowledge Graph Intelligence)\\n\\n**Version:** 1.0 (Architecture Freeze)\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 1. Introduction\\n\\nThe BLIE Retrieval \u0026 Reasoning Architecture defines how the Buddy Learning Intelligent Engine combines:\\n\\n- Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG)\\n- Global Knowledge Graph (GKG)\\n- Student memory\\n- Learning materials\\n- AI reasoning models\\n\\nto generate personalized educational assistance.\\n\\nBLIE is not designed as a simple chatbot.\\n\\nIt is designed as a reasoning system that understands:\\n\\n- What the student is asking.\\n- What the student already knows.\\n- What the student does not understand.\\n- What knowledge is required next.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Core Philosophy\\n\\nThe intelligence loop:\\n\\n```\\nRetrieve → Understand → Reason → Teach → Learn\\n```\\n\\nBLIE must answer based on:\\n\\n## Academic Truth\\n\\nFrom:\\n\\n- Curriculum knowledge.\\n- Learning materials.\\n- Verified educational sources.\\n\\n## Student Context\\n\\nFrom:\\n\\n- Personal knowledge graph.\\n- Learning history.\\n- Mastery level.\\n- Previous mistakes.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. BLIE Reasoning Architecture\\n\\nHigh-level flow:\\n\\n```\\nStudent Question\\n\\n        ↓\\n\\nIntent Understanding\\n\\n        ↓\\n\\nContext Intelligence\\n\\n        ↓\\n\\nKnowledge Retrieval\\n\\n        ↓\\n\\nGraph Reasoning\\n\\n        ↓\\n\\nAI Generation\\n\\n        ↓\\n\\nLearning Update\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Stage 1 — Intent Understanding\\n\\nBefore answering, BLIE identifies the student's intention.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nStudent asks:\\n\\n\\\"Why is recursion difficult?\\\"\\n\\nPossible intents:\\n\\n- Concept explanation.\\n- Debugging problem.\\n- Learning difficulty.\\n- Revision request.\\n- Exam preparation.\\n\\nThe same question may require different responses.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Stage 2 — Student Context Retrieval\\n\\nBLIE retrieves the student's learning state.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nStudent asks:\\n\\n\\\"Explain recursion.\\\"\\n\\nBLIE checks:\\n\\n```\\nStudent PLKG\\n\\nProgramming Basics\\n     ✓ mastered\\n\\nFunctions\\n     ✓ mastered\\n\\nLoops\\n     ✓ mastered\\n\\nRecursion\\n     ✗ struggling\\n```\\n\\nResponse level is adjusted.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Stage 3 — Knowledge Retrieval System\\n\\nBLIE uses hybrid retrieval.\\n\\n## Vector Retrieval\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nFind semantically similar information.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nStudent asks:\\n\\n\\\"What happens when a function calls itself?\\\"\\n\\nFinds:\\n\\n- Recursion notes.\\n- Examples.\\n- Lecture materials.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Knowledge Graph Retrieval\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nUnderstand relationships.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nRecursion\\n\\nrequires\\n\\nFunctions\\n\\nrequires\\n\\nVariables\\n```\\n\\nGraph retrieval identifies prerequisites.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Structured Retrieval\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\nAccess precise information.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Course outline.\\n- Assignment requirements.\\n- Quiz history.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Hybrid RAG Architecture\\n\\nBLIE uses:\\n\\n```\\n              Student Question\\n\\n                     ↓\\n\\n              Retrieval Router\\n\\n        ┌────────────┼────────────┐\\n\\n    Vector Search   Graph Search   Database\\n\\n        └────────────┼────────────┘\\n\\n                     ↓\\n\\n             Context Builder\\n\\n                     ↓\\n\\n                 AI Reasoning\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Knowledge Graph Reasoning\\n\\nThe graph provides relationships that normal search cannot understand.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nStudent asks:\\n\\n\\\"Why do I need calculus for machine learning?\\\"\\n\\nBLIE traverses:\\n\\n```\\nMachine Learning\\n\\nrequires\\n\\nOptimization\\n\\nrequires\\n\\nCalculus\\n\\nrequires\\n\\nDifferentiation\\n```\\n\\nThen explains the learning path.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Personal Knowledge Reasoning\\n\\nBLIE does not only retrieve facts.\\n\\nIt reasons about the student.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nTwo students ask:\\n\\n\\\"Explain database indexing.\\\"\\n\\nStudent A:\\n\\n```\\nDatabase Basics\\n90%\\n```\\n\\nResponse:\\n\\nAdvanced explanation.\\n\\n---\\n\\nStudent B:\\n\\n```\\nDatabase Basics\\n40%\\n```\\n\\nResponse:\\n\\nExplain foundation first.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Context Assembly Engine\\n\\nBefore AI generation, BLIE creates a reasoning package.\\n\\nContains:\\n\\n## Question Context\\n\\nWhat is being asked.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Academic Context\\n\\nRelevant subject information.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Student Context\\n\\nCurrent understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Knowledge Context\\n\\nRelevant concepts and resources.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning Objective\\n\\nWhat outcome is desired.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Response Generation Strategy\\n\\nBLIE responses should follow educational principles.\\n\\nNot only:\\n\\n\\\"Here is the answer.\\\"\\n\\nInstead:\\n\\n```\\nExplain\\n\\n↓\\n\\nConnect\\n\\n↓\\n\\nDemonstrate\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPractice\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCheck Understanding\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nStudent asks:\\n\\n\\\"What is normalization?\\\"\\n\\nBLIE response:\\n\\n1. Explain concept.\\n2. Connect to database design.\\n3. Show example.\\n4. Ask practice question.\\n5. Update understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Hallucination Control Architecture\\n\\nBLIE reduces hallucination through:\\n\\n## Knowledge Grounding\\n\\nResponses are based on retrieved knowledge.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Source Awareness\\n\\nBLIE knows where information came from.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Lecture notes.\\n- Textbook.\\n- Curriculum knowledge.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Confidence Evaluation\\n\\nBLIE evaluates:\\n\\n- Knowledge availability.\\n- Source reliability.\\n- Reasoning confidence.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Learning Feedback Loop\\n\\nAfter interaction:\\n\\n```\\nStudent Interaction\\n\\n        ↓\\n\\nResponse Analysis\\n\\n        ↓\\n\\nLearning Signal Detection\\n\\n        ↓\\n\\nUpdate PLKG\\n\\n        ↓\\n\\nUpdate Memory\\n\\n        ↓\\n\\nImprove Future Responses\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Example Complete BLIE Flow\\n\\nStudent:\\n\\n\\\"Why can't I understand pointers in C++?\\\"\\n\\nBLIE:\\n\\nStep 1:\\n\\nIdentify concept:\\n\\n```\\nPointers\\n```\\n\\nStep 2:\\n\\nCheck PLKG:\\n\\n```\\nVariables ✓\\n\\nMemory Concept ✗\\n\\nAddress Concept ✗\\n```\\n\\nStep 3:\\n\\nFind prerequisites:\\n\\n```\\nMemory Address\\n\\n↓\\n\\nVariables\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPointers\\n```\\n\\nStep 4:\\n\\nGenerate response:\\n\\n\\\"Before pointers, let's strengthen your understanding of memory addresses.\\\"\\n\\nStep 5:\\n\\nUpdate:\\n\\n```\\nStudent needs reinforcement:\\n\\nMemory Model\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Advanced Future Capability\\n\\nFuture BLIE versions may support:\\n\\n- Multi-step reasoning.\\n- Automatic study planning.\\n- Socratic questioning.\\n- Exam strategy generation.\\n- Research assistance.\\n- Cross-disciplinary knowledge discovery.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe BLIE Retrieval \u0026 Reasoning Architecture defines AI Study Buddy as an intelligent learning system.\\n\\nBLIE shall:\\n\\n1. Understand student intent.\\n2. Retrieve knowledge from multiple sources.\\n3. Reason using knowledge graphs.\\n4. Personalize answers using student memory.\\n5. Reduce hallucination through grounding.\\n6. Improve through continuous learning interaction.\\n\\nThe core intelligence principle:\\n\\n**BLIE does not answer questions. BLIE guides the student's understanding journey.**\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume F9**\\n:::\\n\\nBismillah.\\n\\nWith **Volume F9 completed**, we now have the complete intelligence reasoning volume is where AI Study Buddy truly becomes different from conventional note-taking or AI chat applications.\\n\\nThe key philosophy is:\\n\\n\u003e **Students upload documents, but BLIE does not store documents as knowledge. It transforms documents into structured, connected, and personalized knowledge within the Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG).**\\n\\nA PDF is only the starting point. The real asset is the knowledge extracted from it.\\n\\n---\\n\\n:::writing{variant=\\\"document\\\" id=\\\"41287\\\"}\\n# AI Study Buddy\\n\\n# Volume F8 – Knowledge Processing \u0026 Document Intelligence Architecture\\n\\n**Version:** 1.0 (Architecture Freeze)\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 1. Introduction\\n\\nThe Knowledge Processing \u0026 Document Intelligence Architecture defines how BLIE transforms raw learning materials into structured academic knowledge.\\n\\nStudents may upload:\\n\\n- Lecture slides (PDF)\\n- Lecture notes\\n- Assignment documents\\n- Tutorial sheets\\n- Images\\n- Whiteboard photos\\n- Personal handwritten notes\\n\\nBLIE processes these materials and continuously enriches the student's Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG).\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Vision\\n\\nTo convert every learning resource into meaningful, connected knowledge that supports understanding rather than simple document storage.\\n\\nKnowledge should become searchable, explainable, and connected throughout the student's academic journey.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Architecture Principles\\n\\nThe document intelligence pipeline follows six principles.\\n\\n## Knowledge First\\n\\nDocuments are temporary inputs.\\n\\nKnowledge is the permanent asset.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Structure Before Storage\\n\\nInformation must be organised into concepts and relationships.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Incremental Learning\\n\\nEvery uploaded document strengthens the existing PLKG rather than creating isolated information.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Student Context\\n\\nKnowledge extraction considers:\\n\\n- Degree programme\\n- Semester\\n- Subject\\n- Existing PLKG\\n- Current learning progress\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Human Verification\\n\\nStudents may review, edit, or remove extracted knowledge.\\n\\nBLIE assists but does not replace student ownership.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Continuous Enrichment\\n\\nKnowledge continues evolving as more learning materials are added.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Knowledge Processing Pipeline\\n\\nEvery uploaded document follows the same processing flow.\\n\\n```text\\nUpload Document\\n\\n↓\\n\\nDocument Classification\\n\\n↓\\n\\nText \u0026 Image Extraction\\n\\n↓\\n\\nContent Understanding\\n\\n↓\\n\\nConcept Identification\\n\\n↓\\n\\nRelationship Mapping\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPLKG Enrichment\\n\\n↓\\n\\nLearning Intelligence Ready\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Stage 1 – Document Classification\\n\\nBLIE first determines what has been uploaded.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Lecture slides\\n- Tutorial sheet\\n- Assignment\\n- Textbook chapter\\n- Lab manual\\n- Student notes\\n- Whiteboard image\\n\\nThe document type influences later processing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Stage 2 – Content Extraction\\n\\nBLIE extracts all available information.\\n\\nSupported content includes:\\n\\n- Digital text\\n- OCR from images\\n- Tables\\n- Diagrams\\n- Mathematical expressions\\n- Figures\\n- Captions\\n\\nThe objective is to recover as much educational content as possible.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Stage 3 – Semantic Understanding\\n\\nBLIE analyses the meaning of the content.\\n\\nIt identifies:\\n\\n- Main topics\\n- Learning objectives\\n- Definitions\\n- Key concepts\\n- Examples\\n- Procedures\\n- Formula explanations\\n- References between sections\\n\\nThis transforms text into educational understanding.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Stage 4 – Concept Identification\\n\\nBLIE extracts important learning concepts.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nLecture:\\n\\n\\\"Introduction to Database Normalization\\\"\\n\\nExtracted concepts:\\n\\n- Database\\n- Normalization\\n- Functional Dependency\\n- First Normal Form\\n- Second Normal Form\\n- Third Normal Form\\n\\nEach concept becomes a candidate knowledge node.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Stage 5 – Relationship Discovery\\n\\nBLIE discovers how concepts relate.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n```text\\nNormalization\\n\\nrequires\\n\\nFunctional Dependency\\n```\\n\\n```text\\nSecond Normal Form\\n\\nextends\\n\\nFirst Normal Form\\n```\\n\\n```text\\nThird Normal Form\\n\\ndepends_on\\n\\nSecond Normal Form\\n```\\n\\nThese relationships become part of the student's PLKG.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Stage 6 – Knowledge Validation\\n\\nBefore creating new knowledge nodes, BLIE checks:\\n\\n- Does this concept already exist?\\n- Is this another name for an existing concept?\\n- Is this subject-specific terminology?\\n- Does it strengthen an existing relationship?\\n\\nDuplicate knowledge should be avoided whenever possible.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Stage 7 – PLKG Enrichment\\n\\nValidated knowledge is added to the student's Personal Learning Knowledge Graph.\\n\\nThe enrichment process may:\\n\\n- Create new concepts.\\n- Strengthen existing concepts.\\n- Add relationships.\\n- Link learning resources.\\n- Update mastery indicators.\\n\\nThe graph grows continuously rather than restarting with each upload.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Cross-Subject Knowledge Integration\\n\\nKnowledge often spans multiple subjects.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nStatistics\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSupports\\n\\nMachine Learning\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSupports\\n\\nArtificial Intelligence\\n\\nBLIE connects concepts across semesters and subjects to help students understand the bigger picture.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Student Note Integration\\n\\nPersonal notes receive the same intelligent treatment.\\n\\nBLIE can:\\n\\n- Extract concepts.\\n- Link notes to existing knowledge.\\n- Associate notes with lecture materials.\\n- Recommend related concepts.\\n\\nStudent-created knowledge becomes part of the PLKG.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Learning Resource Relationships\\n\\nEach uploaded resource is linked to the knowledge it supports.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nLecture 5.pdf\\n\\n↓\\n\\nExplains\\n\\n↓\\n\\nDatabase Normalization\\n\\n↓\\n\\nRelated Quiz\\n\\n↓\\n\\nStudent Notes\\n\\n↓\\n\\nRevision Flashcards\\n\\nA single resource may support many connected learning activities.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Knowledge Quality Improvement\\n\\nAs additional materials are uploaded, BLIE continuously improves understanding by:\\n\\n- Merging duplicate concepts.\\n- Expanding concept descriptions.\\n- Discovering new relationships.\\n- Improving prerequisite mappings.\\n- Refining learning recommendations.\\n\\nKnowledge quality improves over time rather than remaining static.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Personalization During Processing\\n\\nKnowledge extraction is personalised.\\n\\nThe same document may produce different learning guidance depending on the student's PLKG.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\nStudent A\\n\\nStrong in prerequisite concepts.\\n\\nBLIE recommends advanced exploration.\\n\\nStudent B\\n\\nWeak prerequisite foundation.\\n\\nBLIE recommends prerequisite revision before continuing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. Future Intelligence\\n\\nFuture versions may support:\\n\\n- Handwritten note recognition.\\n- Formula understanding.\\n- Diagram interpretation.\\n- Lecture audio transcription.\\n- Video lecture analysis.\\n- Automatic concept timeline generation.\\n\\nThese capabilities extend the same knowledge processing pipeline without changing the core architecture.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe Knowledge Processing \u0026 Document Intelligence Architecture defines how BLIE transforms educational resources into structured learning intelligence.\\n\\nThe pipeline shall:\\n\\n1. Accept diverse learning materials.\\n2. Extract educational meaning.\\n3. Identify concepts and relationships.\\n4. Enrich the student's Personal Learning Knowledge Graph.\\n5. Improve learning recommendations through continuous knowledge growth.\\n\\nThe permanent asset is **not the uploaded document**.\\n\\nThe permanent asset is the **student's continuously evolving Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG)**, enriched and maintained by BLIE throughout the entire university journey.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume F8**\\n:::\\n\\nBismillah.\\n\\nAt this stage, I believe the core intelligence architecture is taking shape. The next volume, **F9 – BLIE Retrieval \u0026 Reasoning Architecture (RAG + Knowledge Graph)**, is where the entire system comes together. It will define how BLIE combines:\\n\\n- The student's **PLKG** (personal understanding),\\n- The **Global Knowledge Graph** (curriculum and academic concepts),\\n- Retrieved learning resources,\\n- Long-term memory,\\n- And the selected AI model,\\n\\nto produce personalized explanations with minimal hallucination and high educational relevance. BLIE remembers what is meaningful for the student's learning journey.**\\n\\nThe memory system must be intelligent, structured, private, and connected to the student's **Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG).**\\n\\n---\\n\\n:::writing{variant=\\\"document\\\" id=\\\"57391\\\"}\\n# AI Study Buddy\\n\\n# Volume F7 – BLIE Memory Architecture \u0026 Personalization Engine\\n\\n**Version:** 1.0 (Architecture Freeze)\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 1. Introduction\\n\\nThe BLIE Memory Architecture defines how the Buddy Learning Intelligent Engine remembers, understands, and adapts to each student's learning journey.\\n\\nThe purpose of memory is not simply to store conversation history.\\n\\nMemory enables BLIE to understand:\\n\\n- What the student has learned.\\n- What the student understands.\\n- What the student struggles with.\\n- How the student learns best.\\n- What knowledge should be reinforced next.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Memory Vision\\n\\nTo create a lifelong academic memory that grows with the student from the first semester until graduation.\\n\\nThe student's learning history becomes an intelligent foundation for continuous personalized guidance.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Memory Architecture Principle\\n\\nBLIE memory consists of four layers:\\n\\n```text\\nShort-Term Memory\\n\\n        ↓\\n\\nLearning Session Memory\\n\\n        ↓\\n\\nAcademic Memory\\n\\n        ↓\\n\\nPersonal Learning Intelligence\\n```\\n\\nEach layer has a different purpose.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Short-Term Memory\\n\\n## Purpose\\n\\nSupports the current learning interaction.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nStudent:\\n\\n\\\"Explain this formula.\\\"\\n\\nBLIE remembers:\\n\\n- Current conversation.\\n- Current topic.\\n- Current uploaded material.\\n- Current question context.\\n\\n---\\n\\nCharacteristics:\\n\\n- Temporary.\\n- Fast access.\\n- Automatically expires.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Learning Session Memory\\n\\n## Purpose\\n\\nCaptures meaningful information during a study session.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\nStudent studies:\\n\\n\\\"Database Normalization\\\"\\n\\nBLIE records:\\n\\n- Topics reviewed.\\n- Questions asked.\\n- Concepts explored.\\n- Confusion points.\\n- Learning outcomes.\\n\\n---\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```text\\nStudy Session\\n\\nSubject:\\nDatabase Systems\\n\\nTopic:\\nNormalization\\n\\nStudent Difficulty:\\nFunctional Dependency\\n\\nRecommended Review:\\n1NF → 2NF → 3NF\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Academic Memory\\n\\n## Purpose\\n\\nMaintains long-term educational history.\\n\\nThis includes:\\n\\n- Completed subjects.\\n- Learned concepts.\\n- Academic progress.\\n- Assessment history.\\n- Knowledge growth.\\n\\nAcademic memory connects directly with PLKG.\\n\\n---\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```text\\nSemester 1\\n\\nProgramming Fundamentals\\n\\nConcepts:\\n- Variables\\n- Functions\\n- Loops\\n\\n\\nSemester 2\\n\\nData Structures\\n\\nRequires:\\n- Functions\\n- Algorithms\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Personal Learning Intelligence Memory\\n\\nThis is the highest-level memory layer.\\n\\nBLIE learns about the student's learning characteristics.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n## Learning Strengths\\n\\nStudent understands:\\n\\n- Visual explanations.\\n- Practical examples.\\n- Step-by-step reasoning.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning Challenges\\n\\nStudent struggles with:\\n\\n- Abstract concepts.\\n- Mathematical derivations.\\n- Memorization-heavy topics.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning Preferences\\n\\nStudent prefers:\\n\\n- Short explanations.\\n- Detailed explanations.\\n- Examples first.\\n- Theory first.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Memory Relationship with PLKG\\n\\nMemory does not exist separately.\\n\\nIt enriches the student's Personal Learning Knowledge Graph.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nKnowledge Node:\\n\\n```text\\nIntegration\\n```\\n\\nStudent Memory:\\n\\n```text\\nStudent understands:\\n70%\\n\\nLast studied:\\n2 weeks ago\\n\\nCommon mistake:\\nIntegration limits\\n\\nConfidence:\\nMedium\\n```\\n\\nTogether:\\n\\n```text\\nPLKG\\n\\n+\\n\\nStudent Memory\\n\\n=\\n\\nPersonal Learning Intelligence\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Knowledge Mastery Model\\n\\nBLIE tracks understanding using multiple signals.\\n\\nSignals include:\\n\\n- Questions asked.\\n- Quiz results.\\n- Revision frequency.\\n- Explanation ability.\\n- Mistake patterns.\\n\\n---\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nConcept:\\n\\n\\\"Recursion\\\"\\n\\nMastery:\\n\\n```text\\nExposure:\\n5 times\\n\\nPractice:\\n20 questions\\n\\nConfidence:\\n80%\\n\\nStatus:\\nDeveloping Mastery\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Forgetting \u0026 Reinforcement Intelligence\\n\\nBLIE supports knowledge retention.\\n\\nThe system monitors:\\n\\n- Time since learning.\\n- Previous mistakes.\\n- Importance of concept.\\n- Exam relevance.\\n\\n---\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nBLIE detects:\\n\\n```text\\nStudent learned:\\n\\nCalculus Integration\\n\\n3 months ago\\n\\nNo revision detected\\n```\\n\\nRecommendation:\\n\\n\\\"Review integration concepts before advanced calculus.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Personalization Engine\\n\\nBLIE uses memory to personalize:\\n\\n## Explanations\\n\\nSame question:\\n\\nStudent A:\\n\\nNeeds basic explanation.\\n\\nStudent B:\\n\\nReady for advanced explanation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning Path\\n\\nStudent A:\\n\\nNeeds prerequisite review.\\n\\nStudent B:\\n\\nCan advance directly.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Revision Strategy\\n\\nStudent A:\\n\\nNeeds more practice.\\n\\nStudent B:\\n\\nNeeds deeper application.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Memory Update Pipeline\\n\\nEvery meaningful interaction follows:\\n\\n```text\\nStudent Interaction\\n\\n↓\\n\\nMemory Analysis\\n\\n↓\\n\\nDetermine Importance\\n\\n↓\\n\\nUpdate Memory\\n\\n↓\\n\\nUpdate PLKG\\n\\n↓\\n\\nImprove Future Guidance\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Memory Importance Classification\\n\\nNot every interaction becomes permanent memory.\\n\\nBLIE classifies:\\n\\n## Temporary\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n\\\"Explain this sentence.\\\"\\n\\nNo long-term storage.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Useful\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n\\\"Student struggles with recursion.\\\"\\n\\nStore learning insight.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Important\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n\\\"Student repeatedly struggles with programming logic.\\\"\\n\\nCreate long-term learning pattern.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Memory Privacy Architecture\\n\\nStudent memory is private.\\n\\nProtected data:\\n\\n- Learning weaknesses.\\n- Study behaviour.\\n- Academic history.\\n- AI conversations.\\n\\nBLIE can use memory only for that student's learning assistance.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Memory Optimization\\n\\nLong-term memory must remain efficient.\\n\\nThe system uses:\\n\\n- Summarization.\\n- Importance scoring.\\n- Knowledge consolidation.\\n- Duplicate removal.\\n\\nThe goal:\\n\\nMore intelligence with less storage.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Future AI Evolution\\n\\nFuture versions may support:\\n\\n- Personal AI tutor personality.\\n- Voice learning companion.\\n- Predictive study planning.\\n- Adaptive learning strategies.\\n- Offline personal AI memory.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Architecture Freeze\\n\\nBLIE Memory Architecture defines AI Study Buddy as a true learning companion.\\n\\nThe memory system:\\n\\n1. Preserves meaningful learning history.\\n2. Understands student progress.\\n3. Personalizes educational support.\\n4. Enriches the Personal Learning Knowledge Graph.\\n5. Evolves throughout the student's university journey.\\n\\nThe ultimate goal:\\n\\n**BLIE should know the student's learning journey as a trusted study companion, while keeping the student in full control of their academic memory.**\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume F7**\\n:::\\n\\nBismillah. BLIE may assist, but ownership remains with the learner.**\\n\\n---\\n\\n:::writing{variant=\\\"document\\\" id=\\\"18462\\\"}\\n# AI Study Buddy\\n\\n# Volume F6 – Security, Privacy \u0026 Student Data Protection Architecture\\n\\n**Version:** 1.0 (Architecture Freeze)\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 1. Introduction\\n\\nAI Study Buddy is a personal AI learning companion that stores and processes a student's academic knowledge journey.\\n\\nThe platform manages:\\n\\n- Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG)\\n- Lecture materials\\n- Personal notes\\n- AI conversations\\n- Learning history\\n- Academic progress\\n- Study behaviour\\n\\nSecurity and privacy are fundamental requirements to ensure trust between the student and the platform.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Security Vision\\n\\nTo create a trusted learning environment where students can safely build their lifelong academic memory with confidence that their knowledge remains private, protected, and under their control.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Security Principles\\n\\n## Student Data Ownership\\n\\nThe student owns:\\n\\n- Their learning graph.\\n- Their notes.\\n- Their uploaded materials.\\n- Their learning history.\\n- Their AI interactions.\\n\\nThe platform provides intelligence but does not own the student's academic memory.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Privacy by Design\\n\\nPrivacy must be considered from the beginning of every feature.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- New database tables.\\n- AI pipelines.\\n- Data sharing.\\n- Study groups.\\n- Analytics.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Minimum Data Collection\\n\\nThe system should only collect information necessary to provide learning services.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Secure by Default\\n\\nEvery feature must begin with secure settings.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Multi-Tenant Security Model\\n\\nAI Study Buddy uses strict student data isolation.\\n\\nArchitecture:\\n\\n```text\\nStudent A\\n\\nPrivate PLKG\\nPrivate Notes\\nPrivate AI Memory\\n\\n\\n≠\\n\\n\\nStudent B\\n\\nPrivate PLKG\\nPrivate Notes\\nPrivate AI Memory\\n```\\n\\nNo student should ever access another student's private learning data.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Identity \u0026 Authentication Security\\n\\nThe platform manages:\\n\\n- Account identity.\\n- Login security.\\n- Device sessions.\\n- Subscription access.\\n\\nSupported methods:\\n\\n- Email authentication.\\n- Social login.\\n- Device authentication.\\n\\nSecurity requirements:\\n\\n- Secure password handling.\\n- Session expiration.\\n- Device management.\\n- Account recovery.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Authorization Architecture\\n\\nEvery request must pass authorization checks.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nStudent asks:\\n\\n\\\"Show my weak topics.\\\"\\n\\nSystem verifies:\\n\\n```text\\nAuthenticated User\\n\\n↓\\n\\nStudent Identity\\n\\n↓\\n\\nOwnership Check\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAccess PLKG\\n\\n↓\\n\\nReturn Data\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Data Protection Architecture\\n\\nData is protected at multiple layers.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Data in Transit\\n\\nProtection:\\n\\n- Encrypted communication.\\n- Secure API connections.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Data at Rest\\n\\nProtection:\\n\\n- Encrypted databases.\\n- Protected document storage.\\n- Secure backups.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Sensitive Data Separation\\n\\nSeparate:\\n\\n- Identity data.\\n- Learning data.\\n- AI memory.\\n- Payment information.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. PLKG Privacy Architecture\\n\\nThe Personal Learning Knowledge Graph requires special protection.\\n\\nThe PLKG contains:\\n\\n- What the student knows.\\n- What the student does not understand.\\n- Learning weaknesses.\\n- Academic progress.\\n\\nTherefore:\\n\\n```text\\nStudent PLKG\\n\\n=\\n\\nPrivate Intellectual Property\\n```\\n\\nAccess:\\n\\nAllowed:\\n\\n- Student.\\n- BLIE for that student.\\n\\nNot allowed:\\n\\n- Other students.\\n- Unrelated services.\\n- External users.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. AI Privacy Architecture\\n\\nBLIE must respect strict data boundaries.\\n\\nWhen processing:\\n\\nStudent Question\\n\\n↓\\n\\nBLIE receives:\\n\\nAllowed:\\n\\n- Student's PLKG.\\n- Relevant curriculum knowledge.\\n- Student learning history.\\n\\nNot allowed:\\n\\n- Other students' conversations.\\n- Other students' notes.\\n- Unrelated personal data.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. AI Data Usage Policy\\n\\nStudent learning data should not automatically become shared AI training data.\\n\\nThe architecture separates:\\n\\n## Personal Learning Data\\n\\nPrivate:\\n\\n- Notes.\\n- Conversations.\\n- Progress.\\n- Mistakes.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Global Knowledge Data\\n\\nShared:\\n\\n- Academic concepts.\\n- Curriculum structures.\\n- Public educational resources.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Study Group Privacy\\n\\nStudy Groups introduce controlled sharing.\\n\\nStudents may share:\\n\\n- Selected notes.\\n- Learning resources.\\n- Study discussions.\\n\\nHowever:\\n\\nPrivate PLKG remains private.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nShared:\\n\\n\\\"Summary of Chapter 5\\\"\\n\\nPrivate:\\n\\n\\\"My weak understanding of Chapter 5\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Document Security\\n\\nUploaded materials require protection.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Lecture PDFs.\\n- Images.\\n- Personal notes.\\n\\nRequirements:\\n\\n- Private storage.\\n- Access-controlled URLs.\\n- Permission validation.\\n- Secure deletion.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Data Lifecycle Management\\n\\nStudent data follows a lifecycle.\\n\\n## Creation\\n\\nStudent uploads or creates learning content.\\n\\n↓\\n\\n## Processing\\n\\nBLIE analyses and structures knowledge.\\n\\n↓\\n\\n## Usage\\n\\nStudent receives learning assistance.\\n\\n↓\\n\\n## Retention\\n\\nKnowledge remains available throughout academic journey.\\n\\n↓\\n\\n## Deletion\\n\\nStudent may request removal.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Student Control Features\\n\\nStudents should have control over:\\n\\n- Export their learning data.\\n- Delete materials.\\n- Delete account.\\n- Manage sharing permissions.\\n- Review AI memory.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Compliance Direction\\n\\nThe architecture should support relevant privacy requirements including:\\n\\n- Personal data protection principles.\\n- User consent management.\\n- Data access rights.\\n- Data deletion rights.\\n- Secure processing practices.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 16. Security Monitoring\\n\\nThe platform should monitor:\\n\\n- Unauthorized access attempts.\\n- Suspicious activity.\\n- Account security events.\\n- Data access logs.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 17. Future Security Expansion\\n\\nFuture capabilities may include:\\n\\n- Advanced encryption.\\n- Privacy-preserving AI processing.\\n- Local AI memory.\\n- Student-controlled AI models.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Architecture Freeze\\n\\nAI Study Buddy security architecture is built on these principles:\\n\\n1. Student learning memory belongs to the student.\\n2. Every student's PLKG is private and isolated.\\n3. BLIE only accesses authorized student context.\\n4. Personal learning data is not shared without permission.\\n5. Security and privacy are embedded into every layer.\\n\\nThe foundation of trust:\\n\\n**AI Study Buddy protects not only student data, but the student's intellectual journey.**\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume F6**\\n:::\\n\\nBismillah. Introduction\\n\\nAI Study Buddy is designed as a global consumer AI education platform.\\n\\nThe infrastructure must support:\\n\\n- Millions of students.\\n- Continuous learning activity.\\n- Large document processing.\\n- Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG) growth.\\n- AI-powered assistance.\\n\\nThe architecture must balance:\\n\\n- Intelligence quality.\\n- Response speed.\\n- Operational cost.\\n- Scalability.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Infrastructure Philosophy\\n\\nThe platform follows a layered intelligence approach.\\n\\n```text\\nSimple Tasks\\n\\n↓\\n\\nEfficient Models\\n\\n↓\\n\\nComplex Tasks\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAdvanced AI Models\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCritical Reasoning\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPremium Intelligence\\n```\\n\\nNot every interaction requires the most expensive AI model.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Infrastructure Architecture\\n\\nHigh-level structure:\\n\\n```text\\n                 Student Apps\\n\\n                     │\\n\\n                API Gateway\\n\\n                     │\\n\\n        ┌────────────┴────────────┐\\n\\n        BLIE Orchestration Layer\\n\\n                     │\\n\\n    ┌────────────────┼────────────────┐\\n\\nKnowledge Services   AI Services   Data Services\\n\\n                     │\\n\\n              Cloud Infrastructure\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Core Infrastructure Components\\n\\n## Application Servers\\n\\nResponsible for:\\n\\n- User requests.\\n- Authentication.\\n- Subscription management.\\n- Application logic.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Database Infrastructure\\n\\nStores:\\n\\n- Student profiles.\\n- Academic information.\\n- Learning history.\\n- PLKG data.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Object Storage\\n\\nStores:\\n\\n- Lecture PDFs.\\n- Images.\\n- Documents.\\n- Generated learning materials.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## AI Processing Infrastructure\\n\\nHandles:\\n\\n- Document understanding.\\n- Knowledge extraction.\\n- AI conversations.\\n- Graph updates.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. AI Cost Management Strategy\\n\\nBLIE uses AI routing.\\n\\nEvery request is classified:\\n\\n## Level 1 — Simple Intelligence\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Flashcard generation.\\n- Short summaries.\\n- Basic explanations.\\n\\nUses:\\n\\n- Small language models.\\n- Cached responses.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Level 2 — Learning Intelligence\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Concept explanation.\\n- Revision planning.\\n- Knowledge connection.\\n\\nUses:\\n\\n- Medium AI models.\\n- Retrieval from PLKG.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Level 3 — Advanced Reasoning\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Complex problem solving.\\n- Deep subject analysis.\\n- Learning strategy.\\n\\nUses:\\n\\n- Advanced AI models.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. AI Model Strategy\\n\\nBLIE should support multiple AI providers.\\n\\nArchitecture:\\n\\n```text\\nBLIE\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAI Router\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSmall Model\\nMedium Model\\nLarge Model\\nLocal Model\\n```\\n\\nBenefits:\\n\\n- Cost control.\\n- Flexibility.\\n- Future upgrades.\\n- Reduced dependency.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Knowledge Retrieval Before AI Generation\\n\\nA major cost reduction principle:\\n\\nDo not send everything to AI.\\n\\nInstead:\\n\\n```text\\nStudent Question\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPLKG Search\\n\\n↓\\n\\nRelevant Knowledge Retrieval\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSmall Context\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAI Response\\n```\\n\\nBenefits:\\n\\n- Lower token usage.\\n- Faster responses.\\n- More personalized answers.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Document Processing Economics\\n\\nStudent uploads:\\n\\nLecture PDF\\n\\nThe pipeline:\\n\\n```text\\nUpload\\n\\n↓\\n\\nStorage\\n\\n↓\\n\\nProcessing Queue\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAI Extraction\\n\\n↓\\n\\nKnowledge Update\\n```\\n\\nProcessing should be asynchronous.\\n\\nThe student does not need to wait.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Background Processing\\n\\nHeavy tasks run through queues.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- PDF analysis.\\n- OCR.\\n- Knowledge extraction.\\n- Flashcard generation.\\n- Graph enrichment.\\n\\nArchitecture:\\n\\n```text\\nTask Queue\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAI Workers\\n\\n↓\\n\\nDatabase Update\\n\\n↓\\n\\nStudent Notification\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Storage Cost Strategy\\n\\nDifferent data types require different storage.\\n\\n## Hot Data\\n\\nFrequently accessed:\\n\\n- Current semester.\\n- Recent notes.\\n- Active subjects.\\n\\nFast storage.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Warm Data\\n\\nOccasionally accessed:\\n\\n- Previous semesters.\\n- Older materials.\\n\\nLower-cost storage.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Archive Data\\n\\nLong-term academic memory.\\n\\nOptimized for cost.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Subscription Economics\\n\\nThe platform supports:\\n\\n## Free Tier\\n\\nPurpose:\\n\\n- User acquisition.\\n- Product discovery.\\n\\nLimits:\\n\\n- AI usage.\\n- Storage.\\n- Processing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Premium Tier\\n\\nProvides:\\n\\n- Higher AI usage.\\n- Larger PLKG.\\n- More document processing.\\n- Advanced learning features.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Study Group Tier\\n\\nProvides:\\n\\n- Shared learning resources.\\n- Group collaboration.\\n- Reduced subscription cost.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Cost Optimization Through Shared Intelligence\\n\\nThe platform separates:\\n\\n## Global Intelligence\\n\\nShared:\\n\\n- Curriculum knowledge.\\n- Common concepts.\\n- Subject structures.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Personal Intelligence\\n\\nPrivate:\\n\\n- Student understanding.\\n- Learning history.\\n- Personal notes.\\n\\nThis dramatically reduces repeated processing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Infrastructure Scaling Model\\n\\nGrowth stages:\\n\\n## Stage 1 — MVP\\n\\nSupports:\\n\\n- Thousands of students.\\n\\nArchitecture:\\n\\n- Managed cloud services.\\n- Limited AI processing.\\n- Simple scaling.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Stage 2 — Growth\\n\\nSupports:\\n\\n- Hundreds of thousands of students.\\n\\nAdd:\\n\\n- AI queues.\\n- Worker scaling.\\n- Better caching.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Stage 3 — Global Scale\\n\\nSupports:\\n\\n- Millions of students.\\n\\nAdd:\\n\\n- Distributed services.\\n- Regional deployment.\\n- AI optimization.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Local AI Opportunity\\n\\nFuture versions may introduce local intelligence.\\n\\nPossible uses:\\n\\n- Offline explanations.\\n- Flashcard generation.\\n- Personal memory search.\\n\\nArchitecture:\\n\\n```text\\nCloud BLIE\\n\\n+\\n\\nLocal Student AI Assistant\\n\\n+\\n\\nSynchronization\\n```\\n\\nHowever, the primary architecture remains cloud-based for accessibility.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Infrastructure Success Criteria\\n\\nA successful infrastructure enables:\\n\\n- Affordable subscription pricing.\\n- Reliable AI assistance.\\n- Fast response times.\\n- Sustainable operational costs.\\n- Growth from MVP to millions of students.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Architecture Freeze\\n\\nAI Study Buddy infrastructure follows these principles:\\n\\n1. AI cost must scale with business revenue.\\n2. Expensive AI reasoning is used selectively.\\n3. Knowledge retrieval reduces AI dependency.\\n4. Shared intelligence reduces duplication.\\n5. Background processing improves efficiency.\\n6. The architecture supports millions of students sustainably.\\n\\nThe goal:\\n\\n**Deliver a powerful personal AI learning companion while maintaining healthy economics for a global student subscription platform.**\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume F5**\\n:::\\n\\nBismillah. Freeze)\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 1. Introduction\\n\\nAI Study Buddy is designed as a multi-tenant cloud platform supporting millions of individual students.\\n\\nEach student operates within their own private learning environment while sharing common platform infrastructure.\\n\\nThe architecture enables:\\n\\n- Personal AI learning companions.\\n- Individual Personal Learning Knowledge Graphs (PLKG).\\n- Shared academic intelligence.\\n- Secure student data separation.\\n- Scalable AI processing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Multi-Tenant Philosophy\\n\\nAI Study Buddy follows a **student-centric multi-tenant architecture**.\\n\\nA tenant represents an individual student.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nTenant A\\n(Student A)\\n\\n    Personal PLKG\\n    Personal Notes\\n    Personal History\\n    Personal AI Memory\\n\\n\\nTenant B\\n(Student B)\\n\\n    Personal PLKG\\n    Personal Notes\\n    Personal History\\n    Personal AI Memory\\n```\\n\\nEach student's learning world is isolated.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Shared Intelligence Layer\\n\\nAlthough students have private learning graphs, the platform maintains shared knowledge foundations.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n```\\nGlobal Knowledge Layer\\n\\n    Mathematics\\n    Programming\\n    Physics\\n    Engineering\\n    Computer Science\\n\\n\\n+\\n\\nPersonal Learning Layer\\n\\n\\nStudent Understanding\\nStudent Notes\\nStudent Progress\\nStudent Mistakes\\n```\\n\\nThis prevents duplication.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Cloud Architecture Overview\\n\\nHigh-level architecture:\\n\\n```\\n                 Student Apps\\n\\n        Mobile        Web        Tablet\\n\\n                    │\\n\\n             API Gateway\\n\\n                    │\\n\\n        Application Services\\n\\n                    │\\n\\n              BLIE Engine\\n\\n                    │\\n\\n     ┌──────────────┴──────────────┐\\n\\n     Global Knowledge Layer     Personal PLKG\\n\\n                    │\\n\\n            Data Infrastructure\\n\\n                    │\\n\\n              Cloud Platform\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Tenant Isolation Architecture\\n\\nEvery request must carry:\\n\\n```\\nstudent_id\\ntenant_id\\nsession_id\\n```\\n\\nAll data operations must respect ownership boundaries.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nA student's query:\\n\\n\\\"Explain recursion\\\"\\n\\nmust access:\\n\\nAllowed:\\n\\n```\\nStudent's PLKG\\n+\\nShared Programming Knowledge\\n+\\nStudent Learning History\\n```\\n\\nNot allowed:\\n\\n```\\nOther student's notes\\nOther student's mistakes\\nOther student's conversations\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Database Multi-Tenant Design\\n\\nThe system separates data into:\\n\\n## Shared Tables\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n```\\nsubjects\\n\\ncurriculum\\n\\nconcept_library\\n\\nlearning_templates\\n```\\n\\nUsed by all students.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Tenant Tables\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n```\\nstudent_profile\\n\\nstudent_notes\\n\\nstudent_progress\\n\\nstudent_conversations\\n\\nstudent_plkg\\n```\\n\\nPrivate to each student.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Scaling Millions of Students\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n10 million students.\\n\\nThe platform does NOT create:\\n\\n```\\n10 million copies of Calculus knowledge.\\n```\\n\\nInstead:\\n\\n```\\nGlobal Calculus Knowledge\\n\\n        +\\n\\n10 million Personal Learning Layers\\n```\\n\\nThis dramatically reduces storage requirements.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. AI Worker Architecture\\n\\nLarge processing tasks use distributed workers.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nAI Job Queue\\n\\n       │\\n\\n ┌─────┼─────┐\\n\\nWorker  Worker  Worker\\n\\n PDF     OCR    Graph\\n\\n       │\\n\\n       BLIE\\n\\n       │\\n\\n       PLKG Update\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Storage Strategy\\n\\nDifferent data types use different storage.\\n\\n## Relational Database\\n\\nFor:\\n\\n- Accounts\\n- Subscriptions\\n- Academic records\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Object Storage\\n\\nFor:\\n\\n- PDFs\\n- Images\\n- Documents\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Vector Storage\\n\\nFor:\\n\\n- Semantic search\\n- AI retrieval\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Graph Storage\\n\\nFor:\\n\\n- PLKG relationships\\n- Concept networks\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Students may read notes on mobile, review on a laptop, upload materials later, or study in places with unstable internet.\\n\\nThe core principle:\\n\\n\u003e **The student's Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG) must remain available, consistent, and continuously evolving across devices while protecting ownership of personal learning data.**\\n\\n---\\n\\n:::writing{variant=\\\"document\\\" id=\\\"29746\\\"}\\n# AI Study Buddy\\n\\n# Volume F3 – Synchronization \u0026 Offline Architecture\\n\\n**Version:** 1.0 (Architecture Freeze)\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 1. Introduction\\n\\nAI Study Buddy is designed as a personal learning companion that students can use throughout their university journey.\\n\\nBecause learning happens anywhere and anytime, the platform must support:\\n\\n- Mobile-first usage.\\n- Offline learning capability.\\n- Multi-device access.\\n- Reliable synchronization.\\n- Continuous PLKG growth.\\n\\nThe synchronization architecture ensures that the student's learning memory remains consistent across all devices.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Architecture Principles\\n\\nThe synchronization system follows five principles:\\n\\n## Student First\\n\\nThe student's learning data must always be preserved.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Offline Capable\\n\\nStudents can continue learning without constant internet connectivity.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Cloud Intelligence\\n\\nHeavy AI processing occurs through cloud services when available.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Local Learning Access\\n\\nFrequently used learning data should remain available locally.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Conflict Safety\\n\\nNo learning progress should be accidentally lost during synchronization.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Device Architecture\\n\\nAI Study Buddy operates across:\\n\\n```text\\nMobile App\\n\\n      ↕\\n\\nWeb Application\\n\\n      ↕\\n\\nCloud Platform\\n```\\n\\nEach device maintains a local learning environment.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Local Data Layer\\n\\nThe mobile application stores local data for offline operation.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n## Cached Knowledge\\n\\n- Recently accessed concepts\\n- Subject summaries\\n- Flashcards\\n- Revision plans\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning Activity Queue\\n\\nStores activities performed offline:\\n\\n- Notes created\\n- Questions asked\\n- Quiz attempts\\n- Learning progress\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Temporary Materials\\n\\nStores:\\n\\n- Recently opened documents\\n- Images\\n- Study resources\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Cloud Data Layer\\n\\nThe cloud maintains the authoritative learning system.\\n\\nStores:\\n\\n- Student profile\\n- Complete PLKG\\n- Learning history\\n- Documents\\n- AI conversations\\n- Progress records\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Synchronization Flow\\n\\nThe synchronization cycle:\\n\\n```text\\nLocal Device\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSync Queue\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCloud Synchronization Service\\n\\n↓\\n\\nConflict Resolution\\n\\n↓\\n\\nDatabase Update\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPLKG Update\\n\\n↓\\n\\nDevice Refresh\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Offline Learning Mode\\n\\nWhen internet is unavailable, students can still:\\n\\n- Read downloaded materials.\\n- Review flashcards.\\n- Explore cached knowledge.\\n- Write notes.\\n- Complete quizzes.\\n- Record learning activities.\\n\\nThe application stores changes locally until synchronization is available.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Sync Queue System\\n\\nEvery offline activity creates a synchronization event.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nStudent creates a note:\\n\\n```text\\nNew Note Created\\n\\n↓\\n\\nLocal Storage\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSync Event Generated\\n\\n↓\\n\\nWaiting for Connection\\n\\n↓\\n\\nUploaded to Cloud\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Conflict Resolution\\n\\nConflicts may happen when:\\n\\n- Multiple devices update the same information.\\n- Offline changes happen simultaneously.\\n\\nThe system resolves conflicts using:\\n\\n## Timestamp Priority\\n\\nLatest valid update is considered.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Data Type Rules\\n\\nDifferent data types use different strategies.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nNotes:\\n\\nMerge changes.\\n\\nLearning Progress:\\n\\nPreserve history.\\n\\nPLKG:\\n\\nCombine knowledge updates.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. PLKG Synchronization\\n\\nThe Personal Learning Knowledge Graph requires special handling.\\n\\nThe graph is not simply overwritten.\\n\\nInstead:\\n\\n```text\\nNew Knowledge Event\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCompare Existing Graph\\n\\n↓\\n\\nIdentify Existing Nodes\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCreate Relationships\\n\\n↓\\n\\nUpdate Student Learning State\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nMobile:\\n\\nStudent learns:\\n\\n\\\"Recursion\\\"\\n\\nLaptop:\\n\\nStudent completes quiz about:\\n\\n\\\"Recursion\\\"\\n\\nThe system combines:\\n\\n```text\\nStudent\\n\\nunderstands\\n\\nRecursion\\n\\n+\\n\\nQuiz Performance\\n\\n+\\n\\nLearning History\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. AI Processing Synchronization\\n\\nAI processing may happen in different environments.\\n\\n## Online Mode\\n\\nFull BLIE capability:\\n\\n- Document analysis.\\n- Knowledge extraction.\\n- Graph updates.\\n- AI reasoning.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Offline Mode\\n\\nLimited local capability:\\n\\n- Cached knowledge access.\\n- Flashcards.\\n- Notes.\\n- Previous AI responses.\\n\\nWhen online returns:\\n\\n```text\\nPending Learning Events\\n\\n↓\\n\\nBLIE Processing\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPLKG Update\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Document Synchronization\\n\\nLearning materials follow:\\n\\n```text\\nUpload\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCloud Storage\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAI Processing\\n\\n↓\\n\\nKnowledge Extraction\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPLKG Connection\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAvailable Everywhere\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Security Principles\\n\\nSynchronization must protect:\\n\\n- Student privacy.\\n- Learning history.\\n- Personal knowledge graph.\\n- Uploaded materials.\\n\\nRequirements:\\n\\n- Secure authentication.\\n- Encrypted communication.\\n- Controlled device access.\\n- Private student data isolation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Scalability Considerations\\n\\nThe system must support millions of students.\\n\\nThe architecture separates:\\n\\n## Shared Data\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Curriculum structures.\\n- Common subject knowledge.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Personal Data\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Student notes.\\n- Learning history.\\n- Personal PLKG.\\n\\nThis avoids unnecessary duplication.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 15. Long-Term Vision\\n\\nThe synchronization system enables AI Study Buddy to become a lifelong learning companion.\\n\\nA student's learning memory should follow them:\\n\\n- Across devices.\\n- Across semesters.\\n- Across years.\\n- From university entry until graduation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe synchronization architecture of AI Study Buddy is based on:\\n\\n1. Local-first learning experience.\\n2. Cloud-powered BLIE intelligence.\\n3. Continuous PLKG synchronization.\\n4. Reliable offline operation.\\n5. Secure student-owned learning memory.\\n\\nThe student's Personal Learning Knowledge Graph remains the central asset and must always be preserved during synchronization.\\n\\n---\\n\\n**End of Volume F3**\\n:::\\n\\nBismillah, with this we now have:\\n\\n- **Volume F1** — Database \u0026 Data Model Architecture  \\n- **Volume F2** — BLIE AI Pipeline Architecture  \\n- **Volume F3** — Synchronization \u0026 Offline Architecture  \\n\\nThe next logical technical volume would be:\\n\\n**Volume F4 – Multi-Tenant Cloud Architecture \u0026 Scalability**\\n\\nbecause although the product is B2C, the backend must be designed to support millions of individual student learning graphs we move into the intelligence pipeline of the platform.\\n\\n**Volume F2 – BLIE AI Pipeline Specification** defines how BLIE transforms raw learning materials and student interactions into structured knowledge, personalized understanding, and continuous learning guidance.\\n\\nThe key principle remains:\\n\\n\u003e **BLIE does not simply retrieve information. BLIE understands, connects, and evolves the student's Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG).**\\n\\n---\\n\\n:::writing{variant=\\\"document\\\" id=\\\"86429\\\"}\\n# AI Study Buddy\\n\\n# Volume F2 – BLIE AI Pipeline Specification\\n\\n**Version:** 1.0 (Architecture Freeze)\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 1. Introduction\\n\\nThe **Buddy Learning Intelligent Engine (BLIE)** is responsible for transforming educational information into personalized intelligence.\\n\\nBLIE receives information from:\\n\\n- Curriculum structure\\n- Student learning materials\\n- Student interactions\\n- Assessments\\n- Learning activities\\n\\nIt processes this information, updates the Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG), and provides personalized learning assistance.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. BLIE Architecture Overview\\n\\nThe BLIE pipeline consists of six intelligence stages:\\n\\n```\\nInput Collection\\n\\n↓\\n\\nKnowledge Extraction\\n\\n↓\\n\\nKnowledge Understanding\\n\\n↓\\n\\nKnowledge Graph Update\\n\\n↓\\n\\nLearning Intelligence\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPersonalized Response\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Stage 1 — Input Collection Layer\\n\\nBLIE receives learning inputs from multiple sources.\\n\\n## Academic Inputs\\n\\n- Degree programme\\n- Semester\\n- Subjects\\n- Curriculum structure\\n- Learning objectives\\n\\nThese create the initial learning foundation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Student Inputs\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- PDF lecture notes\\n- Images\\n- Personal notes\\n- Questions\\n- Conversations\\n- Quiz attempts\\n- Assignments\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning Behaviour Inputs\\n\\nBLIE observes:\\n\\n- Topics studied\\n- Time spent learning\\n- Revision frequency\\n- Quiz performance\\n- Areas of difficulty\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Stage 2 — Knowledge Extraction Pipeline\\n\\nWhen a student uploads material:\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nLecture PDF\\n\\n```\\nPDF/Image\\n\\n↓\\n\\nDocument Processing\\n\\n↓\\n\\nText Extraction\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSemantic Analysis\\n\\n↓\\n\\nConcept Identification\\n\\n↓\\n\\nKnowledge Mapping\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Document Understanding\\n\\nBLIE identifies:\\n\\n- Topics\\n- Concepts\\n- Definitions\\n- Formulas\\n- Examples\\n- Relationships\\n- Important explanations\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nInput:\\n\\n\\\"Binary Search Tree is a data structure where each node has values smaller on the left and larger on the right.\\\"\\n\\nBLIE extracts:\\n\\n```\\nBinary Search Tree\\n\\nbelongs_to\\n\\nData Structures\\n\\nrequires\\n\\nTree Concept\\n\\nrelated_to\\n\\nSearching Algorithm\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Stage 3 — Knowledge Understanding Layer\\n\\nExtraction alone is not enough.\\n\\nBLIE must understand relationships.\\n\\nIt identifies:\\n\\n## Concept Relationships\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nIntegration\\n\\nrequires\\n\\nDifferentiation\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Subject Relationships\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nMachine Learning\\n\\nrequires\\n\\nStatistics\\n\\nrequires\\n\\nProbability\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning Dependencies\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nProgramming Objects\\n\\nrequires\\n\\nFunctions\\n\\nrequires\\n\\nVariables\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Stage 4 — PLKG Update Pipeline\\n\\nAfter understanding information, BLIE updates the student's Personal Learning Knowledge Graph.\\n\\nThe update process:\\n\\n```\\nNew Knowledge\\n\\n↓\\n\\nFind Existing Concepts\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCreate New Nodes\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCreate Relationships\\n\\n↓\\n\\nUpdate Student Understanding\\n\\n↓\\n\\nStore Learning History\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nBefore:\\n\\n```\\nStudent\\n\\nknows\\n\\nFunctions\\n```\\n\\nAfter learning:\\n\\n```\\nStudent\\n\\nknows\\n\\nFunctions\\n\\n↓\\n\\nunderstands\\n\\nRecursion\\n\\n↓\\n\\npreparing_for\\n\\nAlgorithms\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Stage 5 — BLIE Reasoning Engine\\n\\nThis is where BLIE becomes intelligent.\\n\\nWhen a student asks:\\n\\n\u003e \\\"Why don't I understand this topic?\\\"\\n\\nBLIE does not only search documents.\\n\\nIt analyses:\\n\\n- Current topic\\n- Previous knowledge\\n- Related concepts\\n- Learning history\\n- Assessment results\\n- Known weaknesses\\n\\n---\\n\\nReasoning flow:\\n\\n```\\nStudent Question\\n\\n↓\\n\\nIntent Understanding\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPLKG Exploration\\n\\n↓\\n\\nKnowledge Gap Detection\\n\\n↓\\n\\nContext Assembly\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAI Reasoning\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPersonalized Explanation\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Learning Preparation Pipeline\\n\\nA unique capability of AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nBefore a topic starts:\\n\\n```\\nUpcoming Topic\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCurriculum Graph Analysis\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPrerequisite Identification\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCompare Student PLKG\\n\\n↓\\n\\nFind Missing Knowledge\\n\\n↓\\n\\nGenerate Preparation Plan\\n```\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nUpcoming:\\n\\n\\\"Neural Networks\\\"\\n\\nBLIE identifies:\\n\\nRequired:\\n\\n```\\nLinear Algebra\\nProbability\\nPython\\n```\\n\\nStudent status:\\n\\n```\\nLinear Algebra 80%\\n\\nProbability 45%\\n\\nPython 90%\\n```\\n\\nBLIE recommends:\\n\\n\\\"Review probability concepts before starting Neural Networks.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. AI Tutor Pipeline\\n\\nWhen students request help:\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n\\\"Explain recursion.\\\"\\n\\nBLIE:\\n\\n1. Finds the concept.\\n2. Checks previous understanding.\\n3. Determines appropriate explanation level.\\n4. Provides examples.\\n5. Updates learning state.\\n\\nResponse adapts to the individual student.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Revision Intelligence Pipeline\\n\\nBLIE creates personalized revision activities.\\n\\nInputs:\\n\\n- Knowledge graph\\n- Exam date\\n- Learning progress\\n- Weak concepts\\n\\nOutputs:\\n\\n- Flashcards\\n- Quizzes\\n- Summary notes\\n- Revision plans\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Assessment Intelligence Pipeline\\n\\nBLIE analyses learning performance.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nQuiz result:\\n\\n```\\nData Structures\\n\\nScore: 55%\\n```\\n\\nBLIE updates:\\n\\n```\\nStudent\\n\\nstruggles_with\\n\\nTree Traversal\\n```\\n\\nThen:\\n\\n- Recommend revision.\\n- Generate practice questions.\\n- Link prerequisite concepts.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Memory Pipeline\\n\\nBLIE maintains long-term learning memory.\\n\\nMemory types:\\n\\n## Academic Memory\\n\\n- Subjects\\n- Concepts\\n- Notes\\n- Learning history\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning Behaviour Memory\\n\\n- Preferred learning style\\n- Frequently studied topics\\n- Weak areas\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Progress Memory\\n\\n- Mastery level\\n- Improvements\\n- Achievements\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. AI Model Architecture Principle\\n\\nBLIE should not depend on a single AI model.\\n\\nThe architecture separates:\\n\\n## Intelligence Layer\\n\\nResponsible for:\\n\\n- Reasoning\\n- Planning\\n- Personalization\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Knowledge Layer\\n\\nResponsible for:\\n\\n- PLKG\\n- Documents\\n- Curriculum\\n\\n---\\n\\n## AI Model Layer\\n\\nResponsible for:\\n\\n- Language understanding\\n- Generation\\n- Summarization\\n\\nThis allows future flexibility in selecting AI models.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 14. Continuous Learning Loop\\n\\nBLIE improves through every interaction:\\n\\n```\\nStudent Learning\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAI Interaction\\n\\n↓\\n\\nKnowledge Update\\n\\n↓\\n\\nBetter Understanding\\n\\n↓\\n\\nBetter Recommendations\\n\\n↓\\n\\nImproved Learning\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Architecture Freeze\\n\\nBLIE is defined as the intelligence engine responsible for:\\n\\n1. Extracting knowledge from learning materials.\\n2. Building and updating the Personal Learning Knowledge Graph.\\n3. Understanding student learning progress.\\n4. Providing proactive learning guidance.\\n5. Supporting preparation, learning, and revision.\\n\\nBLIE is not a question-answering chatbot.\\n\\nBLIE is the intelligence layer that transforms AI Study Buddy into a personal learning companion.\\n:::\\n\\n---\\n\\nWith **Volume F1 (Database \u0026 Data Model)** and **Volume F2 (BLIE AI Pipeline)** completed, the next technical foundation should be:\\n\\n**Volume F3 – Synchronization \u0026 Offline Architecture**\\n\\nbecause a student companion app must work reliably across:\\n- mobile devices,\\n- web,\\n- intermittent internet,\\n- local learning sessions,\\n- cloud AI processing,\\n- and long-term PLKG synchronization.\\n\\nThis will define how the student's \\\"learning brain\\\" stays consistent everywhere. we move into the first technical specification.\\n\\n**Volume F1 – Database \u0026 Data Model Specification** will define the data foundation of AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nThe key architecture decision remains:\\n\\n\u003e **The database must support both traditional application data and the student's evolving Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG).**\\n\\nWe will not design this as only a normal relational database, because the heart of the system is knowledge relationships.\\n\\n---\\n\\n:::writing{variant=\\\"document\\\" id=\\\"73942\\\"}\\n# AI Study Buddy\\n\\n# Volume F1 – Database \u0026 Data Model Specification\\n\\n**Version:** 1.0 (Architecture Freeze)\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 1. Introduction\\n\\nThe AI Study Buddy database architecture is designed to support a long-term personal learning companion for university students.\\n\\nThe system manages:\\n\\n- Student identity\\n- Academic journey\\n- Learning materials\\n- AI interactions\\n- Learning progress\\n- Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG)\\n\\nThe architecture combines structured data storage with graph-based knowledge representation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Database Architecture Principles\\n\\nThe database follows five principles:\\n\\n## Student Ownership\\n\\nEvery student's learning data belongs to that individual student.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Knowledge First\\n\\nInformation should become connected knowledge, not remain isolated files.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Long-Term Memory\\n\\nThe database must preserve the student's academic journey from Semester 1 until graduation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Separation of Data Types\\n\\nOperational data and knowledge graph data are separated but connected.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Scalability\\n\\nThe architecture must support millions of students while maintaining individual personalization.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. High-Level Data Architecture\\n\\nThe system consists of three data layers:\\n\\n```\\nApplication Database\\n\\n        │\\n\\nLearning Knowledge Layer\\n\\n        │\\n\\nPersonal Learning Knowledge Graph\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Application Database Layer\\n\\nThe relational database manages core application functions.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4.1 User Domain\\n\\n## Student\\n\\nStores the student's account and profile.\\n\\nEntity:\\n\\n```\\nStudent\\n```\\n\\nAttributes:\\n\\n- student_id\\n- name\\n- email\\n- profile_image\\n- created_date\\n- subscription_status\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4.2 Academic Domain\\n\\n## Programme\\n\\nRepresents the student's academic programme.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nBachelor Computer Science\\n```\\n\\nAttributes:\\n\\n- programme_id\\n- name\\n- institution\\n- duration\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Semester\\n\\nRepresents academic progression.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nSemester 1\\nSemester 2\\n```\\n\\nAttributes:\\n\\n- semester_id\\n- programme_id\\n- sequence\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Subject\\n\\nRepresents courses taken by students.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nProgramming Fundamentals\\nCalculus\\nDatabase Systems\\n```\\n\\nAttributes:\\n\\n- subject_id\\n- name\\n- code\\n- semester\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Student Subject Enrollment\\n\\nConnects students to subjects.\\n\\n```\\nStudent\\n\\n      enrolled_in\\n\\nSubject\\n```\\n\\nAttributes:\\n\\n- student_id\\n- subject_id\\n- semester\\n- status\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Learning Content Domain\\n\\nStores all learning materials.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning Material\\n\\nRepresents uploaded or generated content.\\n\\nTypes:\\n\\n- PDF\\n- Image\\n- Note\\n- AI Summary\\n- Flashcard\\n- Quiz\\n\\nAttributes:\\n\\n- material_id\\n- student_id\\n- subject_id\\n- type\\n- title\\n- storage_location\\n- created_date\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Document Processing Record\\n\\nTracks AI processing.\\n\\nAttributes:\\n\\n- document_id\\n- extraction_status\\n- OCR_status\\n- processing_date\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Learning Activity Domain\\n\\nTracks student interactions.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning Session\\n\\nRepresents a study session.\\n\\nAttributes:\\n\\n- session_id\\n- student_id\\n- subject_id\\n- start_time\\n- duration\\n\\n---\\n\\n## AI Conversation\\n\\nStores interaction history.\\n\\nAttributes:\\n\\n- conversation_id\\n- student_id\\n- question\\n- response\\n- timestamp\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Assessment Activity\\n\\nTracks learning performance.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n- Quiz result\\n- Practice attempt\\n- Assignment review\\n\\nAttributes:\\n\\n- activity_id\\n- student_id\\n- concept_id\\n- score\\n- date\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG)\\n\\nThe PLKG represents the student's academic intelligence layer.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7.1 Core Graph Entities\\n\\n## Knowledge Node\\n\\nThe fundamental unit of knowledge.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n```\\nDerivative\\n\\nPython Function\\n\\nDatabase Normalization\\n```\\n\\nAttributes:\\n\\n- node_id\\n- name\\n- type\\n- description\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Knowledge Node Types\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n```\\nSubject\\n\\nTopic\\n\\nConcept\\n\\nFormula\\n\\nSkill\\n\\nQuestion\\n\\nMistake\\n\\nResource\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7.2 Knowledge Relationships\\n\\nRelationships define understanding.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n```\\nConcept\\n\\nrequires\\n\\nConcept\\n```\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nIntegration\\n\\nrequires\\n\\nDifferentiation\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n```\\nMaterial\\n\\nexplains\\n\\nConcept\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n```\\nStudent\\n\\nstruggled_with\\n\\nConcept\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n```\\nStudent\\n\\nmastered\\n\\nConcept\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Student Knowledge Profile\\n\\nEach student has a personalized layer.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nStudent\\n\\nunderstands\\n\\nConcept\\n```\\n\\nAttributes:\\n\\n- confidence_level\\n- mastery_score\\n- last_reviewed\\n- learning_status\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Curriculum Knowledge Layer\\n\\nThe system maintains a curriculum foundation.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nComputer Science\\n\\n ├── Programming\\n\\n ├── Algorithms\\n\\n └── Database\\n```\\n\\nThis provides the initial structure when a student enrolls.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Knowledge Evolution\\n\\nThe PLKG records growth over time.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nInitial:\\n\\n```\\nCalculus\\n\\nUnknown\\n```\\n\\nAfter learning:\\n\\n```\\nCalculus\\n\\nUnderstanding: 70%\\n```\\n\\nAfter revision:\\n\\n```\\nCalculus\\n\\nUnderstanding: 90%\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Data Flow\\n\\nThe overall flow:\\n\\n```\\nStudent Input\\n\\n↓\\n\\nApplication Database\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAI Processing\\n\\n↓\\n\\nKnowledge Extraction\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPLKG Update\\n\\n↓\\n\\nBLIE Reasoning\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPersonalized Learning\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Multi-Student Scalability\\n\\nThe system separates:\\n\\n## Shared Knowledge\\n\\nCommon curriculum concepts.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nCalculus Fundamentals\\n```\\n\\nUsed by many students.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Personal Knowledge\\n\\nIndividual learning state.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nStudent A struggles with Integration\\n\\nStudent B masters Integration\\n```\\n\\nThis prevents unnecessary duplication.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 13. Database Security Principles\\n\\nThe system must enforce:\\n\\n- Student data ownership\\n- Private learning history\\n- Secure document storage\\n- Controlled AI access\\n- Subscription-based feature access\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe database architecture of AI Study Buddy consists of:\\n\\n1. Relational Application Database\\n2. Curriculum Knowledge Layer\\n3. Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG)\\n\\nThe PLKG is the central knowledge structure that allows BLIE to understand, guide, and personalize each student's learning journey.\\n\\nAll future database, AI, and synchronization designs must conform to this model.\\n:::\\n\\n---\\n\\nThis completes the **conceptual database model**.\\n\\nThe next logical document is:\\n\\n**Volume F2 – BLIE AI Pipeline Specification**\\n\\nwhere we define how uploaded PDFs/images become knowledge, how AI extracts concepts, how embeddings work, how retrieval happens, and how BLIE reasons over the student's Scalability Design\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Volume F – Technical Architecture (Overview)\\n\\n## 1. System Architecture Vision\\n\\nAI Study Buddy consists of five major layers:\\n\\n```\\n                 AI Study Buddy Apps\\n        (Mobile / Web / Tablet)\\n\\n                      │\\n\\n              Application Layer\\n\\n                      │\\n\\n          Buddy Learning Intelligent Engine\\n                    (BLIE)\\n\\n                      │\\n\\n        Personal Learning Knowledge Graph\\n                    (PLKG)\\n\\n                      │\\n\\n          Knowledge \u0026 Data Infrastructure\\n\\n                      │\\n\\n              Cloud Services\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Application Layer\\n\\n## Student Applications\\n\\nPlatforms:\\n\\n- Android\\n- iOS\\n- Web\\n\\nResponsibilities:\\n\\n- User interaction\\n- Upload learning materials\\n- AI conversations\\n- Knowledge graph visualization\\n- Study planning\\n- Revision activities\\n\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Core Backend Services\\n\\nThe backend manages:\\n\\n## Identity Service\\n\\nHandles:\\n\\n- Account\\n- Authentication\\n- Subscription\\n- Student profile\\n\\n\\n## Academic Profile Service\\n\\nStores:\\n\\n- Programme\\n- Semester\\n- Subjects\\n- Curriculum structure\\n\\n\\n## Learning Content Service\\n\\nManages:\\n\\n- PDFs\\n- Images\\n- Notes\\n- Flashcards\\n- Quizzes\\n\\n\\n## PLKG Service\\n\\nThe heart of the system.\\n\\nResponsible for:\\n\\n- Knowledge nodes\\n- Relationships\\n- Concept mapping\\n- Knowledge evolution\\n\\n\\n## BLIE Orchestration Service\\n\\nCoordinates AI tasks:\\n\\n- Question answering\\n- Learning preparation\\n- Revision planning\\n- Knowledge analysis\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Data Architecture\\n\\nThe system has two types of data.\\n\\n## Structured Data\\n\\nTraditional database:\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nStudent\\n\\nSubject\\n\\nSemester\\n\\nCourse\\n\\nSubscription\\n\\nProgress\\n\\nQuiz Result\\n```\\n\\nStored in relational database.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Knowledge Data\\n\\nGraph-based data:\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nCalculus\\n\\n   |\\n   |\\nDifferentiation\\n\\n   |\\n   |\\nChain Rule\\n\\n   |\\n   |\\nAssignment Question\\n\\n   |\\n   |\\nStudent Mistake\\n```\\n\\nStored in graph database / graph layer.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. PLKG Data Model\\n\\nThe graph consists of:\\n\\n## Student Node\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nStudent\\n{\\n id,\\n learning_level,\\n preferences\\n}\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Subject Node\\n\\n```\\nSubject\\n\\nCalculus 1\\n\\nProgramming 1\\n\\nPhysics\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Concept Node\\n\\nThe most important node.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nConcept\\n\\nDerivative\\n\\nbelongs_to\\n\\nCalculus\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning Material Node\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n```\\nLecture PDF\\n\\nImage Note\\n\\nAI Explanation\\n\\nFlashcard\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Learning Event Node\\n\\nRecords:\\n\\n```\\nStudent studied concept\\n\\nStudent asked question\\n\\nStudent failed quiz\\n\\nStudent mastered topic\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Relationship Model\\n\\nThe power comes from relationships.\\n\\nExamples:\\n\\n```\\nConcept A\\n\\nrequires\\n\\nConcept B\\n```\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nIntegration\\n\\nrequires\\n\\nDifferentiation\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n```\\nStudent\\n\\nstruggled_with\\n\\nConcept\\n```\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n```\\nStudent\\n\\nstruggled_with\\n\\nMatrix Multiplication\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n```\\nLecture\\n\\nexplains\\n\\nConcept\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n```\\nAssignment\\n\\ntests\\n\\nConcept\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. AI Pipeline Architecture\\n\\nThe BLIE pipeline:\\n\\n```\\nStudent Input\\n\\n      ↓\\n\\nIntent Understanding\\n\\n      ↓\\n\\nKnowledge Graph Search\\n\\n      ↓\\n\\nContext Retrieval\\n\\n      ↓\\n\\nReasoning Engine\\n\\n      ↓\\n\\nPersonalized Response\\n\\n      ↓\\n\\nKnowledge Graph Update\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Document Intelligence Pipeline\\n\\nWhen student uploads PDF:\\n\\n```\\nPDF/Image\\n\\n↓\\n\\nOCR\\n\\n↓\\n\\nText Extraction\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSemantic Analysis\\n\\n↓\\n\\nConcept Identification\\n\\n↓\\n\\nRelationship Mapping\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPLKG Update\\n\\n↓\\n\\nAI Ready Knowledge\\n```\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nA lecture PDF about \\\"Newton's Law\\\".\\n\\nBLIE extracts:\\n\\n```\\nNewton Law\\n\\nbelongs_to\\n\\nPhysics\\n\\nrelated_to\\n\\nForce\\n\\nrelated_to\\n\\nAcceleration\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Study Preparation Pipeline\\n\\nBefore a topic starts:\\n\\n```\\nUpcoming Topic\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCurriculum Graph\\n\\n↓\\n\\nPrerequisite Analysis\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCompare Student PLKG\\n\\n↓\\n\\nIdentify Knowledge Gap\\n\\n↓\\n\\nGenerate Preparation Plan\\n```\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nBefore \\\"Machine Learning\\\":\\n\\nBLIE checks:\\n\\n```\\nMachine Learning\\n\\nrequires:\\n\\nLinear Algebra\\n\\nStatistics\\n\\nPython\\n```\\n\\nThen:\\n\\n```\\nStudent Knowledge\\n\\nLinear Algebra ⭐⭐⭐\\n\\nStatistics ⭐⭐\\n\\nPython ⭐⭐⭐⭐\\n```\\n\\nRecommendation:\\n\\n\\\"Review probability concepts before starting.\\\"\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Synchronization Architecture\\n\\nBecause students use multiple devices:\\n\\n```\\nMobile App\\n\\n      ↕\\n\\nSync Engine\\n\\n      ↕\\n\\nCloud Backend\\n\\n      ↕\\n\\nPLKG Database\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Offline Capability\\n\\nFuture architecture should support:\\n\\nLocal cache:\\n\\n- Recent notes\\n- Study plans\\n- Flashcards\\n- Knowledge graph subset\\n\\nWhen online:\\n\\n```\\nLocal Changes\\n\\n↓\\n\\nSync Queue\\n\\n↓\\n\\nConflict Resolution\\n\\n↓\\n\\nCloud Update\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 11. Scalability Vision\\n\\nDesigned for millions of students.\\n\\nEach student has:\\n\\n```\\n1 Personal PLKG\\n```\\n\\nbut infrastructure is shared.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\n10 million students:\\n\\n```\\n10M Student Graphs\\n\\n+\\n\\nShared Curriculum Templates\\n\\n+\\n\\nAI Processing Infrastructure\\n```\\n\\nImportant:\\n\\nStudents do NOT duplicate everything.\\n\\nCommon knowledge structures can be reused.\\n\\nExample:\\n\\nCalculus concept graph:\\n\\n```\\nShared Curriculum Knowledge\\n\\n        +\\n\\nPersonal Understanding Layer\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 12. Key Architectural Principle\\n\\nThe platform has two knowledge layers:\\n\\n## Global Learning Knowledge\\n\\nCommon academic knowledge:\\n\\n- Mathematics concepts\\n- Programming concepts\\n- Science concepts\\n\\n## Personal Learning Knowledge\\n\\nIndividual understanding:\\n\\n- Notes\\n- Mistakes\\n- Progress\\n- Confidence\\n- Learning history\\n\\nBLIE combines both.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Architecture Direction\\n\\nThe next detailed documents should be:\\n\\n**Volume F1 – Database \u0026 Data Model Specification**\\n\\n(to define tables, graph entities, relationships)\\n\\nthen:\\n\\n**Volume F2 – BLIE AI Pipeline Specification**\\n\\n(to define OCR, embeddings, retrieval, reasoning, memory)\\n\\nthen:\\n\\n**Volume F3 – Synchronization \u0026 Offline Architecture**\\n\\n(to define mobile-first operation)\\n\\n---\\n\\nThis architecture is now aligned with the frozen vision:\\n\\n**AI Study Buddy = BLIE + PLKG + Personal Learning Journey**\\n\\nNo university platform, no LMS, no institutional expansion. The **Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG)** is the core asset that differentiates AI Study Buddy from conventional AI assistants. This document should focus on the concept and purpose of the PLKG, leaving implementation details for the technical architecture later.\\n\\n:::writing{variant=\\\"document\\\" id=\\\"45873\\\"}\\n# AI Study Buddy\\n\\n# Volume E – Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG)\\n\\n**Version:** 1.0 (Architecture Freeze)\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 1. Introduction\\n\\nThe **Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG)** is the digital representation of a student's academic knowledge.\\n\\nRather than storing learning materials as isolated files, the PLKG organizes knowledge into connected concepts, allowing AI Study Buddy to understand not only what a student has learned, but also how different ideas relate to one another.\\n\\nEvery student owns a private PLKG that grows continuously from the first semester until graduation.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 2. Vision\\n\\nTo create a living academic memory that reflects each student's unique learning journey and becomes increasingly valuable throughout their university life.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 3. Purpose\\n\\nThe PLKG exists to:\\n\\n- Organize knowledge instead of files.\\n- Connect related concepts across subjects.\\n- Preserve long-term academic memory.\\n- Help students understand relationships between topics.\\n- Enable BLIE to provide personalized learning guidance.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 4. Knowledge Foundation\\n\\nThe PLKG begins as soon as the student completes onboarding.\\n\\nUsing the student's:\\n\\n- Degree programme\\n- Current semester\\n- Enrolled subjects\\n\\nBLIE creates an initial knowledge structure based on the curriculum and expected learning outcomes.\\n\\nThis provides the foundation upon which all future learning is built.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 5. Knowledge Growth\\n\\nAs the student learns, the PLKG continuously expands through:\\n\\n- Lecture notes\\n- PDFs\\n- Images\\n- Personal notes\\n- AI conversations\\n- Assignments\\n- Practice quizzes\\n- Flashcards\\n- Revision activities\\n\\nEach new learning experience strengthens and enriches the student's knowledge graph.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 6. Connected Learning\\n\\nKnowledge within the PLKG is interconnected.\\n\\nConcepts are linked to:\\n\\n- Related concepts\\n- Subjects\\n- Topics\\n- Learning materials\\n- Student notes\\n- AI explanations\\n- Practice activities\\n\\nThese connections help students understand how knowledge builds across different subjects and semesters.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 7. Knowledge Evolution\\n\\nThe PLKG evolves alongside the student.\\n\\nAs understanding improves, the graph becomes richer, more detailed, and more interconnected.\\n\\nThe graph is never static.\\n\\nIt reflects the student's ongoing academic development throughout university.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 8. Learning Support\\n\\nBLIE uses the PLKG to:\\n\\n- Recommend prerequisite concepts.\\n- Explain difficult topics.\\n- Identify knowledge gaps.\\n- Personalize revision.\\n- Generate relevant practice questions.\\n- Guide future learning.\\n\\nEvery recommendation is informed by the student's own learning history.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 9. Student Ownership\\n\\nThe Personal Learning Knowledge Graph belongs to the student.\\n\\nIt represents their individual learning journey, academic progress, and accumulated understanding.\\n\\nThe graph is private and exists to support the student's personal growth.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# 10. Product Value\\n\\nBy graduation, the student possesses more than lecture notes and completed assignments.\\n\\nThey own a structured academic knowledge graph that captures years of learning, connections between concepts, and intellectual growth.\\n\\nThis becomes a lasting educational asset that reflects their unique university experience.\\n\\n---\\n\\n# Architecture Freeze\\n\\nThe Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG) is the central knowledge model of AI Study Buddy.\\n\\nBLIE continuously builds, maintains, and reasons over the PLKG to deliver personalized learning support before, during, and after every stage of the student's academic journey.\\n\\nEvery feature within AI Study Buddy shall strengthen, enrich, or utilize the student's Personal Learning Knowledge Graph.\\n:::\\n\\nAt this point, the platform's conceptual foundation is complete:\\n\\n- **Volume A** — Vision \u0026 Strategy\\n- **Volume B** — Product Requirements\\n- **Volume C** — User Experience\\n- **Volume D** — Buddy Learning Intelligent Engine (BLIE)\\n- **Volume E** — Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG)\\n\\nThese five volumes define the product's identity and philosophy. The next phase can shift into implementation-oriented documents—such as technical architecture, data models, AI pipelines, and synchronization—while remaining faithful to the architecture you've frozen. memcite\",{},{\"_305\":3339,\"_312\":3360,\"_35\":3361,\"_316\":3362,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":436,\"_323\":3363,\"_325\":326},\"40f729bd-5a9f-4c57-8056-3aa4febfa90e\",[3323],{\"_370\":444,\"_323\":3365},1783583248.5111964,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":3364},{\"_343\":3351,\"_345\":346,\"_347\":3352,\"_349\":3352,\"_350\":1134,\"_52\":494,\"_354\":3358,\"_360\":497,\"_442\":26,\"_353\":14},[428],{},{\"_305\":3358,\"_312\":3369,\"_35\":3370,\"_37\":3371,\"_316\":3372,\"_318\":319,\"_321\":322,\"_323\":3373,\"_325\":326},\"c1a1ae6d-f7cb-403c-b0d7-156ef9a8bfb8\",[3339],{\"_370\":474,\"_323\":3381},1783583248.235126,1783583259.656845,{\"_365\":366,\"_367\":3379},{\"_350\":494,\"_52\":494,\"_442\":14,\"_334\":3374,\"_339\":3375,\"_519\":3376,\"_521\":3377,\"_523\":14,\"_524\":14,\"_525\":14,\"_526\":14,\"_527\":14,\"_528\":3378,\"_343\":3351,\"_469\":-5,\"_347\":3352,\"_349\":3352,\"_338\":1134,\"_360\":497,\"_353\":14},[],[],[],[],{},[3380],\"Lets continue with a short Volume E – Personal Learning Knowledge Graph (PLKG).
